Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Rulings on Leaving the City and Praying Zuhr Before Jumu'ah
Explains the ruling of leaving the city after adhan and the effect of praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaving the city after the adhan on Friday and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when a prior Zuhr prayer becomes void when one goes to Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Leaving after adhan is makruh; praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah voids it upon going according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah clarifies two interrelated rulings: the disliked nature of departing from the city after the Friday adhan before performing Jumu'ah, and the severe prohibition of praying Zuhr beforehand without excuse. It then delves into the precise moment when that Zuhr is invalidated if one subsequently proceeds to the mosque, a point of disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
First, note the two distinct acts: (1) leaving the city after adhan before praying Jumu'ah, and (2) praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse. Determine the ruling for each as stated in the text.
Leaving is makruh tahrimi; praying Zuhr is haram.
2
Locate the dalil for the voiding of Zuhr
The text cites the hadith mentioned by 'Abd al-Haqq and then gives the rational arguments (qiyas) for the voiding. Identify the basis: the exclusivity (ikhtisas) of going to Jumu'ah makes it like a pillar.
The hadith is considered weak, so the proof is primarily qiyas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the exclusivity argument leads to voiding: since going (sa'y) is unique to Jumu'ah, engaging in it is treated like engaging in a rukn of Jumu'ah, which invalidates the earlier Zuhr as a precaution.
This is a precautionary (ihtiyati) reasoning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that the Zuhr becomes void upon beginning the journey (sa'y), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require actual joining of the congregation or completion.
The practical difference: what if one starts going but does not catch Jumu'ah?
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text declares Abu Hanifa's view as 'al-asahh' (most sound) based on the Balkhi scholars. Note that this is the mufta bihi position.
Relying on the stronger act to override the weaker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكرة الخروج منَ المِصْرِ، بعدَ النَّداءِ مَا لَمْ يُصَلِّ وَمَنْ لَا جُمُعَةَ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ أَدَّاهَا جَازَ عَنْ فَرْضِ الوَقْتِ، وَمَنْ لَا عُدْرَ لَهُ لَوْ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ قَبْلَهَا حَرُمَ، فَإِنْ سَعَى إِلَيْهَا، والإمَامُ فِيهَا بَطَلَ ظُهْرُهُ، وإنْ لَمْ يُدْرِكْهَا.
قال عبد الحق في الأحكام الكبرى هو مرسل، وليس بحجة عنده، وإن أسنده أحمد من حديث عبـد بن لهيعة، وهو معروف في الضعفاء، فلا يحتج به انتهى وكره لمن تجب عليه الجمعة ( الخروج منَ المِصْرِ ) يوم الجمعة ( بعد النّداءِ ) أي: الأذان الأول، وقيل: المعتـبر الثـانـي (مـا لـم يُصَلِّ) الجمعة، لأنه شمله الأمر بالسعي إلى الجمعة، ولم يصر مسافراً قبل الخروج، ولا منفصلاً عن المصر، وإذا خرج قبل الزوال فلا بأس به بلا خلاف كما في ( التاتارخانية»، وكذا بعد فراغ الجمعة وإن لم يدركها (وَمَنْ لا جُمُعَةَ عَلَيْهِ) كمريض ومسافر ورقيق وامرأة وأعمى ومقعد ( إن أَدَّاهَا جَازَ عَنْ فَرْض الوَقْتِ)؛ لأن السقوط تخفيفاً للعذر ، فإذا تحمل ما لم يكلف بـه وهـو الجمعة، جاز عن فرض الوقت وهو الظهر، كالمسافر إذا صام، وكلام الشراح يدل على أن الأفضل لهم الجمعة لقولهم: إن الظهر لهم يوم الجمعة رخصة فدل على أن العزيمة صلاة الجمعة، ويستثنى منهم المرأة لأنها ممنوعة عن حضور الجماعات. (وَمَنْ لا عُدْرَ لَهُ) يمنعه عن حضور الجمعة (لَوْ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ قَبْلَهَا ) أي : قبل صلاة الجمعة انعقد ظهره لوجود وقت أصل الفرض، وهـو الـظـهـر فـي حـق الكافة، إلا أنه لما كان مأموراً بإسقاطه بالجمعة (حَرُمَ) عليه فعل الأصل، وكان انعقاده موقوفاً ( فَإِنْ سَعَى) أي: مشى لا مسرعاً ( إلَيْهَا ) أي : إلى الجمعة، (وَ) كان الإمَامُ فِيهَا) أي: صلاة الجمعة لم يتمها إذ ذاك أو أقيمت بعدما سعى إليها ( بَطَلَ ظُهْرُهُ) أي: بطل وصفه وصـار نـفـلاً، وكذا حكـم المعذور لو صلى الظهر، ثم سعى إلى الجمعة بطل ظهره، وإنْ لَمْ يُدْرِكْهَا)، وهذا عند «أبـي حنيفة» على تخريج البلخيين، وهو الأصح، والمعتبر في السعي الانفصال عن داره، فلا يبطل ظهره قبله على المختار. وقيل: إذا خطا خطوتين في البيت الواسع يبطل، ولا يبطل إذا كان السعي مقارناً للفراغ منها أو بعدها، أو لم تقم الجمعة ؟ قالا : لا يبطل ظهره حتى يدخل مع القوم، وفي رواية حتى يتمها، حتى لو أفسدها بعدما شرع فيها لا يبطل ظهره على هذه الرواية، لهما أن السعي إلى الجمعة دون الظهر فلا يبطل به الظهر، والجمعة فوقه فيبطل بها، ولأبي حنيفة رحمه الله : أن السعي إلى الجمعة من خصائصها، فصار الاشتغال به کالاشتغال بركن من أركانها بجامع الاختصاص، فيؤثر في ارتفاض الظهر احتياطاً، إذ الأقوى يحتاط لإثباتـه مـا لا يحتاط لإثبات الأضعف، ولو صلى مسافر الظهر إماماً، ثم حضر الجمعة فصلاها فهي فرضه، وجازت صلاة أولئك، ولو قدمه الإمام لسبق حدث جازت صلاة القوم؛ لأنَّ ظهره ارتفض في حقه دون أولئك الذين صلى بهم قبل دخوله المصر، فصارت في حق الفريق الثاني كأنه لم يصل الظهر من « التبيين»، و « العناية»، و«فتح القدير»، و « التاتارخانية»، عن «جامع الجوامع » و « التجنيس».
It is disliked to leave the city, after the call to prayer, as long as he has not prayed. And whoever is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah, if he performs it (Jumu'ah), it suffices for the obligatory prayer of the time. And whoever has no excuse, if he prays Zuhr before it, it is unlawful. Then if he goes (sa'ā) to it (Jumu'ah) while the imam is in it, his Zuhr becomes void, even if he does not catch it. 'Abd al-Haqq said in al-Ahkam al-Kubra: It is mursal and not a proof according to him, though Ahmad narrated it from Ibn Lahi'ah, who is known among the weak, so it is not used as proof. End of quote. It is disliked for the one upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory to leave the city on Friday after the call, i.e., the first adhan; some say the second is considered, as long as he has not prayed Jumu'ah, because the command to go to Jumu'ah applies to him, and he does not become a traveler before leaving nor separated from the city. If he leaves before zawal, it is fine without dispute, as in al-Tatarakhaniyya, likewise after completing Jumu'ah even if he did not catch it. (And whoever is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah) like the sick, traveler, slave, woman, blind, and crippled. (If he performs it) it suffices for the obligatory prayer of the time because the exemption is a lightening due to the excuse; so if he takes on that which he was not obligated for, i.e., Jumu'ah, it suffices for the obligatory prayer of the time, which is Zuhr, like the traveler who fasts. The words of the commentators indicate that Jumu'ah is superior for them, because they say that Zuhr for them on Friday is a concession, so that shows that the resolved matter (azima) is Jumu'ah prayer. Women are excepted because they are prohibited from attending congregations. (And whoever has no excuse) preventing him from attending Jumu'ah, (if he prays Zuhr before it) i.e., before the Jumu'ah prayer, his Zuhr contracts because the time for the original obligation is present, which is Zuhr for all. However, since he is commanded to drop it by Jumu'ah, (it is unlawful) for him to perform the original act, and its contraction is suspended. (Then if he goes) i.e., walks, not hurrying, (to it) i.e., to Jumu'ah, (and) the imam is in it (i.e., the Jumu'ah prayer has not yet finished or has been established after he goes), (his Zuhr becomes void) i.e., its quality is void and it becomes supererogatory. The same rule applies to the excused person if he prays Zuhr then goes to Jumu'ah: his Zuhr becomes void, even if he does not catch it. This is according to Abu Hanifa based on the elaboration of the Balkhi scholars, and it is the most correct. The considered point in going (sa'y) is his departure from his house, so his Zuhr does not become void before that according to the chosen view. It is said: if he takes two steps within a spacious house, it becomes void. It does not become void if the going coincides with his finishing it or after it, or if Jumu'ah has not been established. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: his Zuhr does not become void until he enters with the people; in one narration, until he completes it, so even if he invalidates it after starting, his Zuhr does not become void according to this narration. Their proof: that going to Jumu'ah is separate from Zuhr, so the Zuhr is not invalidated by it, and Jumu'ah is above it, so it invalidates it. Abu Hanifa's proof: that going to Jumu'ah is one of its characteristics, so occupying oneself with it is like occupying oneself with one of its pillars due to the common factor of exclusivity, thus it affects the annulment of Zuhr as a precaution, because the stronger is more cautious to establish itself than the weaker. If a traveler prays Zuhr as an imam, then attends Jumu'ah and prays it, then Jumu'ah is his obligation, and the prayer of those (whom he led) is valid. And if the imam is preceded by [an event that invalidates wudu?], the prayer of the people is valid because his Zuhr is annulled in his regard but not in the regard of those whom he led before entering the city, so regarding the second group it is as if he did not pray Zuhr. From al-Tabyin, al-Inaya, Fath al-Qadir, al-Tatarakhaniyya, from Jami' al-Jawami' and al-Tajnis.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings concerning the obligation and desirability of attending Friday prayer (Jumu'ah). The author explains the disliked nature of leaving the city after the adhan before praying Jumu'ah, the permissibility for those not obligated (like travelers, slaves, women) to perform Jumu'ah and have it count for Zuhr, and the severe ruling for one who has no excuse but prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah: it is unlawful and his Zuhr becomes invalid if he later goes to Jumu'ah while the imam is still engaged. The commentary details the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding when exactly the Zuhr becomes void. Abu Hanifa holds that merely starting to go (sa'y) in the direction of the mosque invalidates the Zuhr, while the Sahibayn require actual joining of the congregation. The text cites hadith and rational arguments, emphasizing that the stronger act (Jumu'ah) should override the weaker (Zuhr) as a precaution. It also notes that the excused person who prays Zuhr then goes to Jumu'ah likewise has his Zuhr voided.

Key Terms
السعي (as-sa'y): In this context, walking or going (not hastening) to the Jumu'ah prayer.
النداء (an-nidā'): The call to prayer (adhan) on Friday; here it refers to the first adhan, though some consider the second.
المصر (al-miṣr): A city or large town where Jumu'ah is obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the passage, at what point does the Zuhr prayer become void for a person who has no excuse but prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah and then goes to the mosque?
A) When he joins the congregation
B) When he begins walking (sa'y) from his house
C) When the imam says the takbir
D) When the Friday sermon ends

Key Takeaway
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is haram, and it becomes void (nafl) once one begins walking to the mosque while the imam is engaged, even if Jumu'ah is not caught.

Dislike of Congregational Zuhr for the Excused and Prisoner on Friday
States that it is disliked for those excused from Jumu'ah to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the excused and prisoner regarding congregational Zuhr on Friday, explain the reasoning, and apply it to different scenarios.

Core Idea
Praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked for the excused to avoid reducing Jumu'ah attendance.

This lesson addresses a subtle but important ruling: even though those excused from Jumu'ah are not obliged to attend, they should still avoid praying Zuhr in congregation within the city on Friday. The reason is to protect the congregation of the Jumu'ah prayer. We will unpack who is included, why the ruling exists, and an important exception for villagers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals covered
List the categories: the excused (sick, slave, traveler, blind, cripple) and the prisoner. Understand what qualifies as an excuse for missing Jumu'ah.
The text explicitly mentions the excused and prisoner; the prisoner is separately highlighted because his situation may be misunderstood.
2
State the disliked action and its scope
The action is performing Zuhr prayer in congregation on Friday. The scope is limited to the city (misr) where Jumu'ah is held. Note that this includes both before and after Jumu'ah time.
The dislike applies even if the group is small; the key is that it could potentially reduce the main congregation.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason given is that congregational Zuhr may cause others to follow suit, thus decreasing attendance at the Jumu'ah mosque. This is seen as a form of turning away from sa'y (going to Jumu'ah) and an opposition to the communal obligation.
This reasoning explains why the rule exists even though the individual is not obligated.
4
Distinguish the exception for villagers
Villagers (ahl al-sawad) are not included because there is no Jumu'ah in their area, so their congregational Zuhr does not affect Jumu'ah attendance.
This exception confirms the rationale: if no Jumu'ah exists, the reason vanishes.
5
Analyze the separate mention of the prisoner
The prisoner is mentioned separately because one might think that if he is unjustly imprisoned, the dislike is lifted. However, the text maintains the dislike; if he is a wrongdoer, he must instead attend Jumu'ah by satisfying his opponents.
This nuance shows that the ruling is based on the act itself, not on the justice of the imprisonment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَكُرِهَ لِلْمَعْدُورِ) كمريض ورقيق ومسافر (وَالمَسْجُونِ أَدَاءُ الظُّهْرِ بِجَمَاعَةٍ، في المِصْرِ يَوْمَهَا) أي: الجمعة، يـروى ذلـك عـن عليه، ولأن في أداء الظهر بجماعة قبل الجمعة وبعدها تقليلاً للجماعة في الجامع؛ لأنه قد يقتدي به غيره، وفيه معارضة على وجه المخالفة، وفيه صورة إعراض عن السعي إلى الجمعة، وإن لم يكن مكلفاً بها، بخلاف أهل السواد لأنه لا جمعة هناك، فلا يفضي إلى التقليل ولا إلى المعارضة، وإنما أفرد المسجون بالذكر وإن شمله المعذور؛ لأنه ربما لا يتوهم الكراهة بمنعه من الخروج للجمعة إذا كان مظلوماً، لأنه يمكنه الاستعانة والخروج. وإن كان ظالماً فعليه إرضاء الخصوم وحضور الجمعة كذا قالوه، ولا يخفى ما فيه، ويكره للمعذور صلاة الظهر منفرداً قبل صلاة الجمعة في الصحيح، له تأخيره عنها.
(And it is disliked for the excused) like the sick, slave, and traveler, (and the prisoner) to perform Zuhr in congregation, in the city on Friday. This is narrated from him, and because performing Zuhr in congregation before or after Friday reduces the congregation in the central mosque, as others may follow him. In that is opposition in the manner of contravention, and it is a form of turning away from going (sa'y) to Jumu'ah, even if he is not obligated for it. This differs from the villagers (ahl al-sawad), because there is no Jumu'ah there, so it does not lead to reduction or opposition. The prisoner is mentioned separately, although included in the excused, because one might not suspect dislike if he is prevented from going out for Jumu'ah if he is oppressed, as he can seek assistance and go out. But if he is a wrongdoer, then he must satisfy the opponents and attend Jumu'ah; this is what they said, and it is not hidden. And it is disliked for the excused person to pray Zuhr individually before the Jumu'ah prayer, according to the correct view, because of delaying it.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
The passage explains that it is disliked (makruh) for those who are excused from attending Jumu'ah—such as the sick, a slave, a traveler—and also for a prisoner to pray Zuhr in congregation within the city on Friday. The reason is that their doing so may reduce the number of attendees at the Jumu'ah mosque because others might follow them, thereby showing disregard for the gathering. This ruling does not apply to villagers (ahl al-sawad) because there is no Jumu'ah in their area. The prisoner is mentioned separately because one might think the dislike does not apply if he is unjustly imprisoned, but even then it is disliked; if he is a wrongdoer, he must instead attend Jumu'ah. The text also notes that it is disliked for the excused to pray Zuhr alone before Jumu'ah; the better view is that they should delay it until after Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
المعدور (al-ma'dhūr): A person who has a legitimate excuse from attending Jumu'ah, such as illness, slavery, or travel.
المسجون (al-masjūn): A prisoner; one who is confined and cannot attend Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked for a traveler to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city where Jumu'ah is held?
A) Because travelers are not allowed to pray in congregation
B) Because it may reduce the Jumu'ah congregation at the main mosque
C) Because it is haram to pray Zuhr on Friday
D) Because the traveler must leave the city early

Key Takeaway
Even those excused from Jumu'ah should avoid praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city, to preserve the main Jumu'ah gathering.

Catching Jumu'ah in Tashahhud or Sajdah al-Sahw: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum catch for Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on catching Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajdah al-sahw, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Catching tashahhud makes Jumu'ah valid per the two; Muhammad requires a rak'ah.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the minimum portion of Jumu'ah a latecomer must catch. While Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that any part, even the final tashahhud or prostration of forgetfulness, suffices, Imam Muhammad requires at least one complete rak'ah. We will explore the evidence and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize the act: a latecomer joins the imam during Jumu'ah. Note the ruling according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: catching any part (tashahhud or sajdah al-sahw) makes the prayer valid as Jumu'ah.
The passage uses 'عندهما' to indicate the view of the two.
2
Locate the evidence
The hadith 'ما أدركتم فصلوا وما فاتكم فاقضوا' (pray what you catch, complete what you miss) is cited. Understand that this general command is taken as proof that catching any part suffices.
Hanafi usul: 'amm is qat'i until takhsis.
3
Analyze the dissent
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees: only catching a rak'ah (the second rak'ah) counts for Jumu'ah; otherwise, the latecomer prays Zuhr. Understand his reasoning: Jumu'ah is a two-rak'ah prayer, so catching at least one rak'ah is necessary.
The text says 'وقال محمد: إن أدركه في الركعة الثانية...'
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: According to the two, one who catches tashahhud prays two rak'ahs as Jumu'ah; according to Muhammad, he prays four rak'ahs of Zuhr.
This directly affects the latecomer's prayer.
5
Note the consensus on Eid
The passage mentions that for Eid prayer, there is agreement (except Muhammad's view is noted). Recognize that the ruling for Eid is similar: catching any part suffices by consensus of the two, but Muhammad still requires a rak'ah.
In Al-Siraj: 'لم يصر مدركاً للعيد عند محمد'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَنْ أدْرَكَها :أي: الجمعة ( في التَّشَهُدِ أوْ ) في (سُجُودِ السَّهْوِ) أو تشهده أتم جُمُعَةً) لما روينا من قوله : ( إذا أُقِيمَتِ الصَّلاةَ فَلا تَأْتُوهَا وَأَنْتُمْ تَسْعَوْنَ، فَمَا أَدْرَكْتُمْ فَصَلُّوا وَمَا فَاتَكُمْ فَاقْضُوا ) ، فأمره الله بقضاء ما فاته، وهو الذي صلاه الإمام قبل الاقتداء بـه لا صلاة أخــرى وهذا عندهما، وقال ( محمد ) : إن أدركه في الركعة الثانية ولو قبل الرفع من الركوع أتم جمعة، وإلا أتم ظهراً، وفي العيد يتمه اتفاقاً، كما في «الفتح»، وفي «السراج»: لم يُصر مدركاً للعيـد عنـــد «محمد»، ثم إنه يتخير في قضاء ما فاته إن شاء جهر، وإن شاء أسر.
And whoever catches it (i.e., Jumu'ah) in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) or its tashahhud, he completes it as Jumu'ah, due to what we narrated from his (the Prophet's) saying: "When the prayer is established, do not come to it running; what you catch, pray, and what you miss, complete." So he is commanded to complete what he missed, which is what the imam prayed before he followed him, not another prayer. This is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). But Muhammad said: If he catches him in the second rak'ah, even before rising from bowing, he completes it as Jumu'ah; otherwise he completes it as Zuhr. And for the Eid prayer, it is completed by agreement, as in al-Fath. In al-Siraj: According to Muhammad, one does not become a catcher of the Eid prayer. Then he has the choice in completing what he missed: aloud or silently.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
The passage discusses the ruling for a person who joins the Jumu'ah prayer late. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), if one catches the imam in the final tashahhud or even in the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) and its tashahhud, he completes the prayer as Jumu'ah. This is based on the hadith: "What you catch, pray; what you miss, complete." However, Imam Muhammad has a different opinion: if the latecomer catches the imam in the second rak'ah, even before rising from bowing, he prays it as Jumu'ah; otherwise, he must complete it as Zuhr. The text also notes that for Eid prayer, there is agreement that catching any part counts, but Muhammad still differs regarding Eid. The latecomer then has the choice of reciting aloud or silently for the missed portion.

Key Terms
التشهد (at-tashahhud): The sitting recitation (at-tahiyyat) at the end of the prayer.
سجود السهو (sujūd as-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed after the final tashahhud to compensate for omissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a person catches the imam in the final tashahhud of Jumu'ah, how should he pray?
A) He completes it as Jumu'ah with two rak'ahs
B) He prays four rak'ahs of Zuhr
C) He must repeat the prayer
D) He joins and does not need to complete

Key Takeaway
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, a latecomer who catches any part of the Jumu'ah prayer, even the tashahhud, completes it as Jumu'ah.

Recommended Acts Before Jumu'ah: Ghusl, Perfume, and Best Attire
Summarizes sunnah acts for Jumu'ah with a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts for Jumu'ah and explain why the Hanafi school classifies ghusl as sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.

Core Idea
Ghusl for Jumu'ah is emphasized sunnah, not obligation; its reward depends on actually attending prayer.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah reinforces the highly recommended etiquettes for Friday prayer. While some may assume ghusl is obligatory, the Hanafi school clarifies it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The hadith lists multiple acts and promises forgiveness, highlighting their importance without raising them to wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate where the text states the ruling of ghusl for Jumu'ah. It says 'يسن الغسل' meaning it is sunnah.
In Hanafi fiqh, 'yusannu' indicates sunnah mu'akkadah unless specified otherwise.
2
Examine the nuance about reward
The citation from al-Tatarakhaniyya states that if a person not obligated for Jumu'ah performs ghusl, he does not attain the reward. Understand that the reward is conditional on actually praying Jumu'ah.
3
List the additional recommended acts
From al-Diraya: apply oil, perfume, wear best clothes. From Jami' al-Jawami': trim the mustache.
These are all sunnah acts, not pillars or conditions.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith from Bukhari lists the acts and promises forgiveness between the two Fridays. The Hanafi school uses this to show recommendation (istihbab), not obligation, because the promise of reward does not make an act compulsory.
The promise of forgiveness indicates great virtue but does not impose a legal obligation.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Ghusl for Jumu'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for men attending the prayer. It is not wajib or fard. The authority comes from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
The mufta bihi is that these acts are mustahabb (recommended).

Source Text

Supplement: We have previously stated that performing ghusl for Friday prayer is sunnah. It is said in al-Tatarakhaniyya: If one who is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah performs ghusl, he does not attain the reward. End. Meaning if he does not pray Jumu'ah with it. In al-Diraya: It is recommended (mustahabb) for the one who attends Jumu'ah to perform ghusl, apply oil (to hair), apply perfume if found, and wear his best clothes if he has them. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Any man who performs ghusl on Friday, purifies himself as much as possible, applies oil, or applies perfume from his house, then goes out and does not separate two people, then prays what is written for him, then remains silent when the khatib speaks, will have his sins between that Friday and the next forgiven." Narrated by Bukhari. In Jami' al-Jawami': And he should trim his mustache.

Commentary
This concluding section (tamima) reiterates that performing ghusl (full body wash) for Jumu'ah is a sunnah (recommended act). However, if a person not obligated for Jumu'ah (e.g., a traveler) does ghusl for Jumu'ah but does not actually pray it, they do not earn the special reward. The text recommends for the attendee to also apply oil, perfume, and wear the best clothes. The hadith from Bukhari lists these actions and promises forgiveness of sins between the two Fridays. Additionally, trimming the mustache is mentioned as a recommended act from Jami' al-Jawami'.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full body wash with intention, specifically for Friday prayer.
السنة المؤكدة (as-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and was not abandoned except rarely.

Dislike for Excused and Prisoner to Pray Zuhr in Congregation on Friday
Ruling with proof on karahah for excused and prisoner praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of karahah for the excused and prisoner to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday and explain the illah (effective cause) based on the Hanafi text.

Core Idea
Praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked because it reduces the Jumu'ah congregation.

The sacred Friday prayer is the highlight of the week. For those not obligated to attend—such as the sick, traveler, or prisoner—it might be tempting to pray Zuhr early in congregation and be done. However, the Hanafi school holds this to be disliked (makruh). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that ruling and clarifies who it applies to.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act: the excused (ma'dhur) or prisoner (masjun) performing Zuhr in congregation in a city on Friday. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked), as indicated by the word 'kurihat'.
The excused include the sick, slave, and traveler. The prisoner is singled out to remove doubt.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is not a direct textual evidence but a reasoning (talil): 'because performing Zuhr in congregation reduces attendance at Jumu'ah, constitutes opposition, and is a form of turning away from Friday.'
This is an example of istihsan or meaning-based reasoning in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Identify the illah (effective cause)
The underlying cause is the reduction of the Jumu'ah congregation. If the excused prays Zuhr in congregation, others may follow, decreasing the number for Jumu'ah.
The illah is that the act leads to diminishing the congregational aspect of Jumu'ah.
4
Apply the ruling to specific categories
The ruling applies in the city (misr) where Jumu'ah is held. It does not apply to people of the countryside (ahl al-sawad) because there is no Jumu'ah there. For the prisoner, distinguish: if oppressed (mazlum), the dislike might not arise; if an oppressor (zalim), he must attend Jumu'ah.
The text notes a difference of opinion on this distinction.
5
Note the additional ruling on individual prayer
The passage adds that it is also disliked for the excused to pray Zuhr individually before the Jumu'ah prayer in the correct view (al-sahih).
This is because he should delay until after Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَكُرِهَ لِلْمَعْدُورِ) كمريض ورقيق ومسافر (وَالمَسْجُونِ أَدَاءُ الظُّهْرِ بِجَمَاعَةٍ، في المِصْرِ يَوْمَهَا) أي: الجمعة، يروى ذلك عنه، ولأن في أداء الظهر بجماعة قبل الجمعة وبعدها تقليلاً للجماعة في الجامع؛ لأنه قد يقتدي به غيره، وفيه معارضة على وجه المخالفة، وفيه صورة إعراض عن السعي إلى الجمعة، وإن لم يكن مكلفاً بها، بخلاف أهل السواد لأنه لا جمعة هناك، فلا يفضي إلى التقليل ولا إلى المعارضة، وإنما أفرد المسجون بالذكر وإن شمله المعذور؛ لأنه ربما لا يتوهم الكراهة بمنعه من الخروج للجمعة إذا كان مظلوماً، لأنه يمكنه الاستعانة والخروج. وإن كان ظالماً فعليه إرضاء الخصوم وحضور الجمعة كذا قالوه، ولا يخفى ما فيه، ويكره للمعذور صلاة الظهر منفرداً قبل صلاة الجمعة في الصحيح، له تأخيره عنها.
And it is disliked for the excused person (like a sick person, slave, traveler) and the prisoner to perform Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday, i.e., Friday. This is narrated from him. And because performing Zuhr in congregation before and after Friday reduces the congregation in the mosque, because others might follow him, and it is an opposition in the form of contestation, and it is a form of turning away from attending Friday, even if he is not obligated to it, unlike the people of the countryside because there is no Friday there, so it does not lead to reduction nor opposition. And the prisoner is mentioned specifically although he is included in the excused, because one might not imagine dislike for him if he is prevented from going out for Friday when he is oppressed, since he can seek help and go out. But if he is an oppressor, then he must appease his opponents and attend Friday. Thus they said, and what is in it is not hidden. And it is disliked for the excused to pray Zuhr individually before Friday prayer in the correct view, because he should delay it until after Friday.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage states the ruling of karahah (dislike) for certain individuals who are not obligated to attend Jumu'ah to perform Zuhr prayer in congregation in the city on Friday. The excused persons (ma'dhur) include the sick, the slave, and the traveler. The prisoner (masjun) is mentioned separately even though he is included, because a prisoner who is oppressed might not be expected to encounter the dislike since he is prevented from leaving. However, if the prisoner is an oppressor (justly imprisoned), he must satisfy the claimants and attend Friday if possible. The reason for the dislike is that performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday reduces the congregation in the mosque for Jumu'ah, as others might follow his example. It also constitutes a form of opposition and turning away from attending Jumu'ah, even if one is not obligated. This dislike does not apply to the people of the countryside because there is no Jumu'ah in their area. Additionally, it is disliked for the excused person to pray Zuhr individually before the Jumu'ah prayer in the correct opinion, because he should delay it until after the Jumu'ah prayer.

Key Terms
المَعْدُور (al-ma'dhūr): The excused person who is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah due to illness, slavery, or travel.
المَسْجُون (al-masjūn): The prisoner, whether oppressed or oppressor, who may be unable to attend Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the excused person should not pray in a masjid at all on Friday
D) Because it makes the excused person liable for missing Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
The ruling of karahah for performing Zuhr in congregation before Jumu'ah is rooted in preserving the significance and attendance of the Friday prayer.

Recommended Acts for Jumu'ah: Ghusl, Attire, and Grooming
Lists sunnan and mustahabbat for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan and mustahabbat for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school and identify the ruling level of each act.

Core Idea
Ghusl on Friday is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib; white clothes are preferred, black is not disliked.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists several recommended acts for Friday (Jumu'ah) including ghusl, applying perfume, wearing white clothes, trimming nails, and more. These acts are sunnah muakkadah or mustahabb, enhancing the spiritual experience of the day. We will examine each act, the supporting evidence, and clarify common misconceptions about their legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of each act
As you read the source, note which acts are described as 'sunna' (يسن) vs 'mustahabb' (يستحب). In Hanafi fiqh, these terms indicate different levels of recommendation.
Ghusl is explicitly 'يسن' (sunnah); wearing white clothes is 'يستحب' (mustahabb).
2
Analyze the evidence for each act
The author cites hadith for ghusl (Bukhari hadith) and for white clothes (hadith from Ibn Abbas). Understand how these proofs establish the recommendation.
The ghusl hadith includes a promise of forgiveness.
3
Examine the discussion on black clothing
The passage includes a secondary discussion on the dislike (karahah) of black clothing. Note that some Shafi'is disliked it, but the Hanafi position (via al-Mawardi) holds it is not disliked, citing the Prophet's practice.
This shows ikhtilaf within fiqh.
4
Differentiate between ruling levels
The text distinguishes between sunnah muakkadah (like ghusl) and other recommended acts. Understand that missing a sunnah muakkadah is not sinful but is blameworthy.
Ghusl for Jumu'ah is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Consider a person who attends Jumu'ah without ghusl but prays. The prayer is valid but he misses the reward of following the sunnah.
The reward is for those who perform ghusl with the intention of sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: قدمنا أنه يسن الغسل لصلاة الجمعة ، وقال في التاتارخانية: لو اغتسل من لا جمعة عليه لا ينال الثواب انتهى، يعني: إذا لم يصل به الجمعة وفي الدراية: يستحب لمن حضر الجمعة أن يغتسل ويدهن ويمس طيباً إن وجده، ويلبس أحسن ثيابه إن كان له، قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: « لا يَغْتَسِلُ رَجُلٌ يَوْمَ الجُمُعَةِ وَيَتَطَهَّرُ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ مِنْ طُهْرٍ، وَيَدَّهَنُ مِنْ دُهْنِهِ، أَو يَمَسُّ مِنْ طيب بَيْتِهِ، ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ فَلا يُفَرِّقَ بَيْنَ اثْنَيْنِ، ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي مَا كُتَبَ لَهُ، ثُمَّ يَسْكُتُ إِذَا تَكَلَّمَ الخَطِيبُ إلا غُفِرَ لَهُ مَا بِيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الجُمُعَةِ الأخْرَى ) رواه البخاري، وفي جامع الجوامع: ويقص الشارب ويقلم الأظافير، وفي الحجة: يكره ذلك قبل الصلاة جعلها كالحج، وفي الأخبار: «مَنْ قَلْمَ أَظْفَارَهُ يَوْمَ الجُمُعَةِ أَعَاذَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنَ السُّوءِ إِلَى الجُمُعَةِ القَابِلَةِ، وثَلاثة أيامٍ»، وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِبْسُ الشَّيَابِ البِيْضِ، لما روى ابن عباس أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: « البسسُوا مِنْ ثِيَابِكُمْ البَيَاضِ فَإِنَّهَا مِنْ أَحْسَنِ ثِيَابِكُمْ وكره من الشافعية الغزالي، وأبو طالب المكي لباس السواد، وخالفهما الماوردي في الحاوي لما أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام خطب وعليه عمامة سوداء، ودخل يوم الفتح وعليه عمامة سوداء، وعلى علي وابن عمر عمامة سوداء يوم قتل عثمان، وإحداث بنو العباس لباس السواد شعاراً لهم، لأن الراية التي عقدت العباس الهلال له يوم الفتح ويوم خيبر كانت سوداء.
Continuation: We previously mentioned that ghusl is sunnah for Friday prayer. He said in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If one who is not obligated to Friday performs ghusl, he does not attain reward. Meaning: if he does not pray Friday with it. And in al-Diraya: It is recommended for one who attends Friday to perform ghusl, apply oil, apply perfume if he finds it, and wear his best clothes if he has them. The Prophet said: 'No man performs ghusl on Friday and purifies himself as much as he can, applies oil from his oil, or applies perfume from his house, then goes out and does not separate two people, then prays what is written for him, then remains silent when the khatib speaks, but his sins between that and the next Friday are forgiven.' Narrated by Bukhari. And in Jami' al-Jawami': He trims the mustache and cuts his nails. And in al-Hujja: That is disliked before the prayer, making it like Hajj. And in al-Akhbar: 'Whoever cuts his nails on Friday, Allah protects him from evil until the next Friday and three days.' And it is recommended to wear white clothes, because Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet said: 'Wear your white clothes, for they are among the best of your clothes.' And al-Ghazali from the Shafi'is and Abu Talib al-Makki disliked black clothing; al-Mawardi differed with them in al-Hawi, because the Prophet gave a sermon wearing a black turban, entered Mecca on the day of victory wearing a black turban, and Ali and Ibn Umar wore black turbans on the day Uthman was killed. And the Abbasids adopted black clothing as a symbol, because the banner that was tied for al-Abbas al-Hilali on the day of victory and the day of Khaybar was black.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This section details the recommended acts (sunan and mustahabbat) for Friday. Ghusl is sunnah for those attending Jumu'ah. If one not obligated performs ghusl, he does not receive the specific reward for Friday ghusl unless he prays Jumu'ah. It is mustahabb to apply oil and perfume, wear the best clothes (preferably white), trim the mustache, and cut nails before or on Friday. Cutting nails on Friday brings protection from evil for a period. The preference for white clothes is based on a hadith. There is a difference of opinion regarding black clothes: some Shafi'is disliked it, but al-Mawardi argued that the Prophet and sahaba wore black turbans, and the Abbasids adopted it as a symbol, so it is not disliked. This shows that in Hanafi fiqh, black clothes are not disliked for men, though white is preferable.

Key Terms
الغُسْل (al-ghusl): Washing the entire body with water, performed before Friday prayer.
المُؤَذِّن (al-mu'adhdhin): The person who calls the adhan for prayer.
السّنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-muakkadah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged; omitting it is blameworthy but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is mustahabb, and there is a hadith about protection from evil.
B) It is haram because it resembles the pre-Islamic practice.
C) It is wajib because it is part of fitrah.
D) It is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
The recommended acts for Jumu'ah enhance the spiritual experience and bring reward; ghusl is a confirmed sunnah, and white clothing is preferred over black but black is not disliked.

The Obligation of Eid Prayer and Its Conditions
Opening the chapter on Eid rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer, identify its proof from the Sunnah, and apply the conditions of Jumu'ah to determine its obligation.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib, proven by the Prophet's continuous practice, and depends on the same conditions as Jumu'ah.

The Eid prayer is a special congregational prayer whose legal status is often misunderstood. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position: that it is wajib, not merely sunnah, and that its conditions mirror those of Jumu'ah. We will also see why the khutbah is not a condition for validity, clarifying a common point of confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The author explicitly states that Eid prayer is wajib. Look for the phrase 'صلاة العيدين واجبة' and note that this is the more correct (al-ashahh) view from Abu Hanifa.
Some early texts use 'sunnah' – we will see how to reconcile this.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet replaced the two pre-Islamic festivals with Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. The hadith establishes the legitimacy, but the obligation comes from the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) of performing the Eid prayer without ever omitting it.
In Hanafi usul, continuous practice (al-muwazabah) indicates wujub, not fard.
3
Resolve the intra-madhhab wording
Al-Jami' al-Saghir calls it 'sunnah' – the author explains this is not a contradiction; it refers to the established practice, not a lower legal category. The obligation is proven by the constant practice.
The term 'sunnah' in early Hanafi texts sometimes means 'established practice' and may overlap with 'wajib'.
4
Apply the conditions of Jumu'ah
Eid prayer is wajib on the same person upon whom Jumu'ah is wajib. Recall the conditions: residence (not a traveller), health, freedom, and maleness. These are both shurut al-wujub (conditions of obligation) and shurut al-sihhah (conditions of validity) for Eid prayer.
The khutbah is excluded from the conditions; it is a sunnah, not a condition.
5
Understand the role of the khutbah
The khutbah is a sunnah that follows the prayer. The prayer is valid without it, though it is blameworthy (makruh) to omit it. Similarly, giving the khutbah before the prayer contradicts the Prophetic practice.
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from other schools that may require the khutbah for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب أحكام العيدين من الصلاة وغيرها سمي يوم العيد به لأن الله تعالى عوائد الإحسان إلى عباده دينية ودنيوية أو لأنه يعود ويكرر وحق جمعه أعواد لأن أصله الواو وجمع بالياء للزومها في الواحد أو للفرق بينه وبين عود الخشبة أن يجمع على عيدان وعود الطرب على أعواد وكانت صلاة عيد الفطر في السنة الأولى من الهجرة روى أبو داود عن أنس قال قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة ولهم يومان يلعبون فيهما فقال ما هذان اليومان قيل كنا نلعب فيهما في الجاهلية فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن الله قد أبدلكم بهما خيرا منهما يوم الأضحى ويوم الفطر صلاة العيدين واجبة نص على الوجوب لأنه ورد نصا عن أبي حنيفة في رواية وهي على الأصح رواية ودراية وبه قال الأكثرون وتسميتها في الجامع الصغير سنة لأنه ثبت الوجوب بها لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على صلاة العيدين من غير ترك كما في الفتح فتجب على من تجب عليه الجمعة بشرائطها وقد علمتها فلابد من شرائط الوجوب جميعها وشرائط الصحة سوى الخطبة لأنها لما أخرت عن الصلاة لم تكن شرطا لها فبقيت وعظا كما في سائر الأوقات وكانت الخطبة سنة فتصح صلاة العيدين بدونها أي الخطبة لكن مع الإساءة لترك السنة كما يكون مسيئا لو قدمت الخطبة على صلاة العيد لمخالفته فعل النبي
Chapter of rulings of the two Eids – from prayer and other matters. The day of Eid is so named because Allah (Most High) has regular returns of beneficence to His servants, religious and worldly, or because it returns and repeats. Its correct plural is a'wad because its root is waw, and it is pluralized with ya due to its occurrence in the singular, or to differentiate between it and 'wood stick' (which is pluralized as 'idan) and 'musical instrument' (plural a'wad). The prayer of Eid al-Fitr was in the first year of the Hijrah. Abu Dawud narrated from Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came to Medina and they had two days on which they played. He said: "What are these two days?" They said: "We used to play on them in the Jahiliyyah." The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Indeed, Allah has replaced them for you with something better: the Day of Adha and the Day of Fitr."' (The text says:) 'Eid prayer is wajib' – he explicitly states obligation, because a text came from Abu Hanifa (about it). In one narration, and it is the more correct (al-ashahh) in terms of transmission and reasoning, and most scholars said so. Its being called 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir is because obligation is established by it due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) constant practice of the two Eid prayers without omission, as in al-Fath. So it is obligatory on the one upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, with its conditions – as you have learned – so all conditions of obligation and validity are required except the khutbah, because since it is deferred after the prayer, it is not a condition for it; it remains as an exhortation as in other times, and the khutbah is sunnah. So the Eid prayer is valid without it (i.e., the khutbah), but with dislike (isaa'ah) due to leaving the sunnah, just as one would be considered blameworthy if the khutbah were given before the Eid prayer, due to contradicting the Prophet's action.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, opening the chapter on Eid rulings. The author first explains the etymology of 'Eid': it is derived from 'awd (return) because blessings return, or from regular divine beneficence. He then relates a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet replaced the pre-Islamic festival days with Eid al-Adha and Eid al-Fitr, establishing the legitimacy of these celebrations. The core ruling follows: Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) according to the preferred view (al-ashahh) transmitted from Abu Hanifa. Although al-Jami' al-Saghir terms it 'sunnah', the author clarifies that this is not contradictory; the obligation is proven by the Prophet's continuous practice without ever omitting it. The conditions for obligation mirror those of Jumu'ah prayer: residence, health, freedom, and being male. However, the khutbah is not a condition for validity; it is a separate sunnah. If the khutbah is omitted or given before the prayer, the prayer remains valid but is blameworthy (makruh tanzihi) due to violating the established practice of the Prophet.

Key Terms
عيد (eid): A day of recurring joy and divine favor; the two major Islamic festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
واجبة (wajibah): Obligatory – a legal requirement proven by a zanni (probable) evidence, distinct from fard which is proven by qat'i evidence.
الأصح (al-ashahh): The more correct opinion among conflicting narrations from the imams.
جمعة (jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer; its conditions (residence, health, freedom, maleness) are also conditions for Eid prayer.
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered after the Eid prayer; it is sunnah, not a condition for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on Eid prayer in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard 'ayn
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, proven by the Prophet's continuous practice, and its conditions match those of Jumu'ah, with the khutbah being a sunnah not a condition.

The Thirteen Recommended Acts for Eid al-Fitr
Listing thirteen recommended acts with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the thirteen recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr, state their hukm (recommended), and cite the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice on Eid al-Fitr includes thirteen recommended acts that enhance the worship but are not obligatory.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah enumerates the thirteen acts that are recommended (nadb) for anyone performing the Eid al-Fitr prayer. These acts cover personal grooming, charity, and spiritual readiness. Each act is supported by a hadith, showing that the Prophet consistently followed these practices. While omission is not sinful, leaving them out neglects the full sunnah of Eid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list and its legal category
Read the passage and note that it begins by stating that thirteen things are 'nadb' (recommended). Understand that 'nadb' means mustahabb or sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah – performing them is meritorious, omitting them is not sinful but loses reward.
The term 'nadb' is used interchangeably with 'mustahabb' in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Examine the first three acts: eating before prayer
The first act is eating something sweet, preferably dates, and in an odd number. The hadith from Anas (Bukhari) shows the Prophet's consistent practice. Note that failure to eat before prayer is not sinful, but missing it entirely on that day may be punishable according to al-Diraya.
The odd number (witr) is a sunnah in many actions.
3
Review the acts related to personal hygiene and dress
The next acts are ghusl (full bath), using siwak, applying perfume, and wearing the best clothes (preferably white). Each is supported by specific hadith: ghusl from Ibn Majah, perfume from al-Ikhtiyar, and wearing a fanak cloak from al-Hidayah.
Ghusl for Eid is sunnah, not fard, unlike janabah.
4
Understand the acts of charity and social demeanor
The passage then covers paying sadaqat al-fitr before the prayer (based on Ibn Umar's hadith), expressing joy, wearing a ring (even if not usual), showing cheerfulness to other believers, and giving extra charity. These acts reflect the spirit of Eid.
Sadaqat al-fitr is wajib; paying before prayer is recommended for acceptance.
5
Analyze the final acts: timeliness and devotion
The last acts are tabkir (being alert early) and ibtikar (hastening to the prayer place to gain first row reward), and praying Fajr in the neighborhood mosque so that the entire outing is devoted to worship. These show care for the importance of Eid.
Tabkir and ibtikar are both recommended for maximizing reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب أي استحب لمصلي العيد في يوم الفطر ثلاثة عشر شيئا أن يأكل بعد الفجر قبل ذهابه للمصلى شيئا حلوا كالسكر وندب أن يكون المأكول تمرا وأن يكون عدده وترا كثلاث لما روى البخاري عن أنس قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يغدو يوم الفطر حتى يأكل تمرات ويأكلهن وترا وبه يتحقق معنى الاسم ومبادرة امتثال الأمر كذا في الاختيار ولو لم يأكل قبلها لا يأثم ولو لم يأكل في يومه ذلك ربما يعاقب كذا في الدراية وندب أي سن أن يغتسل وقدمنا أنه للصلاة لما روى ابن ماجه كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يغتسل يوم الفطر ويوم النحر ويوم عرفة ويستاك لأنه مندوب إليه في سائر الصلوات وأعم الحالات ويتطيب لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يتطيب يوم العيد ولو من طيب أهله كذا في الاختيار ويلبس أحسن ثيابه التي يباح لبسها للرجال ومن السنة لبس البيض وكان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم جبة فنك يلبسها في الجمعة والأعياد كذا في الاختيار وفي الهداية جبة فنك أو صوف انتهى والفنك حيوان يشبه الثعلب ويؤدي صدقة الفطر إن وجبت عليه لحديث ابن عمر أنه قال أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بزكاة الفطر أن نؤديها قبل خروج الناس إلى الصلاة وقال من أداها قبل الصلاة فهي زكاة مقبولة ومن أداها بعد الصلاة فهي صدقة من الصدقات كما في التبيين ويظهر الفرح بطاعة الله وشكر نعمته ويتختم فيه لما روي أنه من كان لا يتختم من الصحابة في سائر الأيام تختم يوم العيد كذا في الدراية ويظهر البشاشة في وجه كل من يلقاه من المؤمنين وكثرة الصدقة النافلة حسب طاقته زيادة عن المعتاد له والتبكير وهو سرعة الانتباه أول الوقت أو قبله لأداء العبادة بنشاط والابتكار وهو المسارعة إلى المصلى لينال فضيلته وفضل الصف الأول وصلاة الصبح في مسجد حيه لقضاء حقه ويتمحض ذهابه لعبادة مخصوصة اهتماما بشأنها
And it is recommended (nadb) – i.e., mustahabb – for the one praying the Eid on the day of Fitr (to do) thirteen things: to eat after dawn before going to the prayer place something sweet like sugar; and it is recommended that the food be dates; and that its number be odd (witr), like three – because of what Bukhari narrated from Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he ate dates, and he would eat them odd-numbered.' And by this, the meaning of the name is realized and the promptness in obeying the command, as in al-Ikhtiyar. If he does not eat before it (the prayer), he does not sin; but if he does not eat on that day, perhaps he will be punished, as in al-Diraya. And it is recommended – i.e., sunnah – that he perform ghusl; we already mentioned that it is for the prayer – because of what Ibn Majah narrated: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would perform ghusl on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the day of Arafah.' And to use siwak, because it is recommended in all prayers and most situations. And to apply perfume – because the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) would apply perfume on the day of Eid, even from his wife's perfume, as in al-Ikhtiyar. And to wear his best clothes that are permissible for men to wear, and from the sunnah is to wear white. The Prophet (peace be upon him) had a cloak of fur (junna fanak) that he would wear on Fridays and the two Eids, as in al-Ikhtiyar; in al-Hidaya: a cloak of fanak or wool – end. Al-fanak is an animal resembling a fox. And to pay sadaqat al-fitr, if it is obligatory upon him – because of the hadith of Ibn Umar that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded us to pay zakat al-fitr before the people go out to the prayer,' and he said: 'Whoever pays it before the prayer, it is an accepted zakat; and whoever pays it after the prayer, it is charity from among charities,' as in al-Tabyin. And to express joy for obedience to Allah and thankfulness for His blessing; and to wear a ring on that day – because it has been reported that some companions who did not ordinarily wear rings would wear one on the day of Eid, as in al-Diraya. And to show cheerfulness (al-bashasha) in the face of every believer he meets; and to give abundant optional charity (sadaqah) according to his capacity, more than his usual habit; and al-tabkir – i.e., being alert early, at the beginning of the time or before it, to perform worship actively; and al-ibtikar – i.e., hastening to the prayer place to attain its virtue and the virtue of the first row; and to pray the Dawn Prayer (Subh) in the mosque of his neighborhood to fulfill its right, and his going becomes solely for a specific act of worship, showing care for its importance.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage expounds on the thirteen recommended acts (mustahabbat) for the day of Eid al-Fitr, as stated in the matn. The author (Imam al-Tahtawi or the commentator) provides hadith proofs for each. The list includes: (1) Eating something sweet after Fajr before going to the musalla, preferably dates; (2) Eating an odd number (like 3, 5, 7) – based on the hadith of Anas. (3) Performing ghusl – for which the hadith from Ibn Majah is cited. (4) Using siwak (toothstick). (5) Applying perfume – the Prophet would use perfume even from his wives' supply. (6) Wearing one's best clothes – white is sunnah; the Prophet had a special cloak (junna fanak) for Fridays and Eids. (7) Paying sadaqat al-fitr before the Eid prayer – based on the command from Ibn Umar's hadith. (8) Showing joy and gratitude. (9) Wearing a ring (takhattum) – even for those who usually do not, as reported from some companions. (10) Showing cheerfulness to fellow believers. (11) Giving extra charity beyond normal. (12) Going early (tabkir – being alert and heading out early). (13) praying Fajr in the neighborhood mosque – so that his entire outing is dedicated to worship. The author notes that failure to eat before the prayer does not incur sin, but failure to eat at all on that day may be punishable (from al-Diraya). These acts are sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah? Actually, they are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.

Key Terms
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; an act whose performance is meritorious but omission is not sinful.
وتر (witr): Odd number; a recommended practice in many religious acts (e.g., eating an odd number of dates).
غسل (ghusl): Full ritual washing; recommended for Eid prayer.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan before Eid prayer.
تبكير (tabkir): Going early to the prayer place; being alert and starting early.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Ten
C) Thirteen
D) Fifteen

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Eid al-Fitr sunnah includes thirteen specific recommended acts that enhance the celebration; knowing and acting on them increases reward and follows the established Hanafi practice.

Sunan of Eid: Recommended Acts Before the Eid Prayer
Lists and explains sunan acts for Eid day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan acts before Eid prayer and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Eid sunan beautify the day; giving sadaqat al-fitr before prayer perfects it.

The day of Eid is a celebration of completing Ramadan. The Prophet (peace be upon him) established certain sunan to enhance the joy and spirituality of the day. This lesson examines those recommended acts and their proofs, helping you distinguish what is sunna from what is merely permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan acts
Read the passage carefully and list all the recommended acts for the day of Eid before the prayer. Note that the author uses 'yaf`ilu' or 'yandubu' to indicate sunna.
The acts include ghusl, miswak, perfume, best clothes, sadaqat al-fitr, showing joy, charity, early attendance (tabkir and ibtikar), and praying Fajr in the local mosque.
2
Locate the evidence for each act
For each sunna, the passage cites a hadith or a scholarly reference. Identify the evidence provided in the commentary (the sharh) for each act.
For example, ghusl is supported by a hadith from Ibn Majah; sadaqat al-fitr by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the timing of sadaqat al-fitr
Focus on the hadith about sadaqat al-fitr: it must be paid before the Eid prayer. The passage explains the consequence of paying after the prayer.
The hadith distinguishes between zakah (if paid before) and sadaqah (if paid after).
4
Distinguish between sunna and wajib
Recognize that these acts are sunna mu'akkada, not wajib. The text mentions that not eating before prayer is not sinful but may incur punishment, emphasizing the difference.
Sunna acts are recommended; omitting them is permissible but not preferable.

(1) امتثال الأمر، كذا في ( الاختيار » ، ولو لم يأكل قبلها لا يأثم، ولو لم يأكل في يومه ذلك ربما يعاقب كذا في ( الدراية» ، (وَ) ندب أي سن أن (يَغْتَسِلَ) وقدمنا أنه للصلاة، لما روى ابن ماجـه كـان رسول الله ل ل » « يَغْتَسِلُ يَوْمَ الفِطْرِ وَيَوْمَ النَّحْرِ وَيْوَمَ عَرَفَةَ » ) (وَيَسْتَاكَ ) لأنـه مندوب إليـه فـي سـائـر الصلوات وأعم الحالات، ويَتَطَيَّبَ) ( لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يتطيـب يــوم الـعـيـد، ولـو مـن طيب أهله » ) ، كذا في ( الاختيار » ، ويَلْبَسَ أحسن ثيابه) التي يباح لبسها للرجال، ومن السنة لبس البيض، « وكان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم جبـة فنـك يلبسها في الجمعة والأعياد ) (۳)، كذا في « الاختيار»، وفي الهداية جبة فنك أو صوف انتهى. والفنك حيوان يشبه الثعلب (ويؤدي صدقة الفطر، إن وجبت عليه لحديث ابن عمر أنه قال: « أمرنا رسول الله له و بزكاة الفطر أن نؤديها قبل خروج الناس إلى الصلاة ، وقال : مَنْ أداهَا قَبْلَ الصَّلاةِ ، فهي زَكَاةً مَقْبُولَة، وَمَنْ أدَّاهَا بَعْدَ الصَّلاةِ فَهِيَ صَدَقَةٌ مِنَ الصَّدَقَاتِ » (٥)، كما في «التبيين» ، ويُظْهِرَ الفرح بطاعة الله وشكر نعتمه. ويتختم فيه، لما روي أنـــه مَنْ كَانَ لا يَتَخَتُمُ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ فِي سَائِرِ الأَيَّامِ تَخَتَمَ يَوْمَ العِيدِ ) كذا في « الدراية»، (و) يظهر ( البَشَاشَةَ) في وجه كل من يلقاه من المؤمنين ( وكثرة الصَّدقة) النافلة (حَسَبَ طاقته) زيــادة عن المعتاد له والتبكير، وهـو : سرعة الانتباه أول الوقت أو قبله، لأداء العبادة بنشــاط ( والابتكار ) [ وهو : المسارعة إلى المصلى ] لينال فضيلته، وفضل الصف الأول، (وصلاة الصبح حيه لقضاء حقه، ويتمحض ذهابه لعبادة مخصوصة اهتماماً بشأنها،

(۲) أخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك (٢٥٦/٤)، عن الحسن بن علي قال: أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( أن نتطيب بأجود ما نجد أي: في العيدين» ولم أهتد إليه بلفظه. قبل الصلاة (٩٨٦).

He should perform ghusl, use miswak, apply perfume, wear his best clothes, give sadaqat al-fitr if it is obligatory upon him, show joy and cheerfulness, give abundant charity according to his capacity, and perform early attendance, which is promptness and going early, and pray Fajr in the mosque of his neighborhood.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage lists the sunan (recommended acts) for the day of Eid, as stated in the matn of Nur al-Idah, and the sharh (commentary) provides evidence and details. The acts include: performing ghusl (full body wash), using miswak, applying perfume, wearing the best permissible clothes (white is sunna), giving sadaqat al-fitr before the Eid prayer if it is obligatory, showing happiness and cheerfulness, increasing voluntary charity, going early to the prayer (tabkir and ibtikar: promptness and arriving early to the musalla), and praying Fajr in one's local mosque to fulfill its due. The author cites hadith for each: ghusl from Ibn Majah, perfume from al-Hakim, best clothes from al-Bayhaqi, sadaqat al-fitr timing from Bukhari and Muslim via Ibn Umar. The commentary notes that failure to eat before the prayer is not sinful but may incur punishment. The overall ruling is that these acts are sunna mu'akkada (emphasized sunna), and performing them earns reward.

Key Terms
تبكير (tabkir): Promptness in waking up and going early to the prayer.
ابتكار (ibtikar): Hastening to the musalla to attain virtue and first row.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan before Eid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is the preferred time to pay sadaqat al-fitr?
A) After the Eid prayer
B) Before the Eid prayer
C) On any day of Ramadan
D) It is not time-specific

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sunan for Eid enhance the celebration and ensure spiritual reward; giving sadaqat al-fitr before prayer is essential for its acceptance as zakat.

Rulings on Eid Prayer: Walking, Takbir, and Nafl Prohibition
Discusses walking to musalla, takbir, returning, and nafl prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on walking to the Eid musalla, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir (silent vs loud) with its evidence, identify the timing of stopping takbir, and apply the rule prohibiting nafl before Eid prayer.

Core Idea
Eid takbir is silent in the stronger view, but the school also permits loud recitation—know both.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah outlines several sunan and rulings for the day of Eid. It covers the etiquette of walking to the musalla, the highly debated issue of whether takbir should be silent or loud, when to stop, and the prohibition of voluntary prayer before the Eid prayer. Understanding these details ensures that one follows the sunna correctly and respects the legitimate differences within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
List the actions mentioned: walking to the musalla, saying takbir on the way, stopping takbir at a certain point, returning by another path, and avoiding nafl prayer before Eid.
Each has a specific ruling (sunna, makruh, etc.).
2
Determine the ruling for each action
Walking is sunna; takbir is sunna (manner disputed); returning by another path is sunna; nafl before Eid is makruh.
The text provides evidence for each.
3
Analyze the takbir dispute
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa says silent (sirran) based on Quran 7:205 and hadith; Sahibayn say loud (jahr) based on practice of Umar.
Both positions are narrated; no definitive tarjih in this text.
4
Note the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: one recites takbir silently, the other loudly. Both are acceptable within the school.
This affects the actual practice on Eid day.
5
Apply the nafl prohibition
Understand that it is makruh (disliked) to pray voluntary prayers before the Eid prayer, whether in the musalla or at home, according to the strongest view.
This is based on the practice of the Prophet and Ibn Abbas.

وفي قوله : ( ثم يتوجه إلى المُصَلَّى ) إشارة إلى تقديم ما ذكرناه على الذهاب إلى المصلى (ماشياً) بسكون وسكينة ووقار وغض بصر عما لا ينبغي أن يُبصر . وروي ( أنه عليه الصلاة والســلام كــان يخرج ماشياً » (١) ، وعن علي له : ( أنه خرج إلى المصلى ماشياً وراحلتـه تـقـاد إلى جنبـه » (٢)، وكـان عليه الصلاة والسلام يقول عند خروجه : « اللَّهمَّ إِنِّي خَرَجْتُ إِلَيْكَ مَخْرَجَ العَبْدِ الدَّلِيلِ » (۳)، كذا في معراج الدراية»، وفي ( البرهان روي أن علياً لهلهلهله لما قدم الكوفة استخلف من يُصلي بالضعفة صلاة العيد في الجامع، وخرج إلى الجبانة مع خمسين شيخاً يمشي ويمشون) انتهى، وهذا يخالف ما قاله بعض المشايخ الأفضل للمشايخ الركوب وللشبان المشي (مُكَبِّراً سِراً) عند أبي حنيفة، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاذْكُر رَبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِك [الأعراف : ٢٠٥] وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «خَيْرُ الذِّكْرِ الخَفِيُّ، وَخَيْرَ الرِّزْقِ مَا يَكْفِي ) ولأن الأصل في الثناء الإخفاء إلا مـا خـصـه ، الشــرع كــيــوم الأضحى، وعندهما يسن أن يكبر جهراً، وهو رواية عن الإمام، وكان عمر يرفع صوته بالتكبير، وهو مروي عن عليه ( ويقطعه) أي: التكبير (إذا انتهى إلى المُصلَّى، في رواية) جــزم بها في « الدراية » ، فقال: وعندنا إذا بلغ المصلى قطع (وفي رواية أخرى إذا افْتَتَحَ الصَّلاةَ، كذا في « الكافي» انتهى. وعليه عمل الناس، كذا في شرح المقدسي) انتهى. وفي ( التاتارخانية ) عن ( الحجة» قال « أبو جعفر » و به نأخذ انتهى. (ويرجع من طريق آخر ) تكثيراً للشهود كفعله ، لمـا فـي سـنـن أبـي داود: « أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أَخَذَ يَوْمَ العِيدِ فِي طَرِيْقِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ فِي طَرق آخَرَ » ) كما في ( البرهان». (۱) أخرجه ابن ماجه في إقامة الصلاة، باب ما جاء في الخروج إلى العيد ماشياً (١٢٩٧).
(۲) لم أهتد إليه بهذا اللفظ، ولكن روي عن سيدنا علي الله عنه قال : أن من السنة أن تخرج إلى العيد ماشياً. أخرجه الترمذي في أبواب العيدين (٥٣٠).
(۳) لم أهتد إليه فيما بين يدي من المصادر.
(٤) ذكره الصنعاني في سبل السلام (۷۱/۲).

Then he proceeds to the musalla walking, saying takbir quietly, and stops it when he reaches the musalla in one narration, and in another narration when he begins the prayer. And he returns by another path. And it is disliked to perform nafl prayer before the Eid prayer in the musalla and at home.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage covers rulings related to going to the Eid prayer. It is sunna to walk to the musalla with calmness and dignity, lowering the gaze. The Prophet (peace be upon him) walked, and Ali also walked while his mount was led beside him. Regarding takbir, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Hanifa, takbir is recited quietly (sirran) based on Quran 7:205 ('And remember your Lord within yourself') and the hadith 'The best remembrance is the hidden one.' According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), it is sunna to recite takbir loudly (jahr), and this is also a narration from Abu Hanifa, based on Umar's practice. The takbir stops when one reaches the musalla (in one narration) or when the prayer begins (in another narration; the latter is what people practice). It is sunna to return from a different path to increase witnesses, as the Prophet did. It is disliked (makruh) to pray nafl before the Eid prayer, whether in the musalla (by consensus) or at home (according to most Hanafi scholars, which is the correct view), supported by Ibn Abbas's report that the Prophet did not pray before the Eid prayer.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' on the way to Eid prayer.
المصلى (al-musalla): The open prayer ground designated for Eid prayer.
التنفل (al-tanafful): Performing voluntary (nafl) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on reciting takbir on the way to Eid prayer according to Abu Hanifa?
A) It is wajib and should be recited loudly.
B) It is sunna and should be recited silently.
C) It is makruh to recite it.
D) It is only recited at the musalla.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers two acceptable practices for Eid takbir: silent (Abu Hanifa) or loud (Sahibayn), and nafl before Eid is firmly disliked.

The Eid Takbir: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Volume and Timing
Commentary on sunnahs of going to Eid prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi positions on the volume and timing of takbir during the Eid walk, and identify the proofs cited by each side.

Core Idea
On Eid, silence or audibility in takbir – both are valid Hanafi positions with distinct proofs.

In this lesson we examine the sunnah of takbir when walking to the Eid musalla. The matn presents one ruling, but the commentary unpacks an important internal difference within the Hanafi school: should the takbir be recited silently or audibly? And when exactly should it stop? These questions touch on the methodology of deriving rulings from the Quran and Sunnah, and the flexibility of the school in accommodating multiple valid views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed elements
The passage addresses two points: (1) whether the takbir on the way to the musalla is said silently or audibly, and (2) when the takbir is cut off – upon reaching the musalla or upon starting the prayer.
2
Analyse Abu Hanifa's evidence for silent takbir
Abu Hanifa relies on the verse 'And remember your Lord within yourself' (7:205) and the hadith 'The best remembrance is the hidden one.' He also uses the principle that praise is normally concealed unless a specific exception exists (like the Day of Sacrifice).
The principle of concealment is a general usul rule for dhikr.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's evidence for audible takbir
The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) cite the practice of 'Umar raising his voice in takbir and a narration from Abu Hanifa himself that permits audibility. They also rely on the sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as transmitted in some reports.
This shows that even within the school, multiple proofs can support different views.
4
Compare the two narrations on when to stop the takbir
One narration (from Al-Dirayah) states that the takbir stops upon reaching the musalla. Another (from Al-Kafi) states that it stops upon beginning the prayer. The commentator notes that the latter is the practice of the people (i.e., the mufta bihi).
Both narrations are transmitted within the Hanafi school; the second is preferred in fatwa.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
While the commentator does not explicitly choose between the silent and audible views, he notes that the practice of the people follows stopping the takbir at the start of the prayer. For the volume, both views remain valid.
This reflects the Hanafi tradition of preserving ikhtilaf and following the practice of the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتوجه إلى المُصَلَّى ماشياً، مُكَبِّراً سِراً، ويقطعه إذا انتهى إلى المصلى، في رواية. وفي رواية أخرى إذا افْتَتَحَ الصَّلاةَ. ويرجعُ من طريق آخَرَ ويُكْرَهُ التنقل قبل صلاة العيد في المصلى والبيتِ.. وفي قوله : ( ثم يتوجه إلى المُصَلَّى ) إشارة إلى تقديم ما ذكرناه على الذهاب إلى المصلى (ماشياً) بسكون وسكينة ووقار وغض بصر عما لا ينبغي أن يُبصر . وروي ( أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يخرج ماشياً ) (١)، وعن علي رضي الله عنه : ( أنه خرج إلى المصلى ماشياً وراحلته تقاد إلى جنبه ) (٢)، وكان عليه الصلاة والسلام يقول عند خروجه : « اللهم إني خرجت إليك مخرج العبد الدليل » (٣)، كذا في معراج الدراية»، وفي ( البرهان روي أن علياً رضي الله عنه لما قدم الكوفة استخلف من يُصلي بالضعفة صلاة العيد في الجامع، وخرج إلى الجبانة مع خمسين شيخاً يمشي ويمشون) انتهى، وهذا يخالف ما قاله بعض المشايخ الأفضل للمشايخ الركوب وللشبان المشي (مُكَبِّراً سِراً) عند أبي حنيفة، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاذْكُر رَبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِك [الأعراف : ٢٠٥] وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «خَيْرُ الذِّكْرِ الخَفِيُّ، وَخَيْرُ الرِّزْقِ مَا يَكْفِي ) ولأن الأصل في الثناء الإخفاء إلا ما خصه الشرع كيوم الأضحى، وعندهما يسن أن يكبر جهراً، وهو رواية عن الإمام، وكان عمر يرفع صوته بالتكبير، وهو مروي عن عليه ( ويقطعه) أي: التكبير (إذا انتهى إلى المُصَلَّى، في رواية) جزم بها في « الدراية » ، فقال: وعندنا إذا بلغ المصلى قطع (وفي رواية أخرى إذا افْتَتَحَ الصَّلاةَ، كذا في « الكافي» انتهى. وعليه عمل الناس، كذا في شرح المقدسي) انتهى. وفي ( التاتارخانية ) عن ( الحجة» قال « أبو جعفر » و به نأخذ انتهى.
Then he proceeds to the musalla walking, making takbir silently, and he stops it when he reaches the musalla, in one narration. And in another narration, when he begins the prayer. And he returns by another route, and it is disliked to perform optional prayers before the Eid prayer in the musalla and at home. In His statement: (Then he proceeds to the musalla) is an indication to what we mentioned before going to the musalla (walking) with calmness, tranquility, dignity, and lowering the gaze from what should not be seen. And it is narrated that he (peace and blessings be upon him) used to go out walking. And from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): that he went out to the musalla walking while his riding animal was being led beside him. And he (peace and blessings be upon him) used to say upon his departure: 'O Allah, I have come out to You as the lowly servant comes out.' Thus in Ma'arij al-Dirayah. And in Al-Burhan: it is narrated that when 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) came to Kufa, he appointed someone to lead the weak in Eid prayer in the mosque, and he went out to the cemetery with fifty elders walking, and they walked. End. This contradicts what some shaykhs said: that riding is better for the elders and walking for the youth. (Making takbir silently) according to Abu Hanifa, due to His statement: 'And remember your Lord within yourself' [Al-A'raf: 205], and he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'The best remembrance is the hidden one, and the best sustenance is that which suffices.' And because the origin in praise is concealment except what the Law has specified, like the Day of Sacrifice. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is recommended to say takbir audibly, and this is a narration from the Imam. And 'Umar used to raise his voice with takbir, and it is narrated from him. (And he stops it) i.e., the takbir (when he reaches the musalla, in one narration) which is firmly stated in Al-Dirayah, and he said: According to us, when he reaches the musalla he stops. (And in another narration, when he begins the prayer, as in Al-Kafi. End. And upon this is the practice of the people, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. End. And in Al-Tatarikhaniyyah from Al-Hujjah, Abu Ja'far said: And we take this. End.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Sunnahs related to proceeding to the Eid prayer ground. It begins by stating the matn's ruling: one should walk to the musalla, recite takbir silently, and stop the takbir upon reaching the musalla (or upon starting the prayer in another narration). The commentator then elaborates on the walking: it should be with calmness and dignity, lowering the gaze. He supports this with narrations that the Prophet (peace be upon him) walked, and that 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) walked while his mount was led beside him. The commentator notes a difference of opinion regarding the takbir: according to Abu Hanifa, it is recited silently, based on Quran (Al-A'raf: 205) and hadith ('The best remembrance is the hidden one'), and the principle that praise is normally concealed unless specified otherwise. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), it is recited audibly, and this is also narrated from Abu Hanifa. The commentator also mentions that 'Umar used to recite audibly. On when to stop the takbir, two narrations are given: one says upon reaching the musalla (which is the relied-upon view in Al-Dirayah), the other says upon starting the Eid prayer (which is the practice of the people according to Sharh al-Maqdisi). Abu Ja'far in Al-Tatarikhaniyyah takes the latter. Thus, this passage presents a intra-Hanafi dispute on both the volume and timing of the takbir.

Key Terms
المُصَلَّى (al-musalla): The designated prayer ground outside the mosque for Eid prayers, also called al-jabbanah.
سِراً (sirran): In a low voice, not loud enough for others to hear distinctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must be recited audibly.
B) It must be recited silently.
C) There is a valid disagreement within the school: silent preferred by Abu Hanifa, audible by the Sahibayn.
D) The takbir is not recited at all before the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Two valid narrations within the Hanafi school govern takbir on Eid walk: silent (Abu Hanifa) or audible (Sahibayn); the timing of stopping also has two views, with the practice of the people following the start of prayer.

Returning from a Different Route on Eid
Ruling on returning path

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on returning from a different route after Eid prayer and identify its proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Returning from a different route is a confirmed sunnah to spread goodness and increase witnesses.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) would take one path to the Eid prayer and return via another path. This lesson explores the ruling, the evidence, and the wisdom behind this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is returning from the Eid prayer via a different route. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Some scholars consider it mustahab (recommended); the Hanafi school holds it as sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith in Sunan Abi Dawud: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) took one way on the day of Eid and then returned by another way.'
This hadith is also found in other collections.
3
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The wisdom is to increase the number of witnesses (or streets) that testify for the community, and to spread the joy of Eid in different areas.
Some say it is to greet more people or to make the ritual visible.
4
Apply in practice
After the Eid prayer, try to return via a different street or route than the one you took to come. This is not obligatory but carries reward.
If not possible, there is no sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
