Teaching Udhiyah and Takbir al-Tashriq in the Khutbah
Obligation of the khatib to teach sacrifice and takbir rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific topics the khatib must teach regarding udhiyah and takbir al-tashriq, and explain why the khutbah serves this educational purpose.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah is legislated to teach the rulings of the occasion.

The Eid khutbah is not merely a ritual; it is a platform for instruction. This lesson examines what the khatib must convey about the sacrifice and the takbirs, ensuring the congregation knows how to fulfill these seasonal acts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories taught
The passage mentions two subjects: udhiyah (sacrifice) and takbir al-tashriq (the post-prayer takbirs). Recognize that these are separate but both essential for Eid al-Adha.
2
List the specific rulings for udhiyah
The khatib must explain: who it is obligatory upon, from what wealth or type of animal, the required age, the time of slaughter, who should slaughter, and the rules regarding eating, charity, gifting, and storing the meat.
These details ensure the sacrifice is valid according to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Explain the purpose behind teaching
The passage states the khutbah was legislated to teach the rulings of the time. The khatib should therefore instruct the congregation because some may not know the rules.
This underscores the khutbah's educational function, not just spiritual exhortation.
4
Consider the timing suggestion
Shaykh Zayn recommends teaching in the preceding Friday khutbah for rules that apply before the Eid prayer. Even though he admits this is not transmitted, it shows practical concern for implementation.
The general principle: teach when it benefits the audience's action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعلمُ الأُضْحِيَة)، فيبين من تجب عليه، ومم تجب، وسن الواجب، ووقت ذبحه، والذابح، وحكم أكله، والتصدق، والهدية، والادخار منه، (و) يعلم ( تكبير التشريق في الخُطبة)، لأن الخطبة شرعت لتعليم أحكام الوقت، فيبين الأحكام في الخطبة، لجواز أن لا يعلمها بعض الحاضرين وقال الشيخ زين في ( البحر ) : ينبغي للخطيب أن يعلمهم الأحكام في الجمعة التي يليها العيد ليأتوا بها في محالها، لأن بعضها يتقدم على الخطبة فلا يفيد ذكــره فـيـهـا الآن، قال: ولم يره منقولاً، والعلم أمانة في عنق العلماء، انتهى.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the responsibilities of the khatib on Eid al-Adha. The khatib should teach the congregation about the sacrifice (udhiyah): who must perform it, what type of animal, the required age, the proper time, who may slaughter, and the rules regarding eating, charity, gifting, and storing the meat. He should also teach about takbir al-tashriq (the takbirs recited after each fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah) in his khutbah, because the purpose of the khutbah is to instruct people in the rulings of the occasion. Shaykh Zayn suggests teaching these in the preceding Friday khutbah for those rulings that apply before the Eid prayer itself, though he notes this is not a transmitted practice. The passage emphasizes the duty of the scholars to convey knowledge.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on Eid al-Adha, which is wajib for eligible Muslims.
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The takbirs recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah to Asr of 13th Dhul Hijjah.

Delaying Eid al-Adha Prayer: Ruling and Time Limit
Ruling on delaying Eid al-Adha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer and determine the permissible time window based on the presence or absence of a valid excuse.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer may be delayed up to three days with an excuse; without excuse, delay is disliked.

Eid al-Adha has a unique feature: its prayer can be performed on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or delayed up to three additional days (the days of tashriq) if there is a valid excuse. This flexibility differs from Eid al-Fitr, where the prayer is only for one day. In this lesson, you will learn the ruling, the time limit, and why it is tied to the sacrifice period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the Eid al-Adha prayer. The default ruling is that it should be performed on the day of Nahr (10th).
The prayer itself is wajib (necessary) according to the Hanafi school.
2
Distinguish delay with excuse vs. without excuse
With a valid excuse (e.g., rain, travel, illness), delaying the prayer up to three days is permissible without dislike. Without an excuse, delaying is disliked (makruh) because it goes against the established practice (māthūr).
The key factor is whether there is a preventing factor (māniʿ).
3
Note the time window
The prayer can be performed on any of the three days after the day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th), but only between sunrise and just before noon each day. After noon of the third day (13th), the time expires entirely.
Because the prayer is timed with the time of sacrifice (waqt al-uḍḥiyyah), which ends at sunset of the 13th, but the prayer itself must be before noon.
4
Understand the rationale
The prayer is tied to the sacrifice; its time is thus extended to allow for delays in performing the sacrifice. This is why it differs from Eid al-Fitr.
If the prayer is missed entirely, it is not made up (lā tuqḍā) because it is a sunnah prayer with a fixed time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتُؤَخَّرُ) صلاة عيد الأضحى بــلا كراهة (بعذر إلى ثلاثة أيام)، ومع الكراهة بدونه، لمخالفة المأثور بلا مانع، ولا تجوز بعد الزوال من اليوم الثالث لأنها لا تقضى، وإنما جازت في الأيام الثلاثة لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية، لكن فيما بين ارتفاع الشمس إلى ما قبل الزوال منها.
And the prayer of Eid al-Adha is delayed without dislike due to an excuse up to three days, and with dislike without an excuse, because it contradicts the transmitted practice without a preventing factor. And it is not permissible after the noon of the third day because it is not made up; and it is only permissible during the three days because it is timed with the time of sacrifice, but between sunrise and before noon of those days.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
The passage gives the ruling on delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer. Unlike Eid al-Fitr which can only be delayed one day, Eid al-Adha may be delayed up to three days (the days of tashriq) if there is a valid excuse, and this delay is without dislike. Without an excuse, delaying is disliked because it goes against the established practice. The prayer is not valid after noon of the third day (i.e., after the 13th of Dhul Hijjah) because the time of sacrifice ends at sunset of the 13th, and the prayer is tied to the sacrifice time. The valid time for the prayer each day is from sunrise until just before noon.

Key Terms
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).
عذر (ʿudhr): A valid excuse that permits delaying the Eid prayer without dislike, e.g., rain, travel, illness.
مخالفة المأثور (mukhālafat al-māthūr): Departing from the established sunnah practice; here, delaying without excuse contradicts the prophetic practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Until when can Eid al-Adha prayer be delayed with a valid excuse?
A) The next day only
B) Up to three days (11th to 13th Dhul Hijjah)
C) Up to seven days
D) It cannot be delayed at all

Key Takeaway
Eid al-Adha prayer may be delayed up to three days with a valid excuse without dislike; without excuse, delay is disliked, and the prayer is not valid after noon of the third day.

The Hanafi Ruling on Ta'rif: A Disliked Innovation
Ruling on ta'rif with proofs from qiyas and scholar statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'rif (makruh tanzih), identify the proof based on qiyas, and distinguish the mufta bihi position from a minority permissive view.

Core Idea
Ta'rif is not a sunnah; it is a disliked innovation because it imitates a specific Hajj ritual without basis.

This lesson delves into a practice known as ta'rif, where people gather on the day of 'Arafah in imitation of the Hajj standing. The Hanafi school firmly holds that this is not a recommended act; rather, it is a disliked innovation. We will examine the evidence, including the reasoning of later scholars like al-Kamal, and understand why this practice is discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ta'rif? The passage defines it as imitation of the standing at 'Arafat. The ruling is that it is 'not anything' – not a sunnah nor recommended. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites Imam Malik's statement that such things are innovations and al-Kamal's reasoning that an act of worship is tied to its specific place (qiyas).
The proof is based on analogy and the principle that innovation in religion is not permitted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Al-Kamal argues: 'Standing is known to be a devotion in a specific place, so it cannot be a devotion elsewhere.' This shows that imitating the standing outside 'Arafat is not a valid act of worship.
The specific phrase: 'qurbah fi makan makhsus'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis interpreted a riwayah from Abu Hanifah to permit ta'rif if done without standing and uncovering heads. However, the majority consider this a weak interpretation.
The source text says the permissive view is contingent on no standing and no uncovering.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Later authorities like al-Kamal and the author of al-Kafi emphasize dislike. The mufta bihi is that ta'rif is makruh and not to be practiced.
The prevention is to avoid doctrinal corruption and imitation of Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And what is mentioned in al-Kafi—his saying: From Abu Hanifah that it is not a sunnah, rather it is an event that people initiated, so whoever does it is allowed—is interpreted as being without standing and uncovering of heads, said al-Kamal. End quote. This and it is not hidden what is in gathering and prevention.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on several rulings related to the 'Id al-Adha prayer. The author explains that one should recite takbir loudly on the way to the prayer ground as a recommended act, following the Prophet's practice. He then addresses the duties of the khatib (preacher) in teaching the congregation both the rules of udhiyah (sacrificial animal) and takbir al-tashriq during the sermon, since the sermon is meant to educate. The commentary notes a preferred view that eating before the 'Id prayer is not necessarily disliked, though leaving it is better. Regarding the timing of the 'Id prayer, it can be delayed with an excuse up to three days; without excuse, delay is disliked because it opposes tradition, but the prayer is only valid between sunrise and zenith on those days. The bulk of the passage deals with 'ta'rif'—a practice where people gather on 'Arafah day in imitation of the Hajj standing. The author firmly states this is 'not anything,' i.e., not a sunnah and not recommended; many scholars rule it as disliked (makruh) and a blameworthy innovation (bid'ah), as it can lead to doctrinal confusion. It is thus a practice to be avoided.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rif): A practice of gathering on 'Arafah day in imitation of the Hajj standing, which the text states is not a sunnah and is disliked.
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The prescribed takbir recited after obligatory prayers from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the 'Id of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Recommended Acts for 'Id al-Adha and Timing of the Prayer
Rulings on recommended acts for 'Id al-Adha and timing of the prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended acts for 'Id al-Adha (takbir on the path, teaching udhiyah and takbir tashriq in sermon) and state the ruling on delaying the prayer with and without excuse.

Core Idea
The 'Id prayer is tied to sacrifice; it may be delayed up to three days only with excuse, and the sermon must educate the community.

This passage covers several practical aspects of the 'Id al-Adha prayer: the prophetic practice of reciting takbir loudly on the way to the prayer ground, the duty of the imam to teach the rulings of udhiyah and takbir al-tashriq during the sermon, and the permissibility of delaying the prayer under certain conditions. Understanding these rulings ensures the prayer is performed correctly and that the community is well-informed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act
The passage states that one makes takbir loudly on the path to the musalla. This is a mustahabb (recommended) act based on the practice of the Prophet.
The source says 'kama fa'ala al-nabi' indicating it is sunnah.
2
Identify the duty of the khatib
The imam must teach the rulings of udhiyah (sacrificial animal) and takbir al-tashriq during the sermon, because the sermon was prescribed to teach the rulings of the time.
Shaykh Zayn added that teaching in the preceding Jumu'ah is beneficial.
3
Analyze the ruling on delay
The 'Id al-Adha prayer may be delayed up to three days with an excuse without dislike. Without an excuse, delaying is makruh because it opposes the transmitted practice.
Delay is tied to the time of udhiyah.
4
Note the time limit
The prayer must be performed between sunrise and zawal (noon) on each of the three days. After zawal of the third day, it cannot be performed and is not made up later.
The prayer is only valid in these specific times.
5
Link to udhiyah
The reason for the three-day window is that the prayer is tied to the time of sacrifice (udhiyah), which spans three days.
This explains why delay is allowed despite the general rule that 'Id prayer is performed on the day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكَبِّرُ في الطَّرِيقِ جَهْرَاً. ويعلمُ الأَضْحِيَّة، وتكبير التَّشْرِيقِ، في الخطبة، وتُؤَخَرُ بعذرٍ إلى ثلاثةِ أَيَّامٍ.
والتعريف ليس بشيء
أضحيته أولاً، أما في حق غيره فلا ، ثم قيل الأكل قبل الصلاة مكروه، والمختار أنـه ليـس بـمـكــوه لكن يستحب تركه، ويُكَبِّرُ في الطريق ذاهباً إلى المصلى تكبيراً (جَهْرَاً) استحباباً، كما فعــل النبي ) كذا في « الاختيار»، ويعلمُ الأُضْحِيَة)، فيبين من تجب عليه، ومم تجب، وسن الواجب، ووقت ذبحه، والذابح، وحكم أكله، والتصدق، والهدية، والادخار منه، (و) يعلم ( تكبير التشريق في الخُطبة)، لأن الخطبة شرعت لتعليم أحكام الوقت، فيبين الأحكام في الخطبة، لجواز أن لا يعلمها بعض الحاضرين وقال الشيخ زين في ( البحر ) : ينبغي للخطيب أن يعلمهم الأحكام في الجمعة التي يليها العيد ليأتوا بها في محالها، لأن بعضها يتقدم على الخطبة فلا يفيد ذكــره فـيـهـا الآن، قال: ولم يره منقولاً، والعلم أمانة في عنق العلماء، انتهى. (وتُؤَخَّرُ) صلاة عيد الأضحى بــلا كراهة (بعذر إلى ثلاثة أيام)، ومع الكراهة بدونه، لمخالفة المأثور بلا مانع، ولا تجوز بعد الزوال من اليوم الثالث لأنها لا تقضى، وإنما جازت في الأيام الثلاثة لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية، لكن فيما بين ارتفاع الشمس إلى ما قبل الزوال منها، (والتعريف) يجيء لمعان: للإعلام، والتطيب من العرق، وهو الريح، وإنشاد الضالة، والوقوف بعرفات، والتشبه بأهل الموقف، وهو المراد هنا، فيجتمعون في مكان يوم عرفة، وهو (ليس بشيء) معتبر فهو غير مسنون وغير مستحب، وسئل الإمام مالك عن ذلك، فقال: وإنما مفاتح هذه الأشياء البدع، كذا في « الدراية » ، وقاله الكمال: والأولى الكراهة؛ لأن الوقوف عهد قربة في مكان مخصوص فلا يكون قربة في غيره انتهى. وفي ( الدرر والغرر » : ( : الصحيح الكراهة، ولا . يجوز [ الاختراع ] ) في الدين (۳) ، كذا في «الكافي ، وفي المنع منه حسم لمفسدة اعتقادية تُتُوقَّع من العوام، ونفس الوقوف، وكشف الرؤوس يستلزم التشبه وإن لم يقصد، ويحمل ما ذكره في « الكافي» بقوله: وعن أبي حنيفة أنه ليس بسنة، وإنما هو حدث أحدثه الناس فمن فعله جاز انتهى، على كونه بلا وقوف وكشف الرؤوس قاله الكمال ،انتهى هذا ولا يخفى ما في اجتماع وحسم .
And he makes takbir loudly on the path. And he teaches the udhiyah and takbir of tashriq in the sermon, and it (the prayer) is delayed due to an excuse up to three days. And ta'rif is nothing (i.e., not a sunnah). His udhiyah first, but regarding other than him then no. Then it was said that eating before the prayer is makruh, and the chosen view is that it is not makruh but leaving it is preferable. And he makes takbir on the path going to the musalla loudly as a recommended act, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did. This is in al-Ikhtiyar. And he teaches the udhiyah, so he explains upon whom it is obligatory, from what it is obligatory, the age of the obligatory (animal), the time of slaughter, the slaughterer, the ruling on eating it, giving charity, gifting, and storing from it. And he teaches takbir al-tashriq in the sermon, because the sermon was prescribed to teach the rulings of the time, so he explains the rulings in the sermon, since some of the attendees may not know them. And Shaykh Zayn said in al-Bahr: It is fitting for the khatib to teach them the rulings in the Jumu'ah that follows the 'Id so that they perform them in their proper places, because some of them precede the sermon so mentioning them now would not benefit. He said: I have not seen this transmitted. And knowledge is a trust upon the necks of scholars. End quote. And the 'Id al-Adha prayer is delayed without dislike due to an excuse up to three days, and with dislike without an excuse, due to contravening the transmitted practice without a barrier. And it is not permissible after the zawal of the third day because it is not made up. It is only allowed in the three days because it is tied to the time of udhiyah, but between sunrise and before zawal. And ta'rif has meanings: for announcing, perfuming from sweat (i.e., odor), searching for a lost item, standing at Arafat, and imitating the people of the standing. That is what is meant here. So they gather in a place on the day of Arafah, and it is not considered anything, so it is not a sunnah nor recommended. Imam Malik was asked about it, and he said: The keys of these things are only innovations. This is in al-Dirayah. And al-Kamal said: The better view is dislike, because standing is known to be a devotion in a specific place, so it cannot be a devotion elsewhere. End quote. And in al-Durar wa al-Gharar: The correct view is dislike, and innovation is not permitted in religion. This is in al-Kafi. And in forbidding it lies prevention of a doctrinal corruption feared from the common people. And the standing itself and uncovering of heads entails imitation even if not intended. And what is mentioned in al-Kafi—his saying: From Abu Hanifah that it is not a sunnah, rather it is an event that people initiated, so whoever does it is allowed—is interpreted as being without standing and uncovering of heads, said al-Kamal. End quote. This and it is not hidden what is in gathering and prevention.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on several rulings related to the 'Id al-Adha prayer. The author explains that one should recite takbir loudly on the way to the prayer ground as a recommended act, following the Prophet's practice. He then addresses the duties of the khatib (preacher) in teaching the congregation both the rules of udhiyah (sacrificial animal) and takbir al-tashriq during the sermon, since the sermon is meant to educate. The commentary notes a preferred view that eating before the 'Id prayer is not necessarily disliked, though leaving it is better. Regarding the timing of the 'Id prayer, it can be delayed with an excuse up to three days; without excuse, delay is disliked because it opposes tradition, but the prayer is only valid between sunrise and zenith on those days. The bulk of the passage deals with 'ta'rif'—a practice where people gather on 'Arafah day in imitation of the Hajj standing. The author firmly states this is 'not anything,' i.e., not a sunnah and not recommended; many scholars rule it as disliked (makruh) and a blameworthy innovation (bid'ah), as it can lead to doctrinal confusion. It is thus a practice to be avoided.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The prescribed takbir recited after obligatory prayers from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the 'Id of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible without dislike.
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is not allowed at all.
D) It is prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
The 'Id al-Adha prayer can be delayed up to three days with a valid excuse; without an excuse, delay is disliked. The sermon must include teaching of udhiyah and takbir al-tashriq.

Obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq and Its Conditions
Detailed explanation of when and on whom takbir al-tashriq is wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq, identify the Quranic proof, list the conditions for its obligation, and apply the ruling to followers with various statuses.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib immediately after each fard prayer in congregation from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of 'Id.

This passage establishes the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq with its Quranic proof, then details the specific conditions: who must recite it, when, and how. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly observing this 'Id practice. We will walk through each condition and its application to travelers, women, and those who join late.

Guided Path
1
Locate the ruling and its primary proof
The passage opens by stating that Takbir al-Tashriq is obligatory (wajib) according to the choice of the majority, and cites Quran 2:203 as evidence. Identify the ruling and the verse used.
The verse commands remembrance of Allah during 'numbered days' which the Hanafis interpret as including this specific takbir.
2
Determine the time frame
The takbir begins after Fajr of 'Arafah (9th Dhu al-Hijjah) and ends after 'Asr of the 'Id (10th). Note that this covers eight obligatory prayers (if Fajr and 'Asr are counted).
It excludes nafl, witr, janazah, and 'Id prayers themselves.
3
Identify the conditions for obligation
The passage lists conditions: it must be recited immediately (fawr) after every fard prayer performed in congregation; the imam must be a resident in a city (misr); followers are obligated even if they are travelers, slaves, or women; the follower who joins late (masbuq) recites after completing his own prayer.
Women lower their voice because their voice is 'awrah.
4
Analyze special cases and the effect of the imam's actions
If the imam forgets the takbir, the follower recites after the imam does something that breaks the continuity (e.g., leaving the mosque, intentional hadath, laughter, speech). If the imam has a hadath after salam but before takbir, he recites without renewing wudu according to the correct view.
This shows the importance of the condition of fawr (immediacy).

And Takbir al-Tashriq is obligatory, according to the choice of the majority, due to His statement: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days.' And he performs it once, on condition that it be immediately after every obligatory prayer, which includes Jumu'ah, and excludes nafl, witr, janazah, and 'Id if that prayer is performed. And he performs it, even if it be a make-up of the obligatory prayers of this period, which are eight. With a congregation, which excludes the one praying alone. Due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'There is no takbir during the days of tashriq for the one alone or two; takbir is for the one who prays in congregation.' It was narrated by Harb and Abu Bakr ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz with their chains. And Ahmad narrated with his chain from Ibn 'Umar that he did not make takbir when he prayed alone during the days of tashriq. This is in the handwriting of Shaykh al-Islam al-Maqdisi. With a congregation that is recommended, which excludes the congregation of women. And the woman lowers her voice unlike men because she is 'awrah. And upon the one who caught the prayer after the imam (masbuq) to make takbir, because he is a follower by the opening takbir. So he recites takbir after finishing. If he followed the imam forgetfully, his prayer is not invalidated; but in the case of talbiyah, it does invalidate. And the one in ihram begins with takbir then talbiyah. This is in Fath al-Qadir. And if the imam leaves the takbir, the follower makes takbir, because it is performed aftereffect of the prayer, not within it. But the follower waits until the imam does something that cuts the takbir, which prevents continuation, such as leaving the mosque, intentional hadath, loud laughter, or speaking even forgetfully. When the imam does that, the follower recites takbir, as in al-Tabyin and others. And in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Khulasa: If the imam has a hadath after the salam before the takbir, the correct view is that he recites takbir and does not need wudu. End quote. And al-Zayla'i said: If hadath overtakes him before he recites takbir, he performs wudu and recites takbir according to the correct view. End quote. And Imam al-Sarakhsi said: The correct view in my opinion is that he recites takbir and does not leave the mosque for wudu, because since takbir does not require purity, his leaving without need would cut the immediacy of the prayer, so he cannot recite takbir after that. So he recites immediately to settle the matter. This is in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i'. And that is according to Abu Hanifah, due to the athar of 'Ali, and due to what is from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn...
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation (wujub) of Takbir al-Tashriq according to the Hanafi school, with the majority of scholars. The primary proof is the Quranic verse commanding remembrance of Allah during the 'numbered days.' The takbir begins after Fajr of 'Arafah (9th of Dhu al-Hijjah) and continues until after 'Asr of the 'Id (10th). It is recited once immediately after each obligatory (fard) prayer performed in congregation. This includes Jumu'ah but excludes nafl, witr, janazah, and 'Id prayers. It applies to prayers that have been performed, even if make-up for missed prayers within this period. The obligation falls upon the imam who is a resident in a city (misr) and upon everyone who follows him in prayer, even if the follower is a traveler, slave, or woman. The woman lowers her voice because her voice is considered 'awrah (to be concealed). A person who joins the congregation late (masbuq) must recite the takbir after completing his own prayer. If the imam forgets the takbir, the follower recites it after the imam does something that breaks the continuity of the prayer, such as leaving the mosque or having an intentional hadath. If the imam experiences a hadath after salam but before takbir, the correct view is that he can still recite takbir without renewing wudu, as takbir does not require purity. This is the position of Abu Hanifah based on reports from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The prescribed takbir recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of 9th Dhu al-Hijjah to 'Asr of 10th, once, with specific conditions on imam and congregation.
فور (fawr): Immediately after the prayer, without intentional delay, though a slight natural delay does not harm.
مصر (misr): A city or garrison town where an imam is considered resident; excludes rural areas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The imam and everyone who follows him, even if they are travelers, slaves, or women.
C) Only men who pray in congregation.
D) Everyone who prays, whether alone or in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is a wajib practice for those praying in congregation behind a resident imam during the specified days; its conditions ensure it is performed correctly and in accordance with the Sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Takbir al-Tashriq: Obligation, Conditions, and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains obligation of takbir after fard prayers during tashriq days, including dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Takbir al-Tashriq, identify its conditions according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain why the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer, but when and for whom? The Sahibayn's broader view became the operative fatwa.

Takbir al-Tashriq is a specific recitation of 'Allahu Akbar' performed after the fard prayers during the days of Tashriq. While the Hanafi school agrees it is wajib, there is an internal dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the exact timing and who must perform it. Understanding this dispute and why the Sahibayn's position became the mufta bihi is essential for correctly applying this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Recognise what Takbir al-Tashriq is and its hukm. The text states it is wajib. Note why it is not fard: the Quranic proof is zanni al-dalala according to Hanafi usul.
Wajib in Hanafi terminology is established by a zanni proof, while fard requires a qat'i proof.
2
List the conditions according to Abu Hanifa
From the passage, extract the conditions: must be after a fard prayer, performed in a mustahabb congregation, by an imam resident in a misr and those who follow him, from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of Eid, and said immediately (fawran).
Conditions are for the obligation (shurut al-wujub).
3
Examine the proofs cited by Abu Hanifa
Look at the dalil block: Quran 2:203 and the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. Understand how these proofs restrict the obligation to congregational prayer.
The hadith explicitly negate takbir for those praying alone.
4
Present the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the takbir is wajib after every fard prayer on whoever prays it, even alone, traveler, or villager, from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of the 5th day. Their proof: the Quranic command to remember Allah in those days, and the principle of caution (ihtiyat).
They interpret the same Quranic verses more broadly.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the thamarah al-khilaf
The text states the fatwa and practice are on the Sahibayn's view. Identify the practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, a person praying alone does not say the takbir; according to the Sahibayn, he does. Also, the period is longer in the Sahibayn's view.
The tarjih is based on caution (ihtiyat) and general practice.

Source Text

ويجب تكبير التشريق، من بعدِ فجرِ عَرَفَةَ إلى عصر العيد، مرّةً، فَوْرَ كلّ فرضِ أُدِّيَ بجماعةٍ مُسْتَحَبَّةِ، على إمام مقيم بمصر، وعلى من اقتدى به، ولو كان مسافراً، أو رقيقاً، أو أنثى، عند أبي حنيفة، رحمه الله.. نساء أهل هذا الزمن مع الرجال والأحداث، ورعاع العامة، وغيرهم من الشدة والبأس والفتنة، ذلك واجب . ( ويجب تكبيرُ التَّشريق) في اختيار الأكثر لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَعْدُودَاتِ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۰۳] (من بعدِ ) صلاة (فجرِ عَرَفَةَ إلى عقـب (عـصـر الـعـيـد)، ويـأتـي بـه (مرةٌ) بشرط أن يكون فَوْرَ كلّ) صلاة (فرض)، شمل الجمعة، وخرج النفل والوتر وصلاة الجنازة والعيد إذا كان ذلك الفرض (أُدِّيَ) أي: صلي، ولو كان قضـاء مـن فــروض هـذه الـمـدة فـيـهـا، وهـي الثمانية (بجماعة) خرج به المنفرد، لما عن ابن مسعود : « ليس التكبير أيام التشريق على الواحد المنفرد والاثنين، التكبير على من صلى بجماعة » ، رواه حرب، وأبو بكـر بـن عبـد العـزيـز بإسنادهما، وروى أحمد بإسناده عن ابن عمر ) أنه إذا صلى وحده في أيام التشريق لم يكبر » ، كذا بخط شيخ الإسلام ( المقدسي » (مُسْتَحَبَّةٍ) خرج به جماعة النساء، وقوله: (عـلـى إمـام.... إلخ متعلق بيجب، (مُقيم) : خرج به المسافر ، فلابد من الإقامة ( بمِصْر ) احترز بـه عـن المقيم بغيرها. (و) يجب التكبير على ( من اقتدى بِهِ) أي: بالإمام المقيم ( ولو كان) المقتدي (مسافراً، أو رقيقاً، أو أنثى) تبعاً للإمام، والمرأة تخفض صوتها دون الرجال لأنه عورة )، وعلى المسبوق التكبير، لأنه مقتد تحريمة، فيكبر بعد فراغه، لو تابع الإمام ناسياً لم تفسد صلاته، وفي التلبية: تفسد (٣)، ويبدأ المحرم بالتكبير ثم بالتلبية، كذا في فتح القدير ) ، وإذا ترك الإمام التكبير يكبر المقتدي؛ لأنـه يؤدي في أثر الصلاة لا في نفسها، ولكن ينتظر المأموم حتى يأتي الإمام بشيء يقطع التكبير، وهـو ما يمنع البناء، كالخروج من المسجد والحدث العمد، والقهقهة، والكلام ولو سهواً، فإذا فعل الإمام ذلك كبر المقتدي، كما في ) التبيين ) وغيره، وفي ( التاتارخانية ) عن ( الخلاصة » : الإمام إذا أحدث بعد السلام قبل التكبير الأصح أنه يكبر ولا يلزمه الطهارة انتهى. وقال الزيلعي: وإن سبقه الحدث قبل أن يكبر توضأ وكبر على الصحيح انتهى. وقال الإمام ( السرخسي : الأصح عندي أنه يكبر ولا يخرج من المسجد للطهارة، لأن التكبير لما لم يفتقر إلى الطهارة، كان خروجه مع عدم الحاجة قاطعاً لفور ،الصلاة، فلا يمكنه التكبير بعد ذلك، فيكبر للحال جمعاً جزماً، كذا في «البحر » عــن البدائع » ، وذلك ( عِند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لأثر علي له الله: ولما عن ابن مسعود وابن .
(۱) أخرجه الطبراني في المعجم الكبير (٢٦٨/١٢). (۲) والصحيح أنه يؤدي إلى الفتنة، والمراد بالعورة معناها اللغوي، وهو العيب. ط. (۳) لأنها كلام أجنبي. ط. (٤) أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه (٤٨٨/١).

وقالا: يجبُ فَوْرَ كُلِّ فرض على مَنْ صَلاهُ، ولو منفرداً، أو مسافراً ، أوْ قَرَوِيَاً إلى عَصْرِ الخامس من يومِ
عَرَفَةَ، وبه يُعْمَلُ، وعليه الفَتْوَى..
والإجماع منعقد على الأقل، فكان الأحوط الأخذ بالأقل، كذا في « الدراية»، عن «جــامـع » الكردي، (وقالا ) أي: أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله ( يَجبُ) التكبير (فَوْرَ كُلِّ فرض على مَنْ صَلَاهُ، ولو كان (منفرداً، أو مسافراً، أوْ قَرَوِيَّاً) لأنه تبع للمكتوبة، من فجر عرفة (إلى) عقب (عَصْرِ الخامس من يومِ عرفة)، فيكون إلى آخر أيام التشريق، (وبه) أي بقولهما (يُعْمَلُ ، وعليه الفتوى) إذ هو الاحتياط لأن الإتيان بما ليس عليه أولى من ترك ما عليه، فيكون الأخذ بالأكثر احتياطاً، ولأنه قال تعالى: وَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَعْدُودَاتِ﴾ [الثقة : ٢٠٣] وقال في موضع آخر : ﴿وَيَذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللَّهِ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَّعْلُومَت [ الحج : ۲۸] المعلومات أيام [ العشر ] من ذي الحجة، والمعدودات: أيام التشريق، وقيل: المعلومات: أيام النحر، والمعدودات أيام التشريق، وسميت معدودات لقلتها، وهكذا روي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال: اليوم الأول من المعلومات، واليومان الأوسطان من المعلومات والمعدودات (٢)، فلما أمر الله تعالى بالذكر في هذه الأيام، ولم نجد ذكراً سوى التكبيرات فتجب، كذا في جامع الإسبيجاني»، وفيه وفي التحرير » و « الخلاصة »، و « المجتبى»، و «فتاوى العتابي : والفتوى على قولهما، وعلـيـه عـمـل الأمصار في أغلب الأعصار ، كذا في «معراج الدراية»، وفي ( السراج الوهاج»، و«الجوهرة»، وفي
مجمع الروايات » ، قال الزاهدي والفتوى والعمل في عامة الأمصار على قولهما.

تنبيه: قال في « الدراية و المستصفى هذه الإضافة في تكبير التشريق إنما تستقيم على قولهما؛ لأن بعض التكبيرات تقع في أيام التشريق عندهما، وعلى قول أبي حنيفة: لا يقع شيء من التكبير فيها فلا تستقيم الإضافة، لكن أدنى الملابسة كاف للإضافة، وقيل: التشريق اسم لصلاة العيد، لأنها تؤدى عند إشراق الشمس وارتفاعها، وقيل: التشريق عبارة عن هذه الأيام، لما فيها من تشريق لحوم الأضاحي، فعلى هذين تستقيم الإضافة على قوله انتهى وقال الكمال: الإضافة بيانية، أي: التكبير الذي هو التشريق، فإن التكبير لا يسمى تشريقاً إلا إذا كان بتلك الألفاظ في شيء مــــن الأيام المخصوصة، فهو حينئذ متفرع على قول الكل، وفي » الكافي»، و « الدراية » : ما يقتضي عدم
(۱) ما بين الحاصرتين في المخطوط ( التشريق) والصواب ما أثبتناه من البحر (۱۷۷/۲). (۲) بل ثلاثة معلومة ومعدودة وهي أيام النحر، أما الرابع فمعدود فقط، وأما إذا أريد بأيام التشريق الأيام الثلاثة التي بعد أيام النحر، فالمراد بالأول يوم النحر وهو معلوم، والأوسطان الحادي عشر والثاني عشر معلومـان و معدودان، والأخير معدود لا غير وهو المتبادر. ط.
1001-
And Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib, from after Fajr of Arafa to Asr of Eid, once, immediately after every fard prayer performed in a congregation that is mustahabb, upon an iqamah-resident imam in a misr, and upon whoever follows him, even if that follower is a traveler, a slave, or a woman, according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him... Women of this era with men and youths, and the rabble of the common people, and others due to severity and hardship and tribulation, that is wajib. (And Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib) in the view of the majority due to His statement: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days' [Quran 2:203] (from after) the prayer of (Fajr of Arafa until after Asr of Eid), and it is performed (once) on condition that it is immediately after every (fard) prayer, includes Jumuah, and excludes nafl, witr, funeral prayer, and Eid prayer if that fard is performed, even if it is a makeup prayer from the fard prayers of this period, which are eight (in congregation) excludes the one praying alone, because of Ibn Mas'ud: 'There is no takbir during the days of tashriq upon the one alone and the two, takbir is upon whoever prays in congregation', narrated by Harb and Abu Bakr ibn Abd al-Aziz with their chains, and Ahmad narrated with his chain from Ibn Umar that when he prayed alone during the days of tashriq he did not say takbir, as is in the handwriting of Shaykh al-Islam al-Maqdisi (mustahabb) excludes the congregation of women, and His statement: (upon an imam... etc.) is attached to 'wajib', (resident) excludes the traveler, so residence is necessary (in a misr) as a precaution against one who resides elsewhere. (And) takbir is wajib upon (whoever follows him) i.e., the resident imam (even if) the follower (is a traveler, a slave, or a woman) following the imam, and the woman lowers her voice unlike men because it is awrah, and upon the latecomer is takbir, because he follows in the tahrimah, so he says takbir after finishing; if he followed the imam forgetfully, his prayer is not invalidated, while in talbiyah it invalidates, and the one in ihram begins with takbir then talbiyah, as in Fath al-Qadir. If the imam omits the takbir, the follower says it, because it is performed after the prayer not within it, but the follower waits until the imam does something that cuts off the takbir, which is what prevents building, like leaving the mosque, intentional hadath, guffawing, and speaking even forgetfully; when the imam does that, the follower says takbir, as in al-Tabyin and others. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Khulasa: If the imam has hadath after the salam before the takbir, the correct view is that he says takbir and is not required to perform purification, end. Al-Zaylai said: If hadath overtakes him before he says takbir, he performs ablution and says takbir on the correct view, end. Imam al-Sarakhsi said: The correct view in my opinion is that he says takbir and does not leave the mosque for purification, because since takbir does not require purification, his leaving without need would cut off the immediacy of the prayer, so he cannot say takbir after that, so he says takbir immediately to be sure, as in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i. That is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, due to the athar of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, and from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn... And they two said: It is wajib immediately after every fard upon whoever prays it, even if alone, or a traveler, or a villager, until Asr of the fifth day from Arafa, and with it practice is done, and upon it is the fatwa. And consensus is established upon the minimum, so caution is in taking the minimum, as in al-Dirayah from Jami' al-Kuridi. (And they two said) i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them: (It is wajib) takbir (immediately after every fard upon whoever prays it, even if (alone), or a traveler, or a villager) because it follows the obligatory prayer, from Fajr of Arafa (until) after (Asr of the fifth day from Arafa), so it is until the end of the days of tashriq. (And with it) i.e., their statement (practice is done, and upon it is the fatwa) because it is caution since doing what is not upon one is better than leaving what is upon one, so taking the more is caution, and because He said: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days' [Quran 2:203] and said elsewhere: 'And mention the name of Allah on known days' [Quran 22:28]. The known days are the ten of Dhul Hijjah, and the numbered days are the days of tashriq; and it is said: the known days are the days of sacrifice, and the numbered days are the days of tashriq, and they were called numbered due to their scarcity. Thus it is reported from Abu Yusuf that he said: The first day is from the known, and the two middle days are from the known and the numbered. So when Allah commanded remembrance during these days, and we found no remembrance besides the takbirs, so they are wajib, as in Jami' al-Isbijdhani; and in it, and in al-Tahrir, and al-Khulasa, and al-Mujtaba, and Fatawa al-Attabi: The fatwa is on their statement, and upon it is the practice of the regions in most ages, as in Miraj al-Dirayah, and in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and al-Jawhara, and in Majma' al-Riwayat. Al-Zahidi said: The fatwa and practice in most regions is upon their statement. (Note: He said in al-Dirayah and al-Mustasfa: This addition in 'Takbir al-Tashriq' is only correct according to them, because some takbirs occur during the days of tashriq according to them; according to Abu Hanifa, none of the takbirs occur in them, so the addition is not correct, but the slightest connection is sufficient for the addition. And it is said: al-Tashriq is a name for the Eid prayer because it is performed at the rising of the sun (ishraq). And it is said: Tashriq refers to these days because of the drying (tashriq) of the meat of sacrifices. So on these two, the addition is correct according to him. Ended. Al-Kamal said: The addition is explanatory, i.e., the takbir which is al-tashriq, for the takbir is not called tashriq unless it is with those specific words on specific days. Thus it is then derived from the statement of all. And in al-Kafi and al-Dirayah: what necessitates non...
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah discusses the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq. It begins by stating that Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib according to the majority. The obligation is immediate after each fard prayer that is performed in a congregation that is mustahabb (i.e., not a congregation of women alone). The takbir is said once. It applies specifically to an imam who is a resident in a city (misr) and to anyone who follows him in prayer, even if that follower is a traveler, a slave, or a woman. Women are to lower their voices because their voice is awrah. The passage then cites the Quranic verse 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days' (2:203) as the basis, along with hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar that the takbir is only for those who pray in congregation. The passage then provides details: if the imam omits the takbir, the follower says it, but the follower must wait until the imam does something that cuts off the connection, such as leaving the mosque or having intentional hadath. There is discussion about what to do if the imam has hadath after salam but before takbir; the preferred view is that he says takbir without renewing wudu. The passage then contrasts the view of Abu Hanifa with that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). According to Abu Hanifa, the takbir begins from Fajr of Arafa and ends at Asr of Eid, and it is only for those in congregation. According to the Sahibayn, the takbir is said immediately after every fard prayer by whoever prays it, even if alone, traveler, or villager, and it continues until Asr of the fifth day of Arafa (i.e., until the end of the days of tashriq). The fatwa and practice are on the view of the Sahibayn because it is more cautious and covers more cases. A note (tanbih) explains the term 'Takbir al-Tashriq' – it is only called 'tashriq' because according to the Sahibayn some of these takbirs fall within the days of tashriq; according to Abu Hanifa none do, but the name still applies due to a minimal connection. Alternative explanations: tashriq refers to the Eid prayer (ishraq) or to the drying of sacrificial meat. The commentary also mentions that the fatwa on the Sahibayn's view is the practice in most regions and ages.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The specific takbir (Allahu Akbar) recited after fard prayers from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of Eid (or to end of tashriq according to the Sahibayn).
فور (fawr): Immediately after; the takbir must be recited right after the fard prayer without delay.
مصر (misr): A city or large town that has an imam and congregation; according to Abu Hanifa, the obligation of takbir on the imam is specific to a misr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, when does the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq end?
A) After Asr of Eid
B) After Fajr of Arafa
C) After Asr of the fifth day (end of tashriq)
D) At sunset of the third day

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer; the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn) extends it to all individuals from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of the 5th day.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Takbir al-Tashriq: Timing and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Introduces the ruling on the timing of wajib takbir and the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi position on the timing of Takbir al-Tashriq and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's view and that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The fatwa on Takbir al-Tashriq follows the Sahibayn: wajib from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the 13th.

The takbir that we recite after fard prayers during the Days of Tashriq is a well-known practice, but scholars differed about its exact timing. Within the Hanafi school, there is an important dispute between the founder Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson clarifies the ruling, its evidence, and why the view of the Sahibayn became the mufta bihi (operative position) for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi fatwa position
Identify the ruling held by the majority of the school: Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer, from Fajr of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) until Asr of the 13th (last day of Tashriq). Note that it applies to everyone—even those praying alone, traveling, or in a village.
This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Sahibayn).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Abu Hanifa held a different view: he limited the takbir to the day of Arafah only, so that no takbir occurs in the Days of Tashriq (11th–13th).
The text does not give Abu Hanifa's full proof, but it mentions the objection to the phrase 'takbir al-tashriq'.
3
Analyze the proof of the Sahibayn
Examine the Quranic verses cited: 'Remember Allah in the numbered days' (2:203) and 'Remember the name of Allah in the known days' (22:28). The Sahibayn interpret 'dhikr' as takbir, and the days extend through Tashriq. This is supported by practice of the companions and the fatwa of later scholars.
The Quranic texts are definitive in transmission (qat'i al-thubut) but speculative in meaning (zanni al-dalala), hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to Abu Hanifa's objection
The linguistic objection: if tashriq means 'takbir', then 'takbir al-tashriq' becomes 'takbir of takbir', which is invalid. The response: the addition is either explanatory (bayani) or specific-to-general, making it valid. Also, other meanings of tashriq (Eid prayer, drying meat) allow the phrase even on Abu Hanifa's view.
This shows that linguistic analysis can affect fiqh rulings.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: on Abu Hanifa's view, one stops after Maghrib of Arafah; on the fatwa, one continues until Asr of the 13th. The tarjih (preference) is given to the Sahibayn because of precaution (ihtiyat) and the widespread practice of Muslims across ages.
Numerous sources (ad-Dirayah, al-Mujtaba, etc.) affirm the fatwa on the Sahibayn's statement.

من المعلومات والمعدودات (٢)، فلما أمر الله تعالى بالذكر في هذه الأيام، ولم نجد ذكراً سوى التكبيرات فتجب، كذا في جامع الإسبيجاني»، وفيه وفي التحرير » و « الخلاصة »، و « المجتبى»، و «فتاوى العتابي : والفتوى على قولهما، وعلـيـه عـمـل الأمصار في أغلب الأعصار ، كذا في «معراج الدراية»، وفي ( السراج الوهاج»، و«الجوهرة»، وفي مجمع الروايات » ، قال الزاهدي والفتوى والعمل في عامة الأمصار على قولهما. :( تنبيه: قال في « الدراية و المستصفى هذه الإضافة في تكبير التشريق إنما تستقيم على قولهما؛ لأن بعض التكبيرات تقع في أيام التشريق عندهما، وعلى قول أبي حنيفة: لا يقع شيء من التكبير فيها فلا تستقيم الإضافة، لكن أدنى الملابسة كاف للإضافة، وقيل: التشريق اسم لصلاة العيد، لأنها تؤدى عند إشراق الشمس وارتفاعها، وقيل: التشريق عبارة عن هذه الأيام، لما فيها من تشريق لحوم الأضاحي، فعلى هذين تستقيم الإضافة على قوله انتهى وقال الكمال: الإضافة بيانية، أي: التكبير الذي هو التشريق، فإن التكبير لا يسمى تشريقاً إلا إذا كان بتلك الألفاظ في شيء مــــن الأيام المخصوصة، فهو حينئذ متفرع على قول الكل، وفي » الكافي»، و « الدراية » : ما يقتضي عدم ( صحة الإضافة الثانية التي هي على معنى التكبير ، لأنه ذكر في جواب الاعتراض على الاستدلال لأبي حنيفة، في اشتراط المصر للتكبير بالأثر الذي هو « لا جُمُعَةَ ولا تَشْرِيْقَ ولا أَضحَى إِلا فِي مَصْرٍ جَامِعٍ ) بأن هذا الدليل يستلزم أن الإضافة في تكبير التشريق معناها : تكبير التكبير، فـلا تصح الإضافة، وذلك أنه قال لإيضاح الدليل ما نصه: قال الخليل بن أحمد: التشريق التكبير، وإن كان مشتركاً بينه وبين تقديد اللحم، والقيام في المشرقة، كما نقله صاحب « الصحاح» وغيره، لـكـن هذان المعنيان، غير مختصين بالأمصار بالإجماع، فتعين الأول الذي هو التكبير، تفسيراً لقوله في الأثر : « ولا تشريق أي لا تكبير، وإن لم يتعين هذا التفسير يستلزم التكرار، والأصل عدمه انتهى. فاستلزم تفسير التشريق بالتكبير أن تكون الإضافة في قولنا : تكبير التشريق تكبير التكبير فلم يصح، قال الكمال: لكن الحق ،صحتها، على اعتبار إضافة الخاص إلى العام، مثل مسجد الـجــامـع وحركة الإعراب، فيجب اعتبارها كذلك تصحيحاً للإضافة، فلا يلزم ما قيل أن الإضافة على قولهما؛ لأن شيئاً من التكبير لا يقع في أيام التشريق عند أبي حنيفة، أو على قول الكل باعتبـار القـرب، وأيضاً إنما يلزم هذا الذي قد قيل: لو أضيف التكبير إلى أيام التشريق، وقد أضيف إلى التشريق نفسه، فلا يصح ما قيل، إلا إذا أُريد بالتشريق أيام التشريق، أو قدرت الأيام مقحمة بين المتضايفين، ولا داعي إليه، فتعين ما ذكرنا أنها إضافة خاص إلى عام انتهى
And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The takbir is obligatory immediately after every obligatory prayer upon the one who has prayed it, even if he is alone, or a traveler, or a villager, up to the Asr of the fifth day from the day of Arafah (i.e., the 13th of Dhul Hijjah). And by it (their statement) is action taken, and upon it is the fatwa. Consensus is established on the minimum, so taking the minimum is more precautionary. This is in ad-Dirayah from Jami' al-Kurdi. (And they said) meaning Abu Yusuf and Muhammad the takbir is obligatory immediately after every obligatory prayer upon the one who has prayed it, even if he is alone, or a traveler, or a villager, because it follows the obligatory prayer, from Fajr of Arafah until after the Asr of the fifth day from the day of Arafah, thus it lasts until the end of the Days of Tashriq. And by it (their statement) action is taken and the fatwa is given, because it is precautionary, since performing what is not upon one is better than leaving what is upon one, so taking the greater (time) is precautionary. And because Allah says: 'And remember Allah in the numbered days' and He said in another place: 'And remember the name of Allah in the known days.' The known days are the ten (first days) of Dhul Hijjah, and the numbered days are the Days of Tashriq. It is also said: the known days are the days of sacrifice, and the numbered days are the Days of Tashriq. They are called numbered because they are few. And thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: The first day is from the known days, and the middle two days are from both the known and the numbered. So when Allah commanded remembrance in these days, and we do not find any remembrance except the takbirs, they become obligatory. So in Jami' al-Isbijani, and in it and in at-Tahrir and al-Khulasah and al-Mujtaba and Fatawa al-Attabi: The fatwa is on their statement, and upon it is the practice of the cities in most ages. So in Miraj ad-Dirayah, and in as-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawharah, and in Majma' ar-Riwayat, az-Zahidi said: The fatwa and practice in most cities is on their statement. Cautionary note: He said in ad-Dirayah and al-Mustasfa: This addition in 'takbir at-tashriq' is only valid according to their statement, because some of the takbirs occur in the Days of Tashriq according to them, while according to Abu Hanifa, none of the takbirs occur in them, so the addition is not valid. But the least connection suffices for the addition. And it is said: At-Tashriq is the name for the Eid prayer because it is performed at the time of sunrise. And it is said: At-Tashriq refers to these days because of the slicing of the meat of sacrifices. According to these two (interpretations), the addition is valid according to his statement. End. And al-Kamal said: The addition is explanatory (bayaniyyah), i.e., the takbir which is at-tashriq, because the takbir is not called tashriq unless it is with those specific phrases in specific days, then it is derived from everyone's statement. In al-Kafi and ad-Dirayah, there is what indicates the invalidity of the second addition which is in the sense of takbir, because he mentioned in response to an objection against the proof for Abu Hanifa in the condition of a city for takbir based on the effect: 'No Jumu'ah, no Tashriq, no Adha except in a comprehensive city.' That this proof necessitates that the addition in 'takbir at-tashriq' means 'takbir of takbir', so the addition is invalid. And that is because he said to clarify the proof: Khalil ibn Ahmad said: At-Tashriq is the takbir, although it is shared between it and the slicing of meat and standing in the sun, as quoted by the author of as-Sihah and others, but these two meanings are not specific to cities by consensus, so the first meaning, which is takbir, is determined as an interpretation of his statement in the effect: 'Nor Tashriq' i.e., no takbir. If this interpretation is not determined, it necessitates repetition, and the original is no repetition. End. So interpreting tashriq as takbir entails that the addition in our statement 'takbir at-tashriq' is 'takbir of takbir', so it is not valid. Al-Kamal said: But the truth is its validity based on considering the addition of the specific to the general, like 'masjid al-jami'' and 'harakat al-i'rab', so it must be considered thus to correct the addition. Therefore, it does not necessitate what was said that the addition is according to their statement because none of the takbir falls in the Days of Tashriq according to Abu Hanifa, or according to everyone by considering proximity. Also, this objection only applies if the takbir is added to the Days of Tashriq, but it is added to tashriq itself, so the objection is invalid unless by 'tashriq' the days are meant, or the days are considered interpolated between the two components, and there is no need for that. So what we mentioned is confirmed: it is an addition of specific to general. End.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the ruling on Takbir al-Tashriq, which is the takbir recited after each fard prayer during the Days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The author states the position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that this takbir is wajib immediately after every fard prayer, from the Fajr of the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) until the Asr of the 13th (the last day of Tashriq). This applies to everyone: the one praying alone, the traveler, and the villager (i.e., not just the resident city dweller). They support this with a Quranic verse 'Remember Allah in the numbered days' and a hadith. The author notes that the fatwa is given on this view, and it is the practice in most regions. There is also an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa held a different view, apparently limiting the takbir to the day of Arafah only (so that no takbir falls in the Days of Tashriq). The passage then includes a long note (tanbih) discussing the linguistic phrase 'takbir al-tashriq' and its validity according to each imam, addressing objections. The commentary clarifies that the relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (Takbīr al-Tashrīq): The specific takbir recited after obligatory prayers during the Days of Tashriq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah).
التشريق (al-Tashrīq): Literally means 'slicing' or 'drying in the sun'; technically refers to the days of 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, or the takbir itself according to some.
فَوْرَ (fawra): Immediately after (the prayer), without delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, from which prayer does Takbir al-Tashriq begin and at which prayer does it end?
A) It begins after Fajr of Arafah and ends after Maghrib of the day of Arafah.
B) It begins after Fajr of Arafah and ends after Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
C) It begins after Fajr of the 10th and ends after Asr of the 12th.
D) It begins after Zuhr of Arafah and ends after Asr of the 13th.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib from Fajr of Arafah until Asr of the 13th, a view attributed to the Sahibayn and relied upon for fatwa due to precaution and widespread practice.

Takbir After Eid Prayers: Ruling and Formula
Ruling statement with formula and evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on takbir after Eid prayers and recite the recommended formula.

Core Idea
Takbir after Eid prayers is permissible and recommended, based on continuous practice.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the ruling on reciting takbir after the two Eid prayers. It confirms that this practice is not only permissible but also recommended, as it has been transmitted by the Muslim community. The text also provides the specific wording that should be recited, making it a memorization anchor for students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is reciting takbir after the Eid prayer. The text uses 'la ba's' (no harm), which in the Hanafi school indicates permissibility and often implies recommendation (istihbab).
Distinguish from wajib — the text does not use imperative language.
2
Memorize the formula
The exact wording is given: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahil hamd.' This is the transmitted form.
Variations exist, but this is the standard Hanafi formula.
3
Understand the evidence
The primary evidence is the continuous practice of the Muslims (tawāruth) and statements from early Hanafi scholars, including Abu Hanifa himself.
No explicit hadith is cited; the practice is based on communal transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بالتكبير عَقِبَ صلاة العيدين. والتَّكبيرُ أن يقول: اللهُ أَكْبَرُ، الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر، الله أكبر، ولله الحمد. قال في مبسوط أبي الليث : لا بأس به، لأن المسلمين توارثوا هكذا، وذكر الزاهدي: البلخيون يكبرون عقب العيد، لأنه يؤدى بجمع كالجمعة ، وفي ( الظهيرية» عــن الفقيه «أبـي جعفر » : سمعت أن مشايخنا كانوا يرون التكبير في الأسواق أيام العشر، كذا في « البحر »، و «شرح المقدسي»، وفي ( الدراية ) ، عن « جمع التفاريق : قيل لأبي حنيفة: ينبغي لأهل الكوفة وغيرها أن يكبروا أيام التشريق في الأسواق والمساجد؟ قال: نعم. وذكر « أبو الليث : وكان « إبراهيــم بــن يوسف» يفتي بالتكبير في الأسواق أيام العشر. قال الهنداوني: وعندي أنه لا ينبغي أن يمنع العامة ذلك، لقلة رغبتهم في الخير، وبه نأخذ كذا في ( المجتبى» .
And there is no harm in takbir after the two Eid prayers. The takbir is to say: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahil hamd. It is said in the Mabsut of Abu al-Layth: There is no harm in it because the Muslims have inherited this practice. And az-Zahidi mentioned: The Balkhites used to say takbir after Eid because it is performed with a congregation like Jumu'ah. In az-Zahiriyyah from the faqih Abu Ja'far: I heard that our mashayikh would see takbir in the markets during the ten days (of Dhul Hijjah). So in al-Bahr and Sharh al-Maqdisi. In ad-Dirayah from Jami' at-Tafariq: It was said to Abu Hanifa: Should the people of Kufah and others say takbir during the Days of Tashriq in the markets and mosques? He said: Yes. And Abu al-Layth mentioned: Ibrahim ibn Yusuf used to give fatwa of takbir in the markets during the ten days. Al-Hindawani said: According to me, they should not prevent the common people from that, due to their lack of desire for good, and this is what we take. So in al-Mujtaba.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah covers two points: (1) the ruling on reciting takbir after the two Eid prayers (Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha), and (2) the prescribed formula for the takbir. The text states that it is permissible (la ba'sa) to recite takbir after the Eid prayer, citing the practice of Muslims that has been transmitted. It then gives the formula: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahil hamd.' The author then quotes various sources that support the practice of takbir in the markets and during the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, including a direct statement from Abu Hanifa allowing it. The overall ruling is that takbir after Eid and during the Days of Tashriq is a sunnah practice and should not be discouraged.

Key Terms
لا بأس (lā ba'sa): There is no harm; it is permissible (jā'iz). In the Hanafi school, this often indicates a recommended act or one that is not disliked.
صلاة العيدين (ṣalāt al-‘īdayn): The two Eid prayers: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
التكبير (al-takbīr): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar'; here specifically the formula recited after prayers and during Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Takbir after Eid prayers is a recommended practice with a transmitted formula, based on communal practice and Hanafi authority.

Ruling on Takbir After Eid Prayers and Its Wording
Explains the permissibility and wording of takbir after Eid prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on takbir after Eid prayers in the Hanafi school, recite its prescribed wording, and explain the evidence from the Prophet and Companions.

Core Idea
Takbir after Eid is sunnah; its wording is two takbirs followed by tahlil and tahmid, as transmitted from the Prophet.

After the joy of Eid prayer, Muslims often raise their voices in takbir. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this practice, its exact wording, and the proof from the sunnah. We will also address a common misunderstanding about the phrase 'takbir al-tashriq' and why two takbirs is the established formula.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by stating 'There is no harm (la ba's) in takbir after the two Eid prayers.' This indicates permissibility, but given the widespread practice and evidence, the Hanafi school considers it sunnah (recommended). Recognize that 'la ba's' in fiqh often implies approval, not mere permission.
The author later cites that Muslims have inherited this practice, elevating it to sunnah.
2
Recite the prescribed wording
The text specifies the wording: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd.' Note that it consists of two takbirs, not three, followed by the shahadah and two more takbirs ending with praise.
This formula is directly attributed to the Prophet on the Day of Arafah (hadith from Ibn Umar).
3
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'The best of what I said and the prophets said before me on the Day of Arafah is: Allahu Akbar...' (narrated by Ibn Umar and others). The Prophet's statement indicates the virtue of this supplication, and the Companions' consistent practice confirms it as sunnah.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is at the level of sunnah, not wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf about the wording
The passage explicitly rejects the view of those who say three takbirs in the first part, stating 'whoever makes the takbirs three in the first has no proof for it.' The Hanafi position relies on the transmitted two-takbir formula.
The grammatical discussion about 'takbir al-tashriq' defends the validity of the phrase even if 'tashriq' means takbir, using the principle of idafat al-khas ila al-amm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بالتكبير عَقِبَ صلاة العيدين. والتَّكبيرُ أن يقول: اللهُ أَكْبَرُ، الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر، الله أكبر، ولله الحمد
صحة الإضافة الثانية التي هي على معنى التكبير ، لأنه ذكر في جواب الاعتراض على الاستدلال لأبي حنيفة، في اشتراط المصر للتكبير بالأثر الذي هو « لا جُمُعَةَ ولا تَشْرِيْقَ ولا أَضحَى إِلا فِي مَصْرٍ جَامِعٍ ) بأن هذا الدليل يستلزم أن الإضافة في تكبير التشريق معناها : تكبير التكبير، فـلا تصح الإضافة، وذلك أنه قال لإيضاح الدليل ما نصه: قال الخليل بن أحمد: التشريق التكبير، وإن كان مشتركاً بينه وبين تقديد اللحم، والقيام في المشرقة، كما نقله صاحب « الصحاح» وغيره، لـكـن هذان المعنيان، غير مختصين بالأمصار بالإجماع، فتعين الأول الذي هو التكبير، تفسيراً لقوله في الأثر : « ولا تشريق أي لا تكبير، وإن لم يتعين هذا التفسير يستلزم التكرار، والأصل عدمه انتهى. فاستلزم تفسير التشريق بالتكبير أن تكون الإضافة في قولنا : تكبير التشريق تكبير التكبير فلم يصح، قال الكمال: لكن الحق ،صحتها، على اعتبار إضافة الخاص إلى العام، مثل مسجد الجامع وحركة الإعراب، فيجب اعتبارها كذلك تصحيحاً للإضافة، فلا يلزم ما قيل أن الإضافة على قولهما؛ لأن شيئاً من التكبير لا يقع في أيام التشريق عند أبي حنيفة، أو على قول الكل باعتبار القرب، وأيضاً إنما يلزم هذا الذي قد قيل: لو أضيف التكبير إلى أيام التشريق، وقد أضيف إلى التشريق نفسه، فلا يصح ما قيل، إلا إذا أُريد بالتشريق أيام التشريق، أو قدرت الأيام مقحمة بين المتضايفين، ولا داعي إليه، فتعين ما ذكرنا أنها إضافة خاص إلى عام انتهى ولا بأس بالتكبير عقب صلاة العيدين) قال في مبسوط أبي الليث : لا بأس به، لأن المسلمين توارثوا هكذا، وذكر الزاهدي: البلخيون يكبرون عقب العيد، لأنه يؤدى بجمع كالجمعة ، وفي ( الظهيرية» عن الفقيه «أبي جعفر » : سمعت أن مشايخنا كانوا يرون التكبير في الأسواق أيام العشر، كذا في « البحر »، و «شرح المقدسي»، وفي ( الدراية ) ، عن « جمع التفاريق : قيل لأبي حنيفة: ينبغي لأهل الكوفة وغيرها أن يكبروا أيام التشريق في الأسواق والمساجد؟ قال: نعم. وذكر « أبو الليث : وكان « إبراهيم بن يوسف» يفتي بالتكبير في الأسواق أيام العشر. قال الهنداوني: وعندي أنه لا ينبغي أن يمنع العامة ذلك، لقلة رغبتهم في الخير، وبه نأخذ كذا في ( المجتبى» . ( والتَّكبيرُ أنْ يقول: اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، اللَّهُ أكبر) فهما مرتان ( لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر، الله أكبر ولله الحمد ، لما قال في « الدراية» عن ابن عمر أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال أفضَلُ مَا قُلْتُ وَقَالَتِ الأنْبِيَاءُ قَبْلى يَوْمَ عَرَفَة : اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد ) (۱) وعن جابر أنه صلى الفجر يوم عرفة، وكبر هكذا)، وفي «مجمع الروايات»: روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى صلاة الغداة يوم عرفة، ثم أقبل على أصحابه بوجهه، فقال: « خير ما قلنا وقالت الأنبياء قبلنا في يومنا هذا الله أكبر، الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر، الله أكبر ولله الحمد ) (۳) انتهى. وفي « الهداية » : هذا هو المأثور عن الخليل، قيل : أصل ذلك لما روي أن جبريل لما جاء بالقربان خاف العجلة على إبراهيم فقال: الله أكبر الله أكبر، فلما رآه إبراهيم قال: لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر، كذا في ( العناية»، وقال الكمال: قوله في « الهداية » : وهو مأثور عن الخليل، لم يثبت عند أهل الحديث ذلك، وقد تقدم مأثوراً عن علي وابن مسعود كانا يقولان ذلك عند ابن أبي شيبة ) ، وسنده جيد، ثم عمم عن الصحابة، وقال: كانوا يكبرون يوم عرفة وأحدهم مستقبل القبلة في الصلاة: الله أكبر الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر، والله الحمد ) ، ومن جعل التكبيرات ثلاثاً في الأول لا ثبت له انتهى. وقال في «مجمع الروايات » : ويزيد على هذا إن شاء ويقول: الله أكبر كبيراً، والحمد الله كثيراً، وسبحان الله بكرة وأصيلاً، لا إله إلا الله وحده، صدق وعده ونصر عبده وهزم الأحزاب وحده، لا إله إلا الله، ولا نعبد إلا إياه مخلصين له الدين، ولو كره الكافرون، اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد، وعلى أصحاب محمد ، وعلى أزواج من محمد وسلم تسليماً، انتهى.
There is no harm in saying takbir after the two Eid prayers. And the takbir is to say: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd. The validity of the second idafah (construct phrase) which is upon the meaning of takbir; because it was mentioned in response to an objection against the proof for Abu Hanifa, in restricting the takbir to a populous city by the hadith 'There is no Jumu'ah, no Tashriq, and no Adha except in a populous city' – that this proof necessitates that the idafah in 'takbir al-tashriq' means 'takbir of takbir', so the idafah is not valid. And he said to clarify the proof: al-Khalil ibn Ahmad said: al-Tashriq is takbir, even if it is homonymous between it and slicing meat, and standing in the sunshine, as transmitted by the author of al-Sihah and others, but these two meanings are not specific to cities by consensus, so the first meaning – takbir – is determined as the interpretation of his statement in the hadith 'and no Tashriq' i.e., no takbir. And if this interpretation is not determined, it would necessitate repetition, and the principle is its absence, end. So the interpretation of tashriq as takbir necessitated that the idafah in our saying 'takbir al-tashriq' is 'takbir of takbir', so it became invalid. Al-Kamal said: But the truth is its validity, on the basis of adding the specific to the general, like 'masjid al-jami'' and 'harakat al-i'rab', so it must be considered thus to correct the idafah. Therefore what is said is not necessary – that the idafah is upon their statement; because no part of takbir occurs during the days of Tashriq according to Abu Hanifa, or upon the statement of all by considering closeness. Also, this which is said would only be necessary if takbir were added to the days of Tashriq, but it is added to Tashriq itself, so what is said is not correct, unless Tashriq means the days of Tashriq, or the days are considered inserted between the two parts of the construct, and there is no need for that. So what we mentioned is determined: that it is an idafah of specific to general, end. And there is no harm in takbir after the two Eid prayers. He said in Mabsut Abi al-Layth: there is no harm in it, because the Muslims have inherited it thus. And al-Zahidi mentioned: the Balkhians say takbir after Eid because it is performed with a congregation like Jumu'ah. And in al-Zahiriyyah from al-Faqih Abi Ja'far: I heard that our mashayikh used to consider takbir in the markets during the days of the ten (i.e., first ten days of Dhul Hijjah). Similarly in al-Bahr, and Sharh al-Maqdisi, and in al-Dirayah, from Jami' al-Tafariq: It was said to Abu Hanifa: Should the people of Kufah and others say takbir during the days of Tashriq in the markets and mosques? He said: Yes. And Abu al-Layth mentioned: Ibrahim ibn Yusuf used to give fatwa for takbir in the markets during the days of the ten. Al-Hindawani said: In my view, the common people should not be prevented from that, due to their lack of desire for good, and with it we take, as in al-Mujtaba. And the takbir is to say: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar (twice), La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd, because it is said in al-Dirayah from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best of what I said and the prophets said before me on the Day of Arafah is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd.' And from Jabir that he prayed Fajr on the Day of Arafah and said takbir like this. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed the morning prayer on the Day of Arafah, then turned to his companions and said: 'The best of what we said and the prophets said before us on this day of ours is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd.' End. And in al-Hidayah: This is what is transmitted from al-Khalil (Abraham). It is said the origin is that when Jibril came with the sacrifice, he feared hasting upon Ibrahim, so he said: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar. When Ibrahim saw him, he said: La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar. So in al-Inayah. And al-Kamal said: His statement in al-Hidayah 'and it is transmitted from al-Khalil' is not established among hadith scholars. And what is transmitted from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that they used to say that, as in Ibn Abi Shaybah, and its chain is good. Then he generalized from the Companions and said: They used to say takbir on the Day of Arafah, one of them facing the qiblah in prayer: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd. And whoever makes the takbirs three in the first has no proof for it, end. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: One may add upon this if he wishes and say: Allahu Akbar kabira, walhamdu lillahi kathira, wa subhanallahi bukratan wa asila, la ilaha illallahu wahdahu, sadaqa wa'dahu wa nasara 'abdahu wa hazama al-ahzaba wahdahu, la ilaha illallah, wa la na'budu illa iyyahu mukhlisina lahu al-din, wa law kariha al-kafirun. Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala ali Muhammad wa 'ala ashabi Muhammad wa 'ala azwaji Muhammad wa sallim tasliman. End.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah explains the ruling and wording of the takbir recited after the Eid prayers. The author begins by stating that it is permissible (la ba's) to say takbir after the Eid prayers, and then specifies the well-known wording: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Walillahil hamd. The text then delves into a lengthy grammatical discussion concerning the construct phrase 'takbir al-tashriq' (the takbir of Tashriq). This is in response to an objection against Imam Abu Hanifa's use of the hadith 'There is no Jumu'ah, no Tashriq, and no Adha except in a populous city (misr jami')' to prove that the takbir of Tashriq is confined to a city. The objection was that if 'tashriq' means takbir, then the phrase 'takbir al-tashriq' would be 'takbir of takbir,' which is nonsensical. The author clarifies, following al-Kamal, that the construct is valid as a specification of the general (idafat al-khas ila al-'amm), analogous to 'masjid al-jami'' (the congregational mosque). He then returns to the main ruling, citing various authorities such as Abu al-Layth, al-Zahidi, and others who affirm the practice of takbir after Eid and during the days of Tashriq. The passage also provides the textual evidence for the wording from the Prophet (peace be upon him) narrated by Ibn Umar and Jabir, as well as from the Companions. Finally, an expanded formula from Majma' al-Riwayat is mentioned, which includes additional praises and salawat upon the Prophet. The passage concludes by affirming that the transmitted wording is two takbirs, not three, as some may claim.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): The act of saying 'Allahu Akbar'; here specifically the phrase recited after Eid prayers and during the days of Tashriq.
التشريق (al-tashriq): The days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah); also interpreted as 'takbir' in some contexts.
الإضافة (al-idafah): Grammatical construct phrase; here discussed regarding the phrase 'takbir al-tashriq' and its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on saying takbir after the Eid prayer?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible but not rewarded)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
Takbir after Eid is a confirmed sunnah with a specific two-takbir wording transmitted from the Prophet, and any departure from this wording lacks established proof.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Takbir on the Day of Arafah: Recommended Formulations
Discussion of recommended takbir formulations on the day of Arafah with proofs and scholarly evaluation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended formulation of takbir on the day of Arafah according to the Hanafi school and identify the proofs and scholarly disagreements regarding its wording.

Core Idea
The sunnah takbir on Arafah begins with two 'Allahu akbar', then the shahada, then two more 'Allahu akbar', and ends with praise.

The day of Arafah is a day of heightened worship. Among the Sunnah practices is the recitation of a specific takbir formulation. This lesson examines the evidence for this practice, the exact wording preferred by the Hanafi school, and the scholarly discussion regarding its origin and variations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? (Takbir on the day of Arafah). What is its hukm level according to the Hanafi school? The text indicates it is sunnah, not wajib.
Look for the author's statements on recommendation versus obligation.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith quoted from Jabir and the narration from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud. These form the basis for the recommended formulation.
The hadith is ahad (single-chained) and thus zanni, leading to sunnah rather than fard.
3
Analyze the critique of the Abrahamic attribution
The text mentions that some attribute the takbir to Prophet Ibrahim (al-Khalil). Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam critiques this, stating that hadith scholars do not find it established. Note the shift to the Companion report.
This shows the Hanafi method of preferring authentic Companion transmissions over weak Isra'iliyyat-like stories.
4
Recognize the flexibility in wording
The passage from Majma' al-Riwayat allows optional additional praises after the core takbir. Also, it warns that making the takbirs three in the first part has no proof.
The sunnah formulation is fixed but additional dhikr is permissible.
5
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the wording transmitted from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud, as preferred by al-Kamal and supported by the author. This includes two takbirs at the start.
The tarjih authority is al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.

(۱) مروي بألفاظ متباينة منها ما أخرجه الترمذي في الدعوات، باب في دعاء يوم عرفة (٣٥٨٥)، قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: (خير الدعاء دعاء يوم عرفة، وخير ما قلت أنا والنبيون من قبلي لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد وهو على كل شيء قدير ».
