Allah is the Greatest, there is no god but Allah, Allah is the Greatest, Allah is the Greatest, and to Allah belongs all praise. (1) And from Jabir that he prayed Fajr on the day of Arafah and said the takbir like this. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: It is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, prayed the morning prayer on the day of Arafah, then turned his face to his companions and said: 'The best of what we and the prophets before us have said on this day of ours is: Allah is the Greatest, Allah is the Greatest, there is no god but Allah, and Allah is the Greatest, Allah is the Greatest, and to Allah belongs all praise.' (3) End. And in al-Hidayah: This is the well-known (mashur) from al-Khalil (Abraham). It is said that the origin of this is that when Gabriel came with the sacrifice, he feared haste for Abraham and said: Allah is the Greatest, Allah is the Greatest. When Abraham saw him, he said: There is no god but Allah, and Allah is the Greatest. Thus in al-Inayah. And al-Kamal said: His statement in al-Hidayah: 'It is well-known from al-Khalil' is not established with the hadith scholars. And it has been transmitted earlier from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that they used to say that in the work of Ibn Abi Shaybah, and its chain is good. Then he generalized from the Companions and said: They used to say the takbir on the day of Arafah, one of them facing the qiblah in prayer: 'Allah is the Greatest, Allah is the Greatest, there is no god but Allah, and Allah is the Greatest, Allah is the Greatest, and to Allah belongs all praise.' And whoever makes the takbirs three in the first has no proof for it. End. And he said in Majma' al-Riwayat: And one may add to this if he wishes and say: 'Allah is Greatest, great, and all praise is for Allah, much, and glory be to Allah morning and evening. There is no god but Allah alone, He fulfilled His promise, supported His servant, and single-handedly defeated the confederates. There is no god but Allah, and we worship none but Him, making religion sincerely for Him, even if the disbelievers dislike it. O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, and upon the companions of Muhammad, and upon the wives of Muhammad, and grant abundant peace.' End. [margin?] (1) It is reported with varying wordings, including what al-Tirmidhi recorded in al-Da'awat, chapter on supplication on the day of Arafah (3585): The Prophet said: 'The best of supplications is the supplication of the day of Arafah, and the best of what I and the prophets before me have said is: La ilaha illallah wahdahu la sharika lahu, lahul mulku wa lahul hamdu wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir.' (2) Recorded by al-Daraqutni in his Sunan (0/1). (3) Preceded from the narration of Jabir in the previous hadith. (4) Al-Zayla'i said in Nasb al-Rayah (2/224): 'This well-known from al-Khalil, peace be upon him, I did not find it.' (5) Recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah in his Musannaf (1/488). (6) Mentioned by al-Zayla'i in Nasb al-Rayah (2/224).

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) discusses the recommended formulation of the takbir on the day of Arafah. The author begins by quoting a narration from Jabir that the Prophet prayed Fajr on Arafah and recited a specific takbir. Then from Majma' al-Riwayat, another narration has the Prophet turning to his companions after the morning prayer and teaching them the best supplication for that day, which includes the takbir. The passage then refers to al-Hidayah, which states that this takbir is well-known (mashur) from Prophet Ibrahim (al-Khalil), and provides a story about Gabriel and Ibrahim as its origin. However, al-Kamal ibn al-Humam (al-Kamal) critiques this attribution, noting that hadith scholars do not consider it established. He mentions that the takbir is authentically transmitted from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud through Ibn Abi Shaybah. The narrator then generalizes that the Companions used to say the takbir facing the qiblah on Arafah. The passage also warns against adding a third 'Allahu akbar' in the first part, as that has no proof. Finally, from Majma' al-Riwayat, additional optional wording is given, including extended praise and salah upon the Prophet. The footnotes provide source references and critical evaluations. Overall, the text clarifies the sunnah practice of takbir on Arafah and its established wording.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): The act of saying 'Allahu akbar' (Allah is the Greatest). In this passage, it refers to the specific formulation on the day of Arafah.
مأثور (ma'thur): Well-known from previous practice, i.e., transmitted from the Prophet or earlier prophets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunnah takbir on Arafah is: Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illallah, wallahu akbar, Allahu akbar, walillahil hamd, with optional additional praise.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Ruling and Procedure of the Eclipse Prayer
Explanation of the ruling and manner of the eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the eclipse prayer, identify its conditions and procedure, and explain the evidence and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is a confirmed sunnah, two rak'ahs like nafl, performed silently in congregation only with the imam or his deputy.

The eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a non-obligatory prayer that becomes sunnah when a solar or lunar eclipse occurs. The Hanafi school has a specific procedure: two rak'ahs with one bowing per rak'ah, without extra bowing, adhan, iqamah, or sermon, and only in congregation with the Friday imam or his appointee. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the ruling, the evidence from hadith, and addresses disputes within the school and from scholars who considered it wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling level
The text states 'سن ركعتان' (two rak'ahs sunnah). Confirm that the eclipse prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, based on the Hanafi position. Note the counter-claim from al-Asrar who argued for obligation.
The author refutes the obligation view by citing consensus and interpreting the command as recommendation.
2
Determine the conditions for congregation
The prayer is performed in congregation only with the Friday imam or a deputy appointed by the authority. This is to avoid fitnah. Without these, one prays individually.
This condition differentiates it from other nafl prayers that are normally performed individually.
3
Outline the procedure
Two rak'ahs like nafl (one bowing per rak'ah), silent recitation (according to Abu Hanifa), no adhan, no iqamah, no sermon. The evidence includes the hadith where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs and instructed to pray like the most recent obligatory prayer (Fajr).
The dispute on recitation: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani held it should be aloud; Abu Hanifa said silent. The author follows Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The primary evidence is the hadith 'When you see these signs, hasten to prayer' (Abu Dawud). The Hanafi school interprets the command (amr) as for recommendation (nadb) due to the context and consensus of the Companions. The hadith also shows the prayer was two rak'ahs without extra bowing.
The dalil is ahad (zanni thubut) and its indication (dalala) is zanni as well, so it does not produce obligation.
5
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
There are two main disputes: (1) Silent vs aloud recitation between Abu Hanifa and the two companions. (2) Whether the prayer is wajib (as argued by al-Asrar for solar eclipse) or sunnah. The text rejects the wajib view based on consensus.
The mufta bihi is the sunnah position with silent recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الكسوف والخسوف والأفزاع
سن ركعتانِ كهيئةِ النَّفْلِ، للكُسُوفِ بإمامِ الجمعةِ، أو مأمورِ السُّلطانِ بلا أذان ولا إقامة، ولا جَهْرٍ، وَلا خُطبةٍ
باب صلاة الكسوف والخسوف والأفزاع
الإضافة على نوعين : إضافة تعريف، وإضافة تقييد، فكلما كانت الماهية كاملة فيه تكون إضافته للتعريف، وما كانت ماهيته ناقصة فإضافته للتقييد، نظير الأول: ماء البئر وصلاة الكسوف،
ونظير الثاني: ماء الباقلاء، وصلاة الجنازة، كذا في مجمع الروايات»، وهو من قبيل إضافة الشيء إلى سببه لأن سببها الكسوف وهي سنة ، واختار في ( الأسرار وجوبها، للأمر في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « إِذَا رَأَيْتُمْ شَيْئَاً مِنْ هَذِهِ فَافْزَعُوا إِلَى الصَّلاةِ » ) والظاهر أن الأمر للندب، وعليه إجماع من سوى بعض الأصحاب، ثم من أوجبها منهم قيل : إنما أوجبها للشمس دون القمر، وهـو محـجـوج بالإجماع قبله فلذا قلنا: (سن ركعتان كهيئةِ النَّفْلِ) من غير زيادة ركوع فيهما، لما رواه أبو داود عن قبيصة بإسناد صحيح أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلي ركعتين فأطال فيهما القيام، ثـم انـصـرف وانجلت الشمس، فقال: « إنما هذه الآيات يخوِّفُ الله تعالى بها عبادَهُ فإذا رأيتُمُوهَا فَصَلُّوا كَأَحْدَثِ صَلَاةٍ صَلَّيْتُمُوهَا مِنَ المَكْتُوبَةِ » (۳)، كذا في « التبيين ) ، وروى الكمال أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « إِنَّ نَاسَاً يَزْعُمُونَ أَنَّ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ لا يَنْكَسِفَانِ إِلا لِمَوْتِ عَظِيمٍ مِنْ العُظَمَاءِ وَلَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ، إِنَّ الشَّمْسَ والقَمَرَ لَا يَنْكَسِفَانِ لِمَوْتِ أَحَدٍ وَلَا لِحَيَاتِهِ، وَلَكَنَّهُمَا آيَتَانِ مِنْ آيَاتِ اللَّهِ، إِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا بَدَا لِشَيْءٍ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ خَشعَ لَهُ، فَإِذَا رَأَيْتُمْ ذَلِكَ فَصَلُّوا كَأَحْدَثِ صَلَاةٍ صَلَّيْتُمُوهَا مِنَ المَكْتُوبَةِ » (٣) ثم قال الكمال:
(۳)
فهذه أحاديث منها الصحيح ومنها الحسن، قد دارت على ثلاث أمور ، منها : مـا فـيـه أنه صلى ركعتين، ومنها: الأمر بأن يجعلوها كأحدث ما صلوه من المكتوبات وهي الصبح، فإن كسوف الشمس كان عند ارتفاعها قدر رمحين، فأفاد أنَّ السنة ركعتان، ومنها : ما فصل فأفاد تفصيلـه أنـهـا بركوع واحد في كل ركعة (للكُسُوفِ)، ولا جماعة فيها إلا بإمام الجمعة، أو مأمور السلطان) دفعاً للفتنة، فيصليهما (بلا أذان ولا إقامة، ولا جَهْر ) في القراءة فيهما عنده خلافاً لهما، (ولا خطبة) بإجماع أصحابنا، كما في ( الجوهرة»، لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بالصلاة، ولم يأمر
Chapter on the prayer of solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, and terrifying events. Two rak'ahs sunnah, like the supererogatory prayer, for the eclipse, with the Friday imam or the authority's deputy, without call to prayer or iqamah, without audible recitation, and without a sermon. Chapter on the prayer of solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, and terrifying events. The idafa (construct phrase) is of two types: idafa of definition and idafa of qualification. Whenever the essence is complete in it, its idafa is for definition; and whenever its essence is deficient, its idafa is for qualification. The analogy of the first: water of the well and solar eclipse prayer. The analogy of the second: bean water and funeral prayer. Thus in Majma' al-Riwayat. It is of the type of adding something to its cause, because its cause is the eclipse and it is sunnah. But in al-Asrar, he opted for its obligation due to the command in his statement, peace be upon him: 'When you see something of these, then hasten to prayer.' And the apparent meaning is that the command is for recommendation, and there is consensus on that except for some companions. Then those who made it obligatory among them, it is said that they only made it obligatory for the sun, not the moon, but it is refuted by the consensus before that. Therefore we said: (Two rak'ahs sunnah, like the supererogatory prayer) without increasing bowing in them, because Abu Dawud narrated on the authority of Qabisah with a sound chain that the Prophet, peace be upon him, prayed two rak'ahs and lengthened the standing, then he left and the sun had cleared, so he said: 'These signs are only that Allah frightens His servants thereby. So when you see them, pray as if you are praying the most recent obligatory prayer you have prayed.' Thus in al-Tabyin. And al-Kamal narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'People claim that the sun and moon only eclipse because of the death of a great person, but it is not so. Indeed, the sun and moon do not eclipse for anyone's death or life, but they are two of Allah's signs. When Allah manifests something of His creation, it is humbled before Him. So when you see that, pray as if you are praying the most recent obligatory prayer you have prayed.' Then al-Kamal said: (3) So these hadiths, among them authentic and among them good, revolve around three matters. Among them: that he prayed two rak'ahs. And among them: the command to make it like the most recent obligatory prayer they have prayed, which is the dawn prayer, because the solar eclipse occurred at the height of two spear-lengths. So it indicates that the sunnah is two rak'ahs. And among them: what detailed and indicated that they have one bowing in each rak'ah. (For the eclipse) And there is no congregation in it except with the Friday imam or the authority's deputy, to prevent fitnah. So he prays them without call to prayer or iqamah, and without audible recitation according to him, contrary to them (the two companions), and without a sermon by consensus of our companions, as in al-Jawharah, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, commanded prayer and did not command (anything else).
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the chapter of eclipse prayer. It begins by stating the ruling: two rak'ahs sunnah, like nafl prayer, performed for the eclipse (both solar and lunar) with the Friday imam or his deputy, without adhan, iqamah, audible recitation, or sermon. The author then discusses the grammatical idafa (construct phrase) 'prayer of eclipse' as a definitional idafa, contrasting it with 'prayer of funeral' which is qualifying. The eclipse prayer is sunnah according to the authoritative Hanafi position, though al-Asrar considered it wajib based on the command in the hadith 'hasten to prayer.' However, the author clarifies that the command is for recommendation, citing consensus. The hadith evidence includes Abu Dawud's narration from Qabisah showing the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs without extra bowing, and the instruction to pray as if it were the most recent obligatory prayer (Fajr). Al-Kamal adds that the sunnah is two rak'ahs with one bowing per rak'ah. Congregation is limited to the Friday imam or his appointee to avoid fitnah. Recitation is not aloud according to Abu Hanifa (contrary to his two companions). There is no sermon, by ijma' of the Hanafi school. The footnotes provide further hadith references.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse. In this context, it refers to the event that occasions the prayer.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse. Treated the same as kusuf in the Hanafi school.
فزع (faza'): Terrifying events (such as earthquakes, eclipses) that prompt the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Fard kifayah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The eclipse prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, two rak'ahs like nafl, performed silently in congregation only with the Friday imam or his deputy, without adhan, iqamah, or sermon.

The Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Eclipse Prayer
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eclipse prayer and evaluate the evidence for the sunnah vs wajib dispute.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is sunnah, not wajib; the command is for recommendation, upheld by Hanafi consensus.

In this passage from Imdad al-Fattah, the author addresses the ruling on the eclipse prayer. While some earlier Hanafi scholars deemed it obligatory, the relied-upon position is that it is an emphasized sunnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
The passage opens by stating that two rak'ahs in the manner of nafl are sunnah for the eclipse prayer. Note the phrase 'سن ركعتان كهيئة النفل'.
This sets the default position.
2
Understand the grammatical classification
The author discusses the construct 'صلاة الكسوف' as an idafat ta'rif (definitive addition) because the reality of the prayer is complete, like 'ماء البئر'. This indicates the prayer is a well-defined sunnah.
Not directly related to dispute but frames the discussion.
3
Locate the dispute
The author mentions that in Al-Asrar, some scholars chose obligation (wujub) based on the command 'افزعوا إلى الصلاة'. Identify the opposing argument.
This is the key intra-Hanafi difference.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith 'When you see any of these, hurry to prayer' is cited. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) can indicate either obligation or recommendation. The context and other hadith show it is for recommendation.
Focus on the principle of interpreting amr.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author argues that the consensus of most Hanafi scholars (except a few) is that the prayer is sunnah. He also cites the Prophet's action of praying two rak'ahs without extra ruku', which is like nafl.
Consensus (ijma') and prophetic practice override the literal command.

Source Text

باب صلاة الكسوف والخسوف والأفزاع

فهذه أحاديث منها الصحيح ومنها الحسن، قد دارت على ثلاث أمور ، منها : مـا فـيـه أنه صلى ركعتين، ومنها: الأمر بأن يجعلوها كأحدث ما صلوه من المكتوبات وهي الصبح، فإن كسوف الشمس كان عند ارتفاعها قدر رمحين، فأفاد أنَّ السنة ركعتان، ومنها : ما فصل فأفاد تفصيلـه أنـهـا بركوع واحد في كل ركعة (للكُسُوفِ)، ولا جماعة فيها إلا بإمام الجمعة، أو مأمور السلطان) دفعاً للفتنة، فيصليهما (بلا أذان ولا إقامة، ولا جَهْر ) في القراءة فيهما عنده خلافاً لهما، (ولا خطبة) بإجماع أصحابنا، كما في ( الجوهرة»، لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بالصلاة، ولم يأمر بالخطبة، ولو كانت مشروعة لبينها ، قاله الزيلعي : (بل يُنادَى الصَّلاةَ جامعة) [ ليجتمعوا ] إن لم يكونوا اجتمعوا كما في «الفتح». وسُنَّ تطويلُهما ) وهو الأفضل لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام فعله لحديث عائشة قالت: «حزرتُ قِرَاءتَهُ أنَّه قَرَأ سُورَةَ البَقَرَةِ، وَلَو جَهَرَ سَمِعْتُ مَا حَزرتُ ) (۲)، فيقرأ في الأولى سورة البقرة إن حفظها، أو ما يعدلها إن لم يحفظها ، وفي الثانية آل عمران أو مـا يعدلها، ويجوز تطويل القراءة وتخفيف الدعاء وبالقلب، فإذا خفف أحدهما طول الآخر، لأن المستحب أن يبقى على الخشوع والخوف إلى انجلاء الشمس قال الكمال: وهذا مستثنى من كراهة تطويل الإمام الصلاة، ولو خففها جاز ولا يكون مخالفاً للسنة، لأن المسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلاة والدعاء انتهى. (و) سُن (تطويلُ رُكُوعِهما وسجودِهما ) لما روي عن عبد الله بن عـمـرو بـن العاص قال: انكسفتِ الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم « فقام عليه الصلاة والسلام، فَلَمْ يَرْكَعْ، ثُمَّ رَكَعَ، فَلَمْ يَكَدْ يَرْفَعُ ثُمَّ رَفَعَ، فَلَمْ يَكَدْ يَسْجُدُ، ثُمَّ سَجَدَ، فَلَمْ يَكَدْ يَرْفَعُ، وَفَعَلَ فِي الرَّكْعَةِ الأُخْرَى مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ ) أخرجه الحاكم وصححه، ثمَّ يدعو الإمامُ) عطف : لأن السنة في الأدعية تأخيرها الصلاة، فيدعو الإمام بعدها جالساً مُستقبِلَ القِبلةِ إِنْ شاءَ، أو يدعو (قائماً مستقبل الناس) قال شمس الأئمة ( الحلواني» : ( وهو أحسنُ من استقباله القبلة، ولو قام ودعا معتمداً على عصا أو قوس كان أيضاً حسناً، كذا في «الفتح»، ولا يصعد الإمام المنبر للدعاء ولا يخرج، كذا في البحر » عن « المحيط»، (وَ) إذا دعا على أي حال كان يُؤَمِّنُونَ على دعائه) ويستمرون، كذلك ( حتَّى يَكْمُلَ انْجِلاءُ الشَّمسِ) كما في «الجوهرة» . ( وإن لم يحضُرِ الإمامُ، صَلوا) أي: الناس (فرادى) ركعتين أو أربعاً، كما في شرح الكنز لملا مسكين انتهى، في منازلهم، كذا في ( شــرح الطحاوي»، لأن المقصود هو الرجوع إلى الله تعالى، والإخلاص، كذا في « مجمـع الـروايــات»، ( ك ) أداء صلاة ( الخُسُوفِ ) فرادى لأنه قد خسف القمر في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مراراً، ولم ينقل إلينا أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام جمع الناس له، ولأن الجمع العظيم بالليل سبب للفتنة، وكسوف القمر: ذهاب ضوءه، والخسوف: ذهاب دائرته، والحكم أعم.
Chapter of prayer for solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, and terrors. Two rak'ahs are sunnah, in the manner of nafl, for the solar eclipse with the imam of Jumu'ah or the one appointed by the sultan, without adhan, iqamah, audible recitation, or sermon. The addition is of two types: definitive addition and restrictive addition... and he chose in Al-Asrar its obligation, due to the command in his saying: 'When you see any of these, hurry to prayer.' The apparent meaning is that the command is for recommendation, and there is consensus upon that except some companions. Then those who made it obligatory, it is said they only obligated it for the sun not the moon, and that is refuted by the consensus before him. So we said: two rak'ahs are sunnah in the manner of nafl, without extra bowings in them... and it is sunnah to prolong them, to prolong their bowings and prostrations. Then the imam makes supplication sitting facing the qibla if he wishes, or standing facing the people, and that is better. They say amin to his supplication until the sun fully appears. If the imam is not present, they pray individually, like the lunar eclipse.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on eclipse prayers. The author begins by stating the ruling: praying two rak'ahs in the manner of nafl for the solar eclipse is sunnah, performed in congregation only with the Jumu'ah imam or the sultan's appointee, without adhan, iqamah, audible recitation, or sermon. The commentary then discusses the grammatical classification of the construct phrase 'salat al-kusuf' as a definitive addition (idafat ta'rif) because the reality (mahiyyah) is complete, paralleling 'maa' al-bi'r' (well water). It is an addition of a thing to its cause, as the eclipse is the cause. The author notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars, such as those cited in Al-Asrar, deemed the prayer obligatory, citing the Prophet's command 'hurry to prayer.' However, the author clarifies that the command is for recommendation (nadb), and there is consensus from most Hanafi scholars. Those who obligated it restricted obligation to solar eclipse only, but this is refuted by the prior consensus. Hence the relied-upon position is sunnah. The proof is from a sahih hadith of Abu Dawud and others that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs during an eclipse and then said to pray as you pray the most recent obligatory prayer, which was Fajr. The hadiths indicate two rak'ahs with one bowing per rak'ah. Congregation is only with the imam, to avoid fitna. The prayer is performed without adhan or iqamah, without audible recitation (contrary to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and without sermon by consensus. Instead, the call is 'as-salatu jamiah' (prayer is gathering). It is sunnah to prolong the prayer, recitation, bowing, and prostration, as the Prophet did. The imam then makes supplication, either sitting facing qibla or standing facing the people; the latter is better. The congregation says amin. They continue until the sun reappears fully. If the imam is absent, people pray individually, two or four rak'ahs, in their homes. Similarly, lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually because the Prophet never gathered people for it at night, and large night gatherings cause fitna. The distinction between kusuf (loss of light) and khusuf (loss of disk) is noted, but the ruling applies to both.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Loss of light of the sun or moon; technically, the darkening of the sun (eclipse).
خسوف (khusuf): Eclipse of the moon (lunar eclipse).
كهيئة النفل (ka-hay'at al-nafl): In the manner of supererogatory prayer: two rak'ahs with one bowing per rak'ah, no extra bowings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the eclipse prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) It is wajib (obligatory) for solar eclipse but not lunar.
B) It is sunnah (recommended) for both solar and lunar eclipses.
C) It is fard kifayah for the community.
D) It is mustahab but only if prayed in congregation.

Key Takeaway
The eclipse prayer is sunnah, not wajib, based on the Hanafi interpretation of the command and the consensus of the school.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

The Conditions and Performance of Eclipse Prayer
Conditions and performance details of eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the conditions for congregation, the sunnah acts (prolonging, supplication), and the ruling for lunar eclipse prayer.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is performed like nafl but with prolonged recitation and supplication, individually when no imam.

After establishing the ruling as sunnah, the passage details how the eclipse prayer is to be performed: the conditions for congregation, the prohibition of adhan and sermon, the recommendation of prolonging, and the supplication. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference on audible recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify congregation conditions
The prayer is performed in congregation only with the imam of Jumu'ah or the sultan's appointee, to avoid fitna.
This is a condition for communal prayer.
2
Note the absence of adhan and sermon
The prayer is performed without adhan, iqamah, or sermon. Instead, the call is 'as-salatu jamiah'.
Contrast with Friday prayer.
3
Recognize the sunnah acts
It is sunnah to prolong the prayer: recitation, bowing, and prostration. The imam recites long surahs like al-Baqarah and Al Imran.
This is based on the Prophet's practice.
4
Understand the supplication
After the prayer, the imam makes supplication facing the qibla or standing facing the people; standing is better. The congregation says amin.
Supplication continues until the eclipse ends.
5
Identify the ruling for lunar eclipse and absent imam
If the imam is not present, people pray individually at home. For the lunar eclipse, prayer is always individual because the Prophet never gathered people for it at night, and night gatherings cause fitna.
The same ruling applies to solar eclipse when imam unavailable.

Chapter of prayer for solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, and terrors. Two rak'ahs are sunnah, in the manner of nafl, for the solar eclipse with the imam of Jumu'ah or the one appointed by the sultan, without adhan, iqamah, audible recitation, or sermon. The addition is of two types: definitive addition and restrictive addition... and he chose in Al-Asrar its obligation, due to the command in his saying: 'When you see any of these, hurry to prayer.' The apparent meaning is that the command is for recommendation, and there is consensus upon that except some companions. Then those who made it obligatory, it is said they only obligated it for the sun not the moon, and that is refuted by the consensus before him. So we said: two rak'ahs are sunnah in the manner of nafl, without extra bowings in them... and it is sunnah to prolong them, to prolong their bowings and prostrations. Then the imam makes supplication sitting facing the qibla if he wishes, or standing facing the people, and that is better. They say amin to his supplication until the sun fully appears. If the imam is not present, they pray individually, like the lunar eclipse.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on eclipse prayers. The author begins by stating the ruling: praying two rak'ahs in the manner of nafl for the solar eclipse is sunnah, performed in congregation only with the Jumu'ah imam or the sultan's appointee, without adhan, iqamah, audible recitation, or sermon. The commentary then discusses the grammatical classification of the construct phrase 'salat al-kusuf' as a definitive addition (idafat ta'rif) because the reality (mahiyyah) is complete, paralleling 'maa' al-bi'r' (well water). It is an addition of a thing to its cause, as the eclipse is the cause. The author notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars, such as those cited in Al-Asrar, deemed the prayer obligatory, citing the Prophet's command 'hurry to prayer.' However, the author clarifies that the command is for recommendation (nadb), and there is consensus from most Hanafi scholars. Those who obligated it restricted obligation to solar eclipse only, but this is refuted by the prior consensus. Hence the relied-upon position is sunnah. The proof is from a sahih hadith of Abu Dawud and others that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs during an eclipse and then said to pray as you pray the most recent obligatory prayer, which was Fajr. The hadiths indicate two rak'ahs with one bowing per rak'ah. Congregation is only with the imam, to avoid fitna. The prayer is performed without adhan or iqamah, without audible recitation (contrary to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and without sermon by consensus. Instead, the call is 'as-salatu jamiah' (prayer is gathering). It is sunnah to prolong the prayer, recitation, bowing, and prostration, as the Prophet did. The imam then makes supplication, either sitting facing qibla or standing facing the people; the latter is better. The congregation says amin. They continue until the sun reappears fully. If the imam is absent, people pray individually, two or four rak'ahs, in their homes. Similarly, lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually because the Prophet never gathered people for it at night, and large night gatherings cause fitna. The distinction between kusuf (loss of light) and khusuf (loss of disk) is noted, but the ruling applies to both.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Loss of light of the sun or moon; technically, the darkening of the sun (eclipse).
خسوف (khusuf): Eclipse of the moon (lunar eclipse).
كهيئة النفل (ka-hay'at al-nafl): In the manner of supererogatory prayer: two rak'ahs with one bowing per rak'ah, no extra bowings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for the lunar eclipse prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is the same as solar eclipse, performed in congregation.
B) It is performed individually because the Prophet never gathered people for it at night.
C) It is wajib because it is a night prayer.

Key Takeaway
Eclipse prayer is performed like nafl with specific sunnan acts; it is individual for lunar eclipse and when no imam is present.

Rulings of Solar Eclipse Prayer (Salat al-Kusuf)
Commentary on the rulings of solar eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on solar eclipse prayer and explain the recommended procedures including the call, lengthening, and supplication.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is a confirmed sunnah with specific prolonged actions and a unique call.

The solar eclipse prayer is a special devotional act that reflects the believer's awe of Allah's signs. The Hanafi school details its performance to maximize humility and recollection. This lesson will walk you through the key elements: the call to gather, the length of recitation, bowing, and prostration, the imam's supplication, and how to pray when the imam is absent. We will also examine the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal category of the solar eclipse prayer. Is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? The text states it is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's action (fi'l) without an explicit command.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The text quotes hadith from Aisha (RA) on the length of recitation and from Abdullah ibn Amr on prolonged bowing and prostration.
Both hadith are ahad (single-narrator) and zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith prove the recommended actions. The Prophet's actual practice (fi'l) indicates sunniyyah (recommendation), not obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a fi'l is not obligatory unless accompanied by a command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if other schools differ. The text does not mention ikhtilaf here, but the Hanafi position is consistent. Other schools may have different views on elements like the number of rak'ahs or congregation.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text relies on the zahir al-riwayah and preferences of later Hanafi authorities.
The mufta bihi is as described: sunnah muakkadah with specific acts.

Rather, it is called out: 'The prayer is gathering.' And it is sunnah to lengthen them (the two rak'ahs), and to lengthen their bowing and prostration. Then the imam supplicates sitting facing the qibla if he wishes, or standing facing the people, and that is better. And they say 'amin' to his supplication until the sun is fully cleared. And if the imam is not present, they pray individually, like the lunar eclipse prayer. (Commentary: ...)

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). It begins by stating that instead of the regular adhan, the call 'as-salatu jamiah' (prayer is gathering) is made. Then it explains that it is sunnah to lengthen the prayer, including the recitation, bowing, and prostration. Evidence is given from the hadith of Aisha (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) recited Surah al-Baqarah in the first rak'ah and Al-Imran in the second, and from a hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr describing prolonged bowing and prostration. The imam's supplication after prayer is described: he may sit facing qibla or stand facing the people, with the latter being preferable. The congregation says amin. If the imam is absent, each person prays individually. The text also references that lunar eclipse prayer is similar, and that individual prayer is preferred due to lack of transmitted congregation for lunar eclipses.

Key Terms
صلاة الكسوف (salat al-kusuf): Solar eclipse prayer, consisting of two rak'ahs with prolonged recitation.
فرادى (furada): Individually, not in congregation.

Prayers During Calamities: Individual Prayer for Ayat
Extension of individual prayer from lunar eclipse to other calamities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the calamities for which individual prayer is recommended and explain the rationale based on the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
During natural calamities, pray individually to turn to Allah.

The Hanafi school teaches that just as the lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually, so too are prayers during other terrifying natural events. These events are signs (ayat) from Allah, reminding us to repent and seek closeness to Him through prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recall that the lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually (not in congregation). This is the foundation for the extension.
The source passage begins by linking to the previous discussion on lunar eclipse.
2
List the calamities
Enumerate all the events mentioned: immense darkness by day (solar eclipse), intense wind, earthquakes, thunderbolts, shooting stars, bright light at night, snow, continuous rain, general diseases, overwhelming fear of the enemy, and similar terrors.
The list is illustrative, not exhaustive.
3
Understand the rationale
These events are admonitions for servants to abandon sins and return to obedience. Prayer is the closest state of the servant to his Lord.
The purpose is spiritual reformation, not ritual obligation.
4
Note the mode: individual prayer
All these prayers are performed individually (فرادى), not in congregation, because congregation was not transmitted for such prayers.
This is a distinguishing feature of the Hanafi school.
5
Conclude with the recommendation
The prayer is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended act) based on analogy with the lunar eclipse prayer.
It is not obligatory (wajib or fard).

It states that like the lunar eclipse prayer, prayer during immense darkness by day, intense wind, terror from earthquakes, thunderbolts, shooting stars, bright lights at night, snow, continuous rain, widespread diseases, and fear of the enemy should be performed individually. The reason given is that these events are reminders for people to repent and turn to Allah, and the best way to do so is prayer. The passage ends with a supplication for pardon and well-being.

Valid Excuses for Praying Alone in Congregation
Listing conditions that permit praying individually due to hardship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the valid excuses for praying alone according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between conditions that excuse and those that do not.

Core Idea
Intense darkness, strong wind, natural terror, illness, and enemy fear excuse a man from the wajib congregation.

In the Hanafi school, praying in congregation (jama'ah) is wajib for men. However, the Shari'ah recognizes hardships that make attendance genuinely difficult. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates those excuses, showing the school's balanced approach between obligation and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recall that for Hanafi men, praying in congregation is wajib (obligatory) for the five daily prayers. This lesson covers when that obligation may be lifted.
This ruling applies to men only; women are not required to attend congregation.
2
Locate the list of excuses in the passage
Scan the Arabic text and identify each specific excuse: intense darkness (day), strong wind, terror from earthquakes, thunderbolts, shooting stars, intense light at night, snow, continuous rain, general illnesses, and overwhelming fear of an enemy.
The list is exhaustive for common excuses; similar extreme hardships are included under 'and similar things'.
3
Categorize each excuse
Group the excuses into natural phenomena (e.g., weather, earthquakes) and human-related (illness, enemy fear). Note that all must be genuinely burdensome.
The common element is hardship that makes attending the mosque unreasonably difficult.
4
Understand the requirement of genuineness
The excuse must be real and widespread enough to create difficulty. For example, a mild drizzle is not an excuse, but continuous heavy rain is.
The condition 'continuous rain' implies persistence, not a passing shower.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Take a scenario like a severe thunderstorm at night. Determine that it falls under 'strong wind' and 'terror' from thunderbolts, thus excusing from congregation.
The prayer itself is still obligatory but can be performed alone at home with full validity.

Source Text

And the intense darkness during the day, the strong wind, and the terror. Signs: And (also) praying individually due to the presence of intense darkness during the day, and the strong wind whether night or day, and terror from earthquakes, thunderbolts, shooting stars, intense light at night, snow, continuous rain, general illnesses, overwhelming fear of the enemy, and similar things from fears and terrors. Because all of this frightens the servants so that they abandon sins and return to the obedience of Allah Almighty, which contains their success and righteousness. And the closest state of the servant in returning to his Lord is prayer. We ask Allah of His bounty for pardon and well-being by the rank of our master and our liege lord Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage lists valid excuses that permit a Muslim to pray individually (furan) instead of in congregation. These excuses include: intense darkness during the day, strong wind (night or day), terror from natural phenomena like earthquakes, thunderbolts, shooting stars, intense light at night, snow, continuous rain, general illnesses, and overwhelming fear of an enemy. The underlying rationale is that these conditions cause fear and hardship, turning people away from sins and toward obedience. The author adds that the best way to return to Allah is through prayer, and concludes with a supplication. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that congregation is a wajib (for men) but is waived due to valid excuses.

Key Terms
فَزَع (faza'): Terror or panic caused by natural disasters like earthquakes, thunderstorms, etc.
صلاة فرادى (salat furādā): Praying individually, as opposed to in congregation (jama'ah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Being tired from work

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows praying alone when genuine hardship (like severe weather, illness, or fear) prevents attending congregation, balancing obligation with mercy.

The Wisdom Behind Concessions: Prayer as the Return to Allah
Explaining the wisdom behind the concessions for praying alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hikmah (wisdom) behind the concessions for praying alone, as presented in the Nur al-Idah commentary.

Core Idea
Hardships remind people of their dependence on Allah, and prayer is the best way to return to Him.

After listing the excuses, the author adds a profound rationale: all these terrors are sent to frighten servants so they abandon sins and turn back to Allah. The nearest state of a servant to his Lord is prayer. This lesson delves into the spiritual purpose behind the legal concessions.

Guided Path
1
Read the rationale portion of the passage
Pay attention to the sentence beginning with 'because all of this frightens the servants...' and the conclusion that the closest state is prayer.
The author shifts from legal listing to theological explanation.
2
Identify the purpose of the hardships
The text states that fears and terrors are meant to make people abandon sins (ma'asi) and return to obedience (ta'a). Understand this as divine mercy calling to repentance.
Hardships are not punishments but reminders.
3
Connect the purpose to prayer
The author asserts that the 'closest state' (aqrab ahwal) of a servant in returning to his Lord is prayer. Thus, when hardships occur, prayer becomes the primary means of drawing near to Allah.
This explains why the Shari'ah facilitates prayer during such times by allowing individual prayer.
4
Reflect on the supplication
The passage ends with a supplication asking for pardon and well-being. Recognize this as the author's acknowledgment of human weakness and need for Allah's mercy.
The dua encapsulates the lesson: we rely on Allah's bounty.

Ruling of Istisqa' Prayer: Permissible but Not Sunnah
Establishing the ruling of the prayer for rain with proofs and addressing the dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Istisqa' prayer and explain the proof that it is not a sunnah.

Core Idea
Istisqa' prayer is permissible but not a sunnah; the hadith is shadhdh and Umar's practice confirms it.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the formal prayer for rain (Istisqa'). While many Muslims assume this two-rak'ah prayer is a stressed sunnah, the Hanafi school holds that it is merely permissible (ja'iz) and not a sunnah at all. This conclusion is based on careful hadith criticism and the practice of the early community.

Guided Path
1
Define Istisqa' lexically and legally
Understand the linguistic and terminological meaning of istisqa', and its Quranic basis.
The verses 76:21 and 77:27 use 'suqya' to indicate drink.
2
Identify the ruling and its nuance
The author states that the prayer is ja'iz (permissible) without karahah, but it is not sunnah. Note that this is a negative ruling on the sunnah status.
Ja'iz means permissible; it is not makruh but also not recommended.
3
Examine the key proof: the shadhdh hadith
The author argues that the hadith reporting the Prophet's prayer is shadhdh (anomalous), meaning it contradicts more authentic reports.
Kamal ibn al-Humam explains why it is shadhdh: if it were authentic, it would have been widely transmitted.
4
Analyze the argument from Umar's practice
Umar did not perform the prayer during his own istisqa', and no Companion objected. This silence indicates the prayer was not a known sunnah.
Umar was known for strict adherence to Sunnah.
5
Compare with opposing school
The Shafi'i school holds the prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah. The Hanafi response is based on hadith criticism and the practice of the salaf.
The practical difference: Hanafis may omit the prayer without blame; Shafi'is consider it recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستسقاء هو طلب السقيا، يقال: سقاه الله وأسقاه، وقد جاء في القرآن وَسَقَنَهُمْ رَبُّهُمْ شَرَابًا طَهُورًا [الانسان: ٢١] وَأَسْقَيْنَكُم مَاءً فُرَانًا [المرسلات: ٢٧]، وقيل: سقاه: ناوله ليشرب وأسقاه أي جعل له سقيا. والسقي مصدر، وطلب الماء يكون في ضمنه، كالاستغفار طلب المغفرة وغفر الذنوب في ضمنه، فهو شرعاً طلب العباد السقي من الله تعالى بالثناء عليه، والرجوع إليه بالتوبة والاستغفار، وثبت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، روي أن قوم نوح لما كذبوه بعد طول تكرير الدعوة حبس الله عنهم القطر، وأعقم أرحام نسائهم أربعين سنة، وقيل: سبعين سنة، فوعدهم أنهم إن آمنوا رزقهم الله الخصب، ورفع عنهم ما كانوا عليه، وشرع من قبلنا شرع لنا إذا قصه الله ورسوله من غير إنكار، وهذا كذلك، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استسقى والإجماع ظاهر على الاستسقاء. له صلاةٌ جائزة بلا كراهة، وليست سنة، لأنه إن كان صلى مرة كما ورد شاذاً فقد استسقى مرة أخرى بدون صلاة، فلم تكن الصلاة فيه سنة، قال الكمال: ووجه الشذوذ أن فعله صلى الله عليه وسلم لو كان ثابتاً لاشتهر نقله اشتهاراً واسعاً، ولفعل عمر له حين استسقى، لأنه كان أشد الناس اتباعاً لسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولأنكروا عليه إذ لم يفعل، لأنها كانت بحضرة جميع الصحابة لتوافر الكل في الخروج مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم للاستسقاء، فلما لم تفعل ولم ينكروا ولم تشتهر روايتها في الصدر الأول، بل هو عن ابن عباس، وعبد الله بن زيد، على اضطراب في
Chapter of Istisqa'. It is asking for rain. It is said: 'Saqahu Allah' and 'Asqahu Allah'. It has come in the Quran: 'And their Lord will give them a pure drink' [al-Insan: 21] and 'And We give you fresh water to drink' [al-Mursalat: 27]. It is said: 'Saqahu' means he handed it to him to drink, and 'Asqahu' means he provided a drink for him. 'Saqy' is the source. The request for water is included in it, just as 'istighfar' is a request for forgiveness and the forgiveness of sins is included in it. Legally, it is the servants' request for rain from Allah Almighty by praising Him and returning to Him in repentance and seeking forgiveness. It is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. It is narrated that when the people of Noah denied him after a long repetition of calling, Allah withheld rain from them and made the wombs of their women barren for forty years, and it is said seventy years. Then He promised them that if they believed, Allah would provide them with fertility and remove what they were experiencing. The law of those before us is law for us if Allah and His Messenger relate it without rejection, and this is so. And the Messenger of Allah prayed for rain, and consensus is evident on istisqa'. He has a prayer that is permissible without dislike, and it is not sunnah. Because if he prayed once as transmitted shadhdh, he prayed for rain another time without prayer, so prayer was not established as sunnah in it. Al-Kamal said: The aspect of its shudhudh is that if his action was established, its transmission would have been widely famous, and Umar would have done it when he prayed for rain, because he was the most stringent in following the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, and they would have objected to him for not doing it, because it was in the presence of all the Companions due to everyone coming out with the Prophet for istisqa'. When it was not done and they did not object, and its narration did not become famous in the first generation, rather it is from Ibn Abbas and Abdullah ibn Zayd with some contradiction.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Istisqa' (prayer for rain). The author defines istisqa' lexically and legally, citing Quranic verses (76:21 and 77:27) that use the word 'suqya'. Legally, it is the act of asking Allah for rain through praise, repentance, and seeking forgiveness. The author states that istisqa' is established by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, mentioning the story of Prophet Nuh and the general principle that the laws of previous prophets are binding if mentioned without rejection in Quran. Then the key ruling: 'He has a prayer that is permissible without dislike, and it is not sunnah.' This means the formal two-rak'ah prayer for rain is ja'iz (permissible) and not makruh, but it is not a sunnah (i.e., not a confirmed recommended act). The reasoning: the Prophet is reported to have performed the prayer once in a shadhdh (anomalous) narration, but he also made du'a for rain without the prayer on other occasions. If the prayer were truly sunnah, it would have been widely known and practiced by the Companions, especially Umar, who was meticulous in following Sunnah. Since Umar did not perform the prayer during his own istisqa', and no Companion objected, it indicates the prayer is not sunnah. The author cites Kamal ibn al-Humam's reasoning: the hadith of the Prophet's prayer is shadhdh (contradicts more authentic reports), and the widespread practice of the salaf was mere du'a. Thus, the Hanafi position is that the istisqa' prayer is permissible (some later Hanafis consider it mustahabb, but the author here affirms it is not sunnah).

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa'): Legally, the act of asking Allah for rain through praise, repentance, and seeking forgiveness.
شاذ (shādh): Anomalous narration that contradicts more reliable reports; here the hadith of the Prophet's prayer for rain is considered shadhdh.
سنة (sunnah): A confirmed recommended practice; here the author denies the prayer is sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider the istisqa' prayer not a sunnah?
A) The Quran does not mention prayer for rain
B) The hadith reporting the prayer is shadhdh and Umar did not perform it
C) The Prophet never prayed for rain
D) Consensus that it is not permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Istisqa' prayer is ja'iz but not a sunnah, based on the shadhdh nature of the relevant hadith and the practice of Umar and the Companions.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prayer for Rain (Istisqa): Permissible, Not Sunnah
Defines istisqa, provides proofs, and discusses intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer for rain and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding congregation.

Core Idea
The prayer for rain is permissible but not a sunnah because the Prophet did not consistently perform it.

Istisqa—seeking rain from Allah—is a legitimate act established by the Quran and Sunnah. However, the specific form of a prescribed prayer for rain is debated within the Hanafi school. This lesson explores the ruling on salat al-istisqa, the proofs for its permissibility, and the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether it should be performed in congregation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the passage: the prayer is permissible (ja'iz) but not a sunnah. Understand the reasoning: the Prophet once prayed for rain and once did not, so there is no constancy (muwazabah).
The Hanafi definition of sunnah requires consistent practice.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the imam should lead two rak'ahs with audible recitation like 'Eid, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
They rely on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs for rain without adhan or iqamah.
The hadith is considered odd (shadhdh) by Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that even if the hadith is authentic, it only shows permissibility, not sunnah. Sunnah requires consistency, which is lacking since the Prophet also prayed for rain without the prayer.
Al-Kamal argues the hadith would have been widely known if it were a sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Hanifa says no congregational prayer; individuals may pray alone. The Sahibayn allow congregation. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is permissibility without congregation, and congregation is disliked according to some.
Zahir al-Riwayah states no prayer in istisqa, but the author leans toward permissibility for individuals.

وأسقاه أي جعل له سقيا. والسقي مصدر، وطلب الماء يكون في ضمنه، كالاستغفار طلب المغفرة وغفر الذنوب في ضمنه، فهو شرعاً طلب العباد السقي من الله تعالى بالثناء عليه، والرجوع إليه بالتوبة والاستغفار، وثبت عليه، وشرع من قبلنا شرع لنا إذا قصه الله ورسوله من غير إنكار، وهذا كذلك، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استسقى والإجماع ظاهر على الاستسقاء. له صلاة جائزة بلا كراهة، وليست سنة، لأنه إن كان صلى مرة كما ورد شاذاً فقد استسقى مرة أخرى بدون صلاة، فلم تكن الصلاة فيه سنة، قال الكمال: ووجه الشذوذ أن فعله لو كان ثابتاً لاشتهر نقله اشتهاراً واسعاً، ولفعل عمر له حين استسقى، لأنه كان أشد الناس اتباعاً لسنة رسول الله، ولأنكروا عليه إذ لم يفعل، لأنها كانت بحضرة جميع الصحابة لتوافر الكل في الخروج مع النبي للاستسقاء، فلما لم تفعل ولم ينكروا ولم تشتهر روايتها في الصدر الأول، بل هو عن ابن عباس، وعبد الله بن زيد، على اضطراب في من غير جماعة، كيفيتها عنهما كان ذلك شذوذاً فيما حضره الخاص والعام والصغير والكبير، انتهى. فلذا قلنا: تجوز الصلاة في الاستسقاء، وتؤدى من غير جماعة. ولأنه سأل أبو يوسف أبا حنيفة رحمه الله عن الاستسقاء هل فيه صلاة أو دعاء مؤقت أو خطبة؟ فقال: أما صلاة بجماعة فلا، ولكن فيه الدعاء والاستغفار، وإن صلوا وحداناً فلا بأس به، قال الزيلعي وهذا ينفي كونها سنة أو مستحبة، ولكن إن صلوا وحداناً لا يكون بدعة، ولا يكره، فكأنه يرى إباحتها فقط في حق المنفرد انتهى. قلت: وفيه إشارة إلى كراهة الجماعة فيها انتهى، وذكر صاحب التحفة وغيره أنه لا صلاة في الاستسقاء في «ظاهر الرواية»، وهذا ينفي مشروعيتها مطلقاً انتهى، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله: يصلي الإمام ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقراءة كالعيد بلا أذان ولا إقامة لما روى ابن عباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى فيها ركعتين كصلاة العيد في الجهر بالقراءة والصلاة بلا أذان وإقامة، فقلنا: إن ثبت ذلك دل على الجواز، ونحن لا نمنعه، وإنما الكلام في أنها سنة أو لا، والسنة: ما واظب النبي عليه وها هنا فعله مرة وتركه أخرى، فلم يكن فعله أكثر من تركه حتى تكون مواظبة، فلا يكون سنة كذا في العناية، وقال شيخ الإسلام فيه دليل على الجواز عندنا يجوز لو صلوا بجماعة، لكن ليس بسنة انتهى. وقد صرح الحاكم في الكافي بقوله: وتكره صلاة التطوع بجماعة ما خلا قيام رمضان وصلاة الكسوف انتهى، وهذا خلاف ما قال شيخ الإسلام رحمه الله، ذكره الكمال.
Chapter of Istisqa: It is seeking rain. It is said: God gave him drink (saqahu) and gave drink (asqahu). And it came in the Quran: 'And their Lord gave them a pure drink' and 'And we have given you fresh water to drink.' And it is said: Saqahu: He gave it to him to drink; Asqahu: He made a drinking source for him. The verbal noun is saqy, and seeking water is included in it, just as seeking forgiveness implies forgiveness and pardon. Legally, it is the servants' request for rain from God Almighty through praise of Him, and returning to Him in repentance and seeking forgiveness. It is established by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. It is narrated that when the people of Noah disbelieved him after repeated calling, God withheld rain from them and made their women barren for forty years, or seventy, and promised them that if they believed, He would provide them plenty. The law of those before us is our law if God and His Messenger relate it without rejection, and this is so. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, prayed for rain, and consensus is clear on Istisqa. He has a prayer, permissible without disapproval, but it is not a sunnah, because although he prayed once (as transmitted as odd), he also prayed for rain another time without prayer, so the prayer was not established as a sunnah. Al-Kamal said: The aspect of oddity is that if his action were established, its transmission would be widely known, and Umar would have done it when he prayed for rain, for he was the most adherent to the Sunnah, and they would have objected to him for not doing it. Since it was done in the presence of all the Companions, and they did not do it nor object, and its report was not widespread in the early period, being reported only by Ibn Abbas and Abdullah ibn Zaid with inconsistency, in an assembly of elite and common, young and old, ended. Therefore we say: Prayer in Istisqa is permissible, and it is performed without congregation. Because Abu Yusuf asked Abu Hanifa about Istisqa: Is there a prayer, a timed supplication, or a sermon? He said: As for prayer in congregation, no; but there is supplication and seeking forgiveness. If they pray individually, there is no harm. Al-Zayla'i said: This negates its being sunnah or recommended, but if they pray individually, it is not an innovation nor disliked. It seems he permits it only for the individual, ended. I say: In it is an indication of disapproval of congregation in it, ended. The author of al-Tuhfa and others mentioned that there is no prayer in Istisqa in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), which negates its legitimacy absolutely, ended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may God have mercy on them) said: The imam prays two rak'ahs, reciting audibly like the 'Eid prayer, without adhan or iqamah, based on Ibn Abbas's report that he, peace be upon him, prayed two rak'ahs like the 'Eid prayer in audible recitation and without adhan and iqamah. We say: If that is established, it indicates permissibility. We do not prohibit it. The discussion is on whether it is a sunnah or not. Sunnah is what the Prophet consistently did. Here, he did it once and omitted it other times, so his doing it was not more than his omitting it to constitute constancy, so it is not a sunnah; as in al-'Inayah. Shaykh al-Islam said: It is evidence of permissibility in our view; it is permissible if they pray in congregation, but it is not a sunnah, ended. Al-Hakim stated in al-Kafi: 'Voluntary prayer in congregation is disliked except for qiyam Ramadan and eclipse prayer,' ended. This contradicts what Shaykh al-Islam said, mentioned by al-Kamal.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of the prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa). The author begins by defining istisqa linguistically and legally, then establishes its legitimacy via the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. He then states the core ruling: 'He has a prayer, permissible without disapproval, but it is not a sunnah.' This is the Hanafi position based on the fact that the Prophet ﷺ prayed for rain at least once but also did so without prayer on other occasions, indicating it was not a consistent practice (wuzub). The author then details the dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that there is no congregational prayer; individuals may pray alone without blame, but it is not recommended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the imam should lead two rak'ahs with audible recitation like 'Eid, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The author clarifies that even if the hadith is established, it only proves permissibility, not sunnah status, because the criterion for sunnah is constancy. The passage also notes a difference between 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (which denies any prayer) and the more lenient view of some later scholars. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the prayer is permissible but not sunnah, and congregation is disliked according to some, though others permit it.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa): The act of seeking rain from Allah through prayer and supplication.
شاذ (shadhdh): A hadith that is transmitted by a reliable narrator but contradicts a more reliable or widespread transmission.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The most authoritative and widely transmitted rulings within the Hanafi school, from the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa)?
A) It is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and should be performed in congregation.
B) It is permissible (ja'iz) but not sunnah, and congregation is not recommended.
C) It is obligatory (wajib) in times of drought.
D) It is disliked (makruh) because it resembles the practices of other religions.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, salat al-istisqa is permissible but not a sunnah, and congregation is not recommended.

Recommended Etiquettes for Istisqa (Prayer for Rain)
Lists recommended actions for istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended actions (mustahabbat) for istisqa and explain their purpose of demonstrating humility.

Core Idea
Istisqa mustahabbat: humility through clothing, charity, and three days.

Istisqa is not only the prayer itself but a multi-day event of collective humility and repentance. The Hanafi school prescribes specific outward actions to invoke Allah's mercy, as transmitted from the Prophet ﷺ and the righteous predecessors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling level
Recognize that all actions listed are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. Their purpose is to enhance humility and desperation before Allah.
2
List the recommended actions from the text
Extract each recommended practice: three days going out, walking, wearing worn or patched clothes, giving charity daily, renewing repentance, seeking forgiveness for Muslims, reconciling, and bringing out animals.
3
Understand the rationale for each action
Each action symbolizes humility: old clothes show poverty of soul, charity shows sincerity, and separating animals evokes mercy.
Patched clothes (muraqqa'ah) are even better.
4
Differentiate from normal prayer conduct
Normally, wearing clean clothes is recommended; for istisqa, worn clothes are prescribed to alter the usual dignified appearance.
5
Apply the list to a contemporary scenario
Imagine a community facing drought: how would you implement these etiquettes today (e.g., announcement of three days, collection of charity, advising on dress)?
The actions are adaptable as long as the spirit of humility is maintained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله استغفار لما ذكرناه. ويُستحب الخروج له ثلاثة أيام متتابعات، ولم ينقل أكثر منها، ويخرجون مشاة في ثياب خَلَقَةٍ غَسِيلَةٍ غير مرقعة أو مُرَقَعَةٍ، وهو أولى إظهاراً لصفة كونهم متذللين متواضعين خاشعين لله تعالى ناكسين رؤوسهم مقدمين الصدقة كل يوم قبل خروجهم ويجددون التوبة، ويستغفرون للمسلمين، ويتراضون فيما بينهم برد المظالم وطلب المسامحة من التبعات، ويُستحب إخراج الدواب وأولادها، ويشتتون فيما بينها.
And he has seeking forgiveness as we mentioned. And it is recommended to go out for it (i.e., for istisqa) for three consecutive days, and more than that has not been transmitted. And they go out walking in worn, washed clothes, not patched, or patched, and the latter is better to show the attribute of being humbled, humble, reverent before Allah, lowering their heads, giving charity each day before their departure. And they renew repentance, seek forgiveness for the Muslims, reconcile among themselves by returning wrongs and seeking forgiveness from liabilities. And it is recommended to bring out animals and their young, and separate them.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a list of recommended practices (mustahabbat) for those going out to perform istisqa. The author first notes that seeking forgiveness (istighfar) is also part of the practice. Then, the recommended actions include: going out for three consecutive days (no more is reported), walking, wearing old washed clothes (or patched, which is better to show humility), giving charity each day before leaving, renewing repentance, seeking forgiveness for all Muslims, reconciling with each other by returning unjustly taken rights and seeking pardon. Additionally, it is recommended to bring out domestic animals and even separate them (so their sounds and condition evoke mercy). These actions are meant to demonstrate utmost humility, desperation, and dependence on Allah, in contrast to normal dignified behavior.

Key Terms
خَلَقَة (khaliqah): Old, worn-out clothes that have been used for a long time.
مُرَقَّعَة (muraqqa'ah): Patched clothing, indicating poverty and humility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Istisqa is accompanied by recommended acts of humility, including worn clothing, charity, and three days of prayers.

The Hanafi Ruling on Congregational Prayer for Rain (Istisqa')
Intra-Hanafi dispute on congregational prayer and recommended practices for istisqa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi on congregational prayer for istisqa', distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and identify the recommended etiquettes for seeking rain.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that no congregational prayer is prescribed for rain; individual prayer is permissible but not sunnah.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the Hanafi position on istisqa'. While the Prophet performed a prayer for rain, the Hanafi school, following Zahir al-Riwayah, does not prescribe a congregational prayer as sunnah. Abu Hanifa’s view is that only supplication and seeking forgiveness are legislated; individual prayer is permissible but not a sunnah. The passage also details the recommended etiquettes for the community when seeking rain.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position on congregational prayer
From the text, Abu Hanifa says 'As for congregational prayer, no.' So there is no sunnah prayer; only supplication and istighfar.
This is the mufta bihi.
2
Identify the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
They hold that the imam should lead two rak'ahs aloud like 'Eid, based on a hadith of Ibn Abbas.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the proof for the opposing view
The hadith of Ibn Abbas is cited. The Hanafi response acknowledges its authenticity but argues it was done only once, so it does not establish sunnah (which requires consistency).
The principle: sunnah requires continuous practice.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and why
The relied-upon view is that there is no congregational prayer; it is merely permissible individually. The text follows Zahir al-Riwayah and Abu Hanifa's fatwa.
Tarjih authority: the commentator follows Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Apply the recommended etiquettes for istisqa'
The text outlines recommended practices such as going out for three days, wearing worn clothes, giving charity, etc., which are agreed upon.
These are mustahabbat, not disputed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منْ غيرِ جماعةٍ، وله استغفار. ويُستحب الخروج له ثلاثةَ أَيَّامٍ مُشاةً، في ثيابِ خَلَقَةٍ غَسِيلَةٍ، أَوْ مُرَقَّعَةٍ متذللينَ، متواضعين، خاشعين لله تعالى، ناكسين رؤوسَهُمْ، مقدمين الصدقة كل يوم قبل خروجهم. ويُستحب إخراج الدواب. >> كيفيتها عنهما كان ذلك شذوذاً فيما حضره الخاص والعام والصغير والكبير، انتهى. فلذا قلنا: تجوز الصلاة في الاستسقاء، وتؤدى من غير جماعةٍ ولأنه سأل أبو يوسف أبا حنيفة رحمه الله عن الاستسقاء هل فيه صلاة أو دعاء مؤقت أو خطبة؟ فقال: أما صلاة بجماعة فلا، ولكن فيه الدعاء والاستغفار، وإن صلوا وحداناً فلا بأس به، قال الزيلعي وهذا ينفي كونها سنة أو مستحبة، ولكن إن صلوا وحداناً لا يكون بدعة، ولا يكره، فكأنه يرى إباحتها فقط في حق المنفرد انتهى. قلت: وفيه إشارة إلى كراهة الجماعة فيها انتهى، وذكر صاحب ( التحفة ) وغيره أنه لا صلاة في الاستسقاء في «ظاهر الرواية»، وهذا ينفي مشروعيتها مطلقاً انتهى، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله: يصلي الإمام ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقراءة كالعيد بلا أذان ولا إقامة لما روى ابن عباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى فيها ركعتين كصلاة العيد في الجهر بالقراءة والصلاة بلا أذان وإقامة، فقلنا: إن ثبت ذلك دل على الجواز، ونحن لا نمنعه، وإنما الكلام في أنها سنة أو لا، والسنة: ما واظب النبي عليه وها هنا فعله مرة وتركه أخرى، فلم يكن فعله أكثر من تركه حتى تكون مواظبة، فلا يكون سنة كذا في ( العناية )، وقال شيخ الإسلام فيه دليل على الجواز عندنا يجوز لو صلوا بجماعة، لكن ليس بسنة انتهى. وقد صرح الحاكم في ( الكافي) بقوله: وتكره صلاة التطوع بجماعة ما خلا قيام رمضان وصلاة الكسوف انتهى، وهذا خلاف ما قال شيخ الإسلام رحمه الله، ذكره الكمال. (وله استغفار ) لما ذكرناه، (ويُستحبُّ الخروج له) أي: للاستسقاء (ثلاثة أيام) متتابعات، ولم ينقل أكثر منها، ويخرجون (مُشاةً في ثياب خَلَقَةٍ غَسِيلَةٍ) غير مرقعة (أو مُرَقَعَةٍ)، وهو أولى إظهاراً لصفة كونهم متذلّلين متواضعين خاشعين لله تعالى ناكسين رؤوسَهُمْ مقدمينَ الصدقة كل يوم قبل خروجهم) ويجددون التوبة، ويستغفرون للمسلمين، ويتراضون فيما بينهم برد المظالم وطلب المسامحة من التبعات، ويُستحب إخراج الدواب وأولادها، ويشتتون فيما بينها، والشيوخ الكبار، والأطفال. وفي مكة وبيت المقدس في المسجد الحرام والمسجد الأقصى يجتمعون. وينبغي ذلك أيضاً لأهل مدينة سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. ويقومُ الإمامُ مستقبِلَ القِبلة، رافعاً يديهِ. (1) ليحصل التحنن وظهور الضجيج بالحاجات، (وَ) خروج (الشيوخ الكبار، والأطفال) لأن نزول الرحمة بهم، لما في الحديث الشريف، قال : ( هَلْ تُرْزَقُونَ وَتُنْصَرُونَ إِلَّا بِضُعَفَائِكُمْ ) رواه البخاري، وفي خبر ضعيف: « لولا شَبَابٌ خُشَعَ وَبَهَائِمَ رُبَّع، وشيوخٌ رُكَّعَ، وَأَطْفَالٌ رُضَع لَصُبَّ عَلَيْكُمُ العَذَابُ صَبَّا» وورد: «لَوْلا صَبْيَانُ رُضَعُ، وَبَهَائِمَ رُتَّعٌ وَعِبَادٌ اللَّهِ رُكَّعٌ لَصُبَّ عَلَيْكُمُ البَلاءُ صبا ) (وَ) إذا استسقوا يخرجون إلى الصحراء للاتباع، إلا في مكة و) في (بيت المقدس) لا يخرجون، ولكن ( في المسجد الحرام والمسجد الأقصى يجتمعون) اقتداء بالسلف والخلف لشرف المحل، ولزيادة فضله ونزول الرحمة به، ولذا قلت لكوني لم أره مسطوراً، (وينبغي ذلك) أي: الاجتماع للاستسقاء بالمسجد النبوي (أيضاً لأهل مدينة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ) وهذا أمر جلي ظاهر، إذ لا يستغاث وتستنزل الرحمة في مدينته المنورة بغير حضرته ومشاهدته في كل حادثة، وإنما يكون بين يديه في مسجده الشريف ومحل سكنه المنيف، وروضته الزهراء، وخليفتيه لمهمات الدنيا والآخرة. وحمل بعض المشايخ عدم ذكره فيما استثني على ضيق المسجد النبوي غير ظاهر، لأن من هو مقيم بالمدينة المنورة لا يبلغ قدر الحاج، وعند اجتماع جملتهم يشاهد اتساع المسجد الشريف في أطرافه، وأما شدة الزحام ففي الروضة وما قاربها للرغبة في زيادة الفضل، وطلب القرب من المصطفى لتبليغ الرسائل، والتوسل لجنابه الكريم بصاحبيه أبي بكر وعمر من كل سائل، فلا يمنع الاجتماع للاستسقاء، ولا إيقاف الدواب بالباب، كما يلزم إيقافها كذلك بالمسجد الحرام والأقصى على الباب، ويقومُ الإمامُ مستقبل القبلة) حالة دعائه (رافعاً يديه) لقول أنس: أن النبي كان لا يرفع يديه في شيء إلا في الاستسقاء فإنه كانَ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضَ إِبْطَيْهِ، وَقَوْلِهِ: وَمَدَّ يَدَيْهِ وَجَعَلَ بُطُونَهُما مِمَّا يَلِي الْأَرْضَ، حَتَّى رَأَيْتُ بَيَاضَ إِبْطَيْهِ ). رواهما أبو داود.
Without congregation, and he has seeking forgiveness. And it is recommended to go out for it for three days on foot, in worn washed clothes, or patched, humbling themselves, humble, submissive to Allah Almighty, lowering their heads, giving charity each day before their departure. And it is recommended to take out animals. >> Its modality according to them was odd in what was attended by the elite and common, young and old, end. So we said: Prayer for rain is permissible, and it is performed without congregation. And because Abu Yusuf asked Abu Hanifa about istisqa': Is there a prayer, or a time-specific supplication, or a sermon? He said: As for congregational prayer, no, but there is supplication and seeking forgiveness. If they pray individually, there is no harm. Al-Zayla'i said: This negates it being sunnah or mustahabb. But if they pray individually, it is not a bid'ah nor disliked. It seems he only permits it for the individual. End. I said: In it is an indication of dislike for congregation in it. End. The author of al-Tuhfah and others mentioned that there is no prayer for rain in 'Zahir al-Riwayah', and this negates its legislated nature absolutely. End. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The imam prays two rak'ahs, reciting aloud like 'Eid, without adhan or iqamah, because Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs like 'Eid prayer in reciting aloud and prayer without adhan and iqamah. So we said: If that is established, it indicates permissibility, and we do not prevent it. The discussion is whether it is sunnah or not. Sunnah is what the Prophet consistently did. Here he did it once and left it other times, so his doing it was not more than his leaving it for it to be consistent, so it is not sunnah. Thus in al-'Inayah. Shaykh al-Islam said: In it is evidence for permissibility. According to us, it is permissible if they pray in congregation, but it is not sunnah. End. Al-Hakim in al-Kafi stated: Voluntary prayer in congregation is disliked except for Qiyam Ramadan and eclipse prayer. End. This contradicts what Shaykh al-Islam said, mentioned by al-Kamal. (And he has seeking forgiveness) as we mentioned. (And it is recommended to go out for it) i.e., for istisqa' (three days) consecutive, and no more has been transmitted. They go out (on foot in worn washed clothes) not patched (or patched), and the latter is better to show their quality of being humbled, humble, submissive to Allah, lowering their heads, giving charity each day before their departure). They renew repentance, seek forgiveness for Muslims, reconcile among themselves by returning wrongful acts and seeking pardon for liabilities. (And it is recommended to take out animals) and their young, and separate them. (And the elderly, and children). In Mecca and Jerusalem, they gather in the Sacred Mosque and al-Aqsa Mosque. And that is also recommended for the people of the city of our master the Prophet . The imam stands facing the qiblah, raising his hands. (1) To attain tenderness and manifestation of clamor with needs, (and) the exit (of the elderly and children) because mercy descends through them, as in the noble hadith: 'Are you given provision and victory except through your weak?' narrated by Bukhari. In a weak report: 'Were it not for humble youth, grazing animals, bowing elders, and suckling infants, punishment would be poured upon you.' (And) when they pray for rain, they go out to the desert following the practice, except in Mecca and Jerusalem, they do not go out but gather in the Sacred Mosque and al-Aqsa Mosque, following the predecessors and successors for the honor of the place, and for its increased virtue and descent of mercy. Therefore I say, because I have not seen it recorded: (And that is recommended) i.e., gathering for istisqa' in the Prophet's mosque (also for the people of the Prophet's city). This is clear, for aid and mercy are sought in his luminous city only through his presence and witnessing in every incident, and it is before him in his noble mosque and elevated dwelling, his fragrant garden, and his two successors for the affairs of this world and the hereafter. Some scholars' justification of its omission from the exceptions due to the narrowness of the Prophet's mosque is not apparent, because one residing in Medina does not reach the status of a pilgrim, and when they gather, the spaciousness of the noble mosque is seen at its edges. As for severe crowding, it is in the garden and its vicinity due to desire for increased virtue and seeking closeness to the Chosen One to convey messages and seek intercession through his two companions Abu Bakr and Umar for every supplicant, so it does not prevent gathering for istisqa' nor halting animals at the door, just as it is necessary to halt them at the door of the Sacred Mosque and al-Aqsa. (And the imam stands facing the qiblah) during his supplication (raising his hands) because of Anas's statement: The Prophet never raised his hands in anything except in istisqa', and he raised his hands until the whiteness of his armpits was seen, and his saying: 'He extended his hands and made their palms facing the ground until I saw the whiteness of his armpits.' Both narrated by Abu Dawud.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion of the matn on the prayer for rain (istisqa'). It opens with the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that there is no congregational prayer for istisqa', only supplication and seeking forgiveness; individuals may pray without congregation, but it is neither sunnah nor mustahabb. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two disciples) say the imam leads two rak'ahs aloud like 'Eid, based on a hadith of Ibn Abbas. The commentator clarifies that the Hanafi school follows the Zahir al-Riwayah, which rejects any prayer for istisqa'. However, the hadith is acknowledged as evidence for permissibility; the issue is whether it is sunnah. Since the Prophet did not consistently perform it, it is not sunnah, but it is permissible. The commentator notes that Shaykh al-Islam allows congregational prayer but not as sunnah, while al-Hakim in al-Kafi states that voluntary congregational prayer is disliked except for Tarawih and eclipse prayer. The relied-upon view is that istisqa' prayer is not legislated as sunnah; individual prayer is permissible without dislike. The passage then details recommended etiquettes: going out for three consecutive days on foot, wearing worn clothes, displaying humility, giving charity, seeking forgiveness, reconciling, bringing out animals and children, and the imam raising his hands with palms facing down. Exceptions are made for Mecca and Jerusalem where people gather in the mosques; the commentator adds that the same applies to the Prophet's mosque in Medina, despite crowding concerns. The recommended practices are based on prophetic example and the principle that mercy descends through the weak.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqā’): Praying for rain; a collective act of seeking rain from Allah through supplication and recommended practices.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the authoritative source within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi position, what is the ruling on praying the istisqa' prayer in congregation?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Permissible without being sunnah
C) Haram
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on istisqa' is that there is no congregational prayer; the community should engage in supplication, repentance, and charity, following the recommended etiquettes.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Location and Participants of Istisqa Prayer
Details the recommended location and participants for istisqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where the istisqa prayer should be performed and who should attend, and justify the exception for Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis.

Core Idea
Istisqa is performed in the desert, except in the three holy cities where the mosque is the preferred place due to honor and mercy.

The istisqa prayer is a sunnah during drought. While the general rule is to go to the desert, the Hanafi school makes a special exception for Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State where istisqa is normally performed and why.
The general practice is to go to the desert following the Prophet's ﷺ example.
2
Identify the exception
Which cities are exempted and where do they gather instead?
Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis are exceptions.
3
Note the proof for weak participants
What hadith supports bringing elders and children?
The hadith 'Are you given provision and victory except through your weak ones?'
4
Examine the extension to Madinah
What is the author's argument for including Madinah alongside Makkah and Bayt al-Maqdis?
The author argues that the mosque's virtue and the fact that Madinah residents do not reach the status of pilgrims justify it.
5
Analyze the refutation of the narrowness objection
Why does the author reject the objection that Masjid an-Nabawi is too narrow?
The author notes that when all gather, the mosque's expanse is apparent, so gathering is not prevented.
