والشيوخ الكبار، والأطفال. وفي مكة وبيت المقدس في المسجد الحرام والمسجد الأقصى يجتمعون. وينبغي ذلك أيضاً لأهل مدينة سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. ويقومُ الإمامُ مستقبِلَ القِبلة، رافعاً يديهِ . لِيَحْصُلَ التَّحَنُنُ وَظُهُورُ الضَّجِيجِ بِالْحَاجَاتِ، وَخُرُوجُ الشُّيُوخِ الْكِبَارِ، وَالْأَطْفَالِ لِنُزُولِ الرَّحْمَةِ بِهِمْ، لِمَا فِي الْحَدِيثِ الشَّرِيفِ: ( هَلْ تُرْزَقُونَ وَتُنْصَرُونَ إِلَّا بِضُعَفَائِكُمْ ) رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ. وَفِي خَبَرٍ ضَعِيفٍ: « لَوْلَا شَبَابٌ خُشَّعُ وَبَهَائِمُ رُبَّعُ، وَشُيُوخٌ رُكَّعُ، وَأَطْفَالٌ رُضَّعُ لَصُبَّ عَلَيْكُمُ الْعَذَابُ صَبَّا» . وَوَرَدَ: «لَوْلَا صِبْيَانُ رُضَّعُ، وَبَهَائِمُ رُتَّعُ وَعِبَادُ اللَّهِ رُكَّعُ لَصُبَّ عَلَيْكُمُ الْبَلَاءُ صَبَّا» . وَإِذَا اسْتَسْقَوْا يَخْرُجُونَ إِلَى الصَّحْرَاءِ لِلِاتِّبَاعِ، إِلَّا فِي مَكَّةَ وَبَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ لَا يَخْرُجُونَ، وَلَكِنْ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَالْمَسْجِدِ الْأَقْصَى يَجْتَمِعُونَ اقْتِدَاءً بِالسَّلَفِ وَالْخَلَفِ لِشَرَفِ الْمَحَلِّ، وَلِزِيَادَةِ فَضْلِهِ وَنُزُولِ الرَّحْمَةِ بِهِ. وَيَنْبَغِي ذَلِكَ أَيْضًا لِأَهْلِ مَدِينَةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ. وَحَمَلَ بَعْضُ الْمَشَايِخِ عَدَمَ ذِكْرِهِ فِيمَا اسْتُثْنِيَ عَلَى ضِيقِ الْمَسْجِدِ النَّبَوِيِّ غَيْرُ ظَاهِرٍ، لِأَنَّ مَنْ هُوَ مُقِيمٌ بِالْمَدِينَةِ الْمُنَوَّرَةِ لَا يَبْلُغُ قَدْرَ الْحَاجِّ، وَعِنْدَ اجْتِمَاعِ جُمْلَتِهِمْ يُشَاهَدُ اتِّسَاعُ الْمَسْجِدِ الشَّرِيفِ فِي أَطْرَافِهِ. فَلَا يَمْنَعُ الِاجْتِمَاعُ لِلِاسْتِسْقَاءِ، وَلَا إِيقَافُ الدَّوَابِّ بِالْبَابِ، كَمَا يُلْزَمُ إِيقَافُهَا كَذَلِكَ بِالْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَالْأَقْصَى عَلَى الْبَابِ. وَيَقُومُ الْإِمَامُ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ حَالَةَ دُعَائِهِ رَافِعًا يَدَيْهِ لِقَوْلِ أَنَسٍ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ لَا يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي الِاسْتِسْقَاءِ فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضُ إِبْطَيْهِ. وَقَوْلِهِ: وَمَدَّ يَدَيْهِ وَجَعَلَ بُطُونَهُمَا مِمَّا يَلِي الْأَرْضَ، حَتَّى رَأَيْتُ بَيَاضَ إِبْطَيْهِ. رَوَاهُمَا أَبُو دَاوُدَ. وَالنَّاسُ قُعُودٌ، مُسْتَقْبِلِينَ الْقِبْلَةَ، يُؤَمِّنُونَ عَلَى دُعَائِهِ، وَيَدْعُو بِأَدْعِيَةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْوَارِدَةِ، وَهِيَ كَثِيرَةٌ وَمِنْهَا مَا نَصَّ عَلَيْهِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: « اللَّهُمَّ اسْقِنَا غَيْثًا مُغِيثًا، هَنِيئًا مَرِيئًا، مُرِيعًا غَدَقًا مُجَلِّلًا سَحًّا طَبَقًا دَائِمًا » وَمَا أَشْبَهَهُ، سِرًّا أَوْ جَهْرًا. وَمِنَ الْوَارِدِ: « اللَّهُمَّ اسْقِنَا الْغَيْثَ وَلَا تَجْعَلْنَا مِنَ الْقَانِطِينَ » « اللَّهُمَّ إِنَّ بِالْعِبَادِ وَالْبِلَادِ وَالْخَلْقِ مِنَ اللَّأْوَاءِ » « اللَّهُمَّ أَنْبِتْ لَنَا الزَّرْعَ، وَأَدِرَّ لَنَا الضَّرْعَ وَاسْقِنَا مِنْ بَرَكَاتِ السَّمَاءِ » « اللَّهُمَّ ارْفَعْ عَنَّا الْجَهْدَ وَالْجُوعَ وَالْعُرْيَ، وَاكْشِفْ عَنَّا مِنَ الْبَلَاءِ مَا لَا يَكْشِفُهُ غَيْرُكَ » « اللَّهُمَّ إِنَّا نَسْتَغْفِرُكَ إِنَّكَ كُنْتَ غَفَّارًا »
And the great elders and children. And in Mecca and Bayt al-Maqdis, in the Sacred Mosque and the Aqsa Mosque, they gather. And that is also befitting for the people of the city of our master the Prophet ﷺ. And the Imam stands facing the qibla, raising his hands. So that compassion and the appearance of loud supplication with needs occur, and the exit of elders and children for the descent of mercy through them, because of the noble hadith: 'Are you given provision and victory except through your weak ones?' narrated by al-Bukhari. And in a weak report: 'If it were not for humble youth, grazing animals, bowing elders, and suckling infants, punishment would be poured upon you.' And it is reported: 'If it were not for suckling infants, grazing animals, and bowing servants of Allah, calamity would be poured upon you.' And when they pray for rain, they go out to the desert following the tradition, except in Mecca and Bayt al-Maqdis they do not go out, but in the Sacred Mosque and the Aqsa Mosque they gather, following the Salaf and Khalaf, for the honor of the place, and for the increase of its virtue and the descent of mercy in it. And that is also befitting for the people of the city of the Prophet ﷺ. And some teachers' attribution of its non-mention among the exceptions to the narrowness of the Prophet's Mosque is not apparent, because whoever resides in Madinah Munawwarah does not reach the status of a pilgrim, and when they all gather, the expanse of the noble mosque is seen in its outskirts. So gathering for istisqa is not prevented, nor stopping animals at the door, as it is necessary to stop them similarly at the Sacred Mosque and the Aqsa at the door. And the Imam stands facing the qibla while supplicating, raising his hands, due to the statement of Anas: 'The Prophet ﷺ would not raise his hands in anything except in istisqa, for he would raise his hands until the whiteness of his armpits was seen.' And his statement: 'And he extended his hands and made their palms facing the ground, until I saw the whiteness of his armpits.' Both are narrated by Abu Dawud. And the people are seated, facing the qibla, saying 'Amin' to his supplication, and he supplicates with the supplications of the Prophet ﷺ that are reported, which are many, including what is stated: 'O Allah, give us an aid-giving rain, wholesome, pleasant, giving increase, abundant, covering, torrential, widespread, continuous.' And similar, privately or publicly. And among the reported: 'O Allah, give us rain and do not make us among the despairing.' 'O Allah, indeed the servants, the land, and the creation are in distress.' 'O Allah, grow for us the crops, and flow for us the udders, and give us from the blessings of the sky.' 'O Allah, remove from us hardship, hunger, and nakedness, and remove from us affliction that none but You can remove.' 'O Allah, we seek Your forgiveness, indeed You are Oft-Forgiving.'
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage from the commentary expands on the rulings of Salat al-Istisqa (prayer for rain). It is a ruling with proof type. The author begins by stating that it is recommended for elders and children to go out for istisqa, as they are more likely to attract mercy. He cites the hadith 'You are given provision and victory only through your weak ones' from Bukhari. Then he discusses the location: Muslims should go out to the open desert except for Makkah and Bayt al-Maqdis, where they gather in al-Masjid al-Haram and al-Masjid al-Aqsa respectively, following the Salaf and Khalaf due to the honor of those places. The author extends this to Madinah, arguing that gathering in Masjid an-Nabawi is also recommended, refuting the objection that the mosque is too narrow. Then the author describes the imam's actions: he stands facing the qibla and raises his hands while supplicating, based on the hadith of Anas. The congregation sits, faces the qibla, and says 'Amin'. Finally, he lists several supplications from the Prophet ﷺ that can be used, including variations in wording, and notes that one may supplicate silently or aloud.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa): Prayer for rain, a sunnah practice performed during drought.
الضجيج (al-dhajeej): Loud supplication and crying out in need.
التحنن (al-tahanun): Showing compassion, especially by bringing children and elders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which locations should the istisqa prayer be performed inside the mosque rather than in the desert?
A) Only in Makkah and Madinah
B) In Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis (Jerusalem)
C) Only in the Sacred Mosque in Makkah
D) In all cities with a mosque

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends performing istisqa in the desert, except in Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis where gathering in the mosque is preferred due to the honor of those places.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Imam's Actions and Supplications in Istisqa
Details the recommended actions and supplications during istisqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah actions of the imam and congregation during the istisqa prayer, including the raising of hands and specific supplications.

Core Idea
The imam faces the qibla, raises his hands until his armpits show, and supplicates with prophetic words while the congregation says amin.

During the istisqa prayer, specific actions are recommended for the imam and the congregation. These include facing the qibla, raising hands, and using the Prophet's ﷺ supplications. This lesson details these sunnah practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's posture
What does the imam do when supplicating (facing direction, hand position)?
The imam stands facing the qibla and raises his hands.
2
Locate the proof for raising hands
Which hadith is cited and what does it show?
The hadith of Anas: the Prophet ﷺ raised his hands until his armpits were white.
3
Determine the congregation's role
How do the people sit and what do they say?
They sit facing the qibla and say amin to the imam's supplication.
4
List the recommended supplications
What are some examples from the Prophet ﷺ?
The text provides several supplications, e.g., 'Allahumma asqina ghaythan mughithan...'.
5
Note the variation in volume
Is it permissible to supplicate silently or aloud?
The text says 'sirran aw jahran' (quietly or aloud), indicating both are allowed.

والشيوخ الكبار، والأطفال. وفي مكة وبيت المقدس في المسجد الحرام والمسجد الأقصى يجتمعون. وينبغي ذلك أيضاً لأهل مدينة سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. ويقومُ الإمامُ مستقبِلَ القِبلة، رافعاً يديهِ . لِيَحْصُلَ التَّحَنُنُ وَظُهُورُ الضَّجِيجِ بِالْحَاجَاتِ، وَخُرُوجُ الشُّيُوخِ الْكِبَارِ، وَالْأَطْفَالِ لِنُزُولِ الرَّحْمَةِ بِهِمْ، لِمَا فِي الْحَدِيثِ الشَّرِيفِ: ( هَلْ تُرْزَقُونَ وَتُنْصَرُونَ إِلَّا بِضُعَفَائِكُمْ ) رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ. وَفِي خَبَرٍ ضَعِيفٍ: « لَوْلَا شَبَابٌ خُشَّعُ وَبَهَائِمُ رُبَّعُ، وَشُيُوخٌ رُكَّعُ، وَأَطْفَالٌ رُضَّعُ لَصُبَّ عَلَيْكُمُ الْعَذَابُ صَبَّا» . وَوَرَدَ: «لَوْلَا صِبْيَانُ رُضَّعُ، وَبَهَائِمُ رُتَّعُ وَعِبَادُ اللَّهِ رُكَّعُ لَصُبَّ عَلَيْكُمُ الْبَلَاءُ صَبَّا» . وَإِذَا اسْتَسْقَوْا يَخْرُجُونَ إِلَى الصَّحْرَاءِ لِلِاتِّبَاعِ، إِلَّا فِي مَكَّةَ وَبَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ لَا يَخْرُجُونَ، وَلَكِنْ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَالْمَسْجِدِ الْأَقْصَى يَجْتَمِعُونَ اقْتِدَاءً بِالسَّلَفِ وَالْخَلَفِ لِشَرَفِ الْمَحَلِّ، وَلِزِيَادَةِ فَضْلِهِ وَنُزُولِ الرَّحْمَةِ بِهِ. وَيَنْبَغِي ذَلِكَ أَيْضًا لِأَهْلِ مَدِينَةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ. وَحَمَلَ بَعْضُ الْمَشَايِخِ عَدَمَ ذِكْرِهِ فِيمَا اسْتُثْنِيَ عَلَى ضِيقِ الْمَسْجِدِ النَّبَوِيِّ غَيْرُ ظَاهِرٍ، لِأَنَّ مَنْ هُوَ مُقِيمٌ بِالْمَدِينَةِ الْمُنَوَّرَةِ لَا يَبْلُغُ قَدْرَ الْحَاجِّ، وَعِنْدَ اجْتِمَاعِ جُمْلَتِهِمْ يُشَاهَدُ اتِّسَاعُ الْمَسْجِدِ الشَّرِيفِ فِي أَطْرَافِهِ. فَلَا يَمْنَعُ الِاجْتِمَاعُ لِلِاسْتِسْقَاءِ، وَلَا إِيقَافُ الدَّوَابِّ بِالْبَابِ، كَمَا يُلْزَمُ إِيقَافُهَا كَذَلِكَ بِالْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَالْأَقْصَى عَلَى الْبَابِ. وَيَقُومُ الْإِمَامُ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ حَالَةَ دُعَائِهِ رَافِعًا يَدَيْهِ لِقَوْلِ أَنَسٍ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ لَا يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي الِاسْتِسْقَاءِ فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ حَتَّى يُرَى بَيَاضُ إِبْطَيْهِ. وَقَوْلِهِ: وَمَدَّ يَدَيْهِ وَجَعَلَ بُطُونَهُمَا مِمَّا يَلِي الْأَرْضَ، حَتَّى رَأَيْتُ بَيَاضَ إِبْطَيْهِ. رَوَاهُمَا أَبُو دَاوُدَ. وَالنَّاسُ قُعُودٌ، مُسْتَقْبِلِينَ الْقِبْلَةَ، يُؤَمِّنُونَ عَلَى دُعَائِهِ، وَيَدْعُو بِأَدْعِيَةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْوَارِدَةِ، وَهِيَ كَثِيرَةٌ وَمِنْهَا مَا نَصَّ عَلَيْهِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: « اللَّهُمَّ اسْقِنَا غَيْثًا مُغِيثًا، هَنِيئًا مَرِيئًا، مُرِيعًا غَدَقًا مُجَلِّلًا سَحًّا طَبَقًا دَائِمًا » وَمَا أَشْبَهَهُ، سِرًّا أَوْ جَهْرًا. وَمِنَ الْوَارِدِ: « اللَّهُمَّ اسْقِنَا الْغَيْثَ وَلَا تَجْعَلْنَا مِنَ الْقَانِطِينَ » « اللَّهُمَّ إِنَّ بِالْعِبَادِ وَالْبِلَادِ وَالْخَلْقِ مِنَ اللَّأْوَاءِ » « اللَّهُمَّ أَنْبِتْ لَنَا الزَّرْعَ، وَأَدِرَّ لَنَا الضَّرْعَ وَاسْقِنَا مِنْ بَرَكَاتِ السَّمَاءِ » « اللَّهُمَّ ارْفَعْ عَنَّا الْجَهْدَ وَالْجُوعَ وَالْعُرْيَ، وَاكْشِفْ عَنَّا مِنَ الْبَلَاءِ مَا لَا يَكْشِفُهُ غَيْرُكَ » « اللَّهُمَّ إِنَّا نَسْتَغْفِرُكَ إِنَّكَ كُنْتَ غَفَّارًا »
And the great elders and children. And in Mecca and Bayt al-Maqdis, in the Sacred Mosque and the Aqsa Mosque, they gather. And that is also befitting for the people of the city of our master the Prophet ﷺ. And the Imam stands facing the qibla, raising his hands. According to the hadith cited, how did the Prophet ﷺ raise his hands during istisqa?
A) With palms up

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Supplications for Rain and the Ruling on Attributing Rain to Stars
Ruling on recommended du'as and aqidah regarding rain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended supplications for rain and identify the aqidah ruling regarding attributing rain to stars with the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Attributing rain to stars with belief in their effect is kufr; only Allah sends rain.

This lesson covers the sunnah du'as for seeking rain and the proper response when rain falls. It also clarifies a critical aqidah point from a hadith qudsi: the distinction between a believer who attributes rain to Allah's mercy and a disbeliever who attributes it to a star.

Guided Path
1
Learn the recommended du'as for istisqa' and after rain
Familiarize yourself with the phrases taught by the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Allahumma isqina ghaythan mughithan...' and when it rains: 'Allahumma sayyiban nafi'an.' Note the variants from different hadith collections.
The du'as are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Understand the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid
Study the complete hadith: the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم reported that Allah said some become believers by attributing rain to His bounty, while others become disbelievers by attributing it to a star.
The hadith is sahih, narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Distinguish between permissible and impermissible statements about stars
Note the key nuance: saying 'mutilna bi-naw'i katha' is only kufr if one believes the star independently causes rain. Merely stating the time or context without such belief is not kufr.
The commentary clarifies: 'if he believes that the stars have an effect in bringing about (rain) independently or as a partner'.
4
Identify the ruling level for du'as and the aqidah ruling
The du'as are sunnah (mustahabb). The aqidah ruling: attributing rain to a star with belief in its causal effect is kufr. The evidence is the explicit hadith.
There is consensus among the schools on this aqidah point.

Source Text

(۲) هَفْوَاتِ عِبَادِكَ فَأَرْسِلِ السَّمَاءَ» أي السَّحَابَ أو المَطَرَ (عَلَيْنَا مِدْرَاراً ) أي : كثيراً وثبت عن النبي ( اسْقِنَا غَيْنَاً مُغِيْنَاً نَافِعَاً غَيْرَ ضَارٌ عَاجِلا غَيْرَ آجِل ) () ( اللَّهُمُ اسْقِ عَبَادَكَ وَبَهَائِمَكَ وانشر رَحْمَتَكَ ، وأَحْيِ بَلَدَكَ المَيْتَ ، « اللهم أنت الله لا إلَهَ إِلا أَنْتَ الغَنِيُّ وَنَحْنُ الفُقَرَاءُ، أَنْزِلْ عَلَيْنَا الغَيْثَ، وَاجْعَلْ مَا أَنْزَلْتَ لَنَا قُوَّةً وَبَلاغاً إلى حسين ، فإذا أمطروا قالوا استحباباً: « اللهم صيِّباً «اللَّهُمَّ نافعاً» ()، كذا في رواية البخاري بتشديد الياء، والصاد المهلمة، أي: مطراً، وقيل: مطراً كثيراً، وفي رواية لابن ماجه ( سيباً ) () بفتح السين المهلمة وإسكان الياء: أي عطاء، وفي رواية لأبي داود وابن ماجه: «صيباً هنيئاً ) ()، فيجمع بين الروايات في الدعاء بها، ويقولون: مطرنا بفضل الله وبرحمته لا ينوء كذا، لما روى الشيخان عن زيد بن خالد الجهني قال صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصبــح عـلـى إثـر سحاب كانت من الليل، فلما انصرف أقبل على الناس، فقال: « أَتَدْرُونَ مَاذَا قَالَ رَبُّكُمْ؟» قالوا: الله ورسوله اعلم قال: «قَدْ أصْبَحَ مِنْ عِبَادِي مُؤْمِنْ بِي وَكَافِرْ، فَأَمَّا مَنْ قَالَ: مُطِرْنَا بِفَضْلِ اللَّهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ فَذَلِكَ مُؤْمِنْ بِي وَكَافِرٌ بِالكَوَاكِبِ، وَمَنْ قَالَ مُطِرْنَا بَنوءٍ كَذَا، فَذَلِكَ كَافِرٌ بِي مُؤْمِنُ بِالْكَوَاكِبِ ، انتهى. أي: إذا اعتقد أن للكواكب تأثيراً في الإيجاد استقلالاً أو شركة، لا . ركة، لا من قال: مطرنا في نوء كذا،
(He said: 'the faults of Your servants, so send the sky' meaning clouds or rain 'upon us abundantly' meaning much. And it is confirmed from the Prophet: 'Give us a heavy, beneficial, not harmful rain, quickly not delayed. O Allah, give water to Your servants and Your cattle, spread Your mercy, and revive Your dead land. O Allah, You are Allah, there is no god but You, the Rich, and we are the poor; send down rain upon us, and make what You send strength and provision until a good outcome.' When it rains they say, as recommended: 'O Allah, make it a downpour, O Allah, beneficial.' Thus in the narration of Bukhari with shaddah on the ya and with sad muhmalah, meaning rain; it is said abundant rain. In a narration of Ibn Majah: 'sayban' with fat-ha on the sin and sukun on the ya: meaning gift. In a narration of Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah: 'sayban hani'an' so one combines the narrations in supplication with them. And they say: 'We have been given rain by the bounty of Allah and His mercy, not by such-and-such star.' Because the two shaykhs narrated from Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani: he said, 'The Messenger of Allah led us in the dawn prayer after a night of clouds. When he finished, he turned to the people and said: Do you know what your Lord has said? They said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: This morning some of My servants have become believers in Me and disbelievers. As for the one who said: We have been given rain by the bounty of Allah and His mercy, that one is a believer in Me and a disbeliever in the stars. And as for the one who said: We have been given rain by such-and-such star, that one is a disbeliever in Me and a believer in the stars.' End. That is: if he believes that the stars have an effect in bringing about (rain) independently or as a partner, not... not one who said: we have been given rain during such-and-such star.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the recommended supplications (du'as) for seeking rain (istisqa') and what to say when it rains. It first presents phrases taught by the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم for asking rain, then mentions the sunnah of saying 'Allahumma sayyiban nafi'an' and its variants when rain falls. The core ruling is that when it rains, one should attribute it solely to Allah's bounty and mercy, saying 'Mutilna bi-fadlillahi wa-rahmatihi' not to any star or constellation. The hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani is the proof: whoever attributes rain to a star with belief in its independent effect commits disbelief (kufr). The commentary clarifies that this applies only if one believes the star has an effect independently or as a partner with Allah; simply saying 'we received rain during such-and-such star' without such belief is not kufr. The passage thus establishes the Islamic creed of tawhid in daily life events.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqā'): Prayer for rain; a sunnah performed during drought.
نوء (naw'): A star or constellation that was believed to cause rain; attributing rain to it with belief in its independent effect is kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid, what distinguishes a believer from a disbeliever regarding rain?
A) Believers say 'Mutilna bi-fadlillahi wa-rahmatihi', disbelievers say 'Mutilna bi-naw'i katha' with belief in star's independent effect
B) Believers pray for rain, disbelievers do not
C) Believers seek rain in mosques, disbelievers seek it in open fields
D) There is no distinction mentioned

Key Takeaway
The sunnah when it rains is to say 'Mutilna bi-fadlillahi wa-rahmatihi' and avoid attributing rain to any created cause with belief in its independent power.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Supplication When Rain is Excessive (Allahumma Hawalayna)
Ruling on the recommended du'a when rain causes harm, with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended supplication when rain is excessive and harmful, and explain the wisdom and etiquettes of supplication as demonstrated by the Prophet's du'a.

Core Idea
When rain causes harm, the sunna is to pray for its diversion to beneficial places, not for its complete removal.

This lesson presents the recommended du'a to recite when rainfall becomes excessive and causes harm. The Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) taught his companions to say 'Allahumma hawalayna wa la 'alayna'—asking Allah to divert the rain to the hills and valleys, not upon buildings and people. The hadith from Anas ibn Malik in al-Sahihayn serves as the proof, and the commentary reveals the deeper adab (etiquette) in supplication: preserving the blessing while removing its harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is its legal classification (hukm)? The act is reciting a specific du'a when rain is excessive; the ruling is sunnah (recommended).
The text from Imdad al-Fattah states: 'If the rain increases until harm is feared, they say: Allahumma hawalayna...' — this indicates a recommended action.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof supports this ruling? The hadith from al-Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) narrated by Anas ibn Malik about the man who first requested rain, then after a week of continuous rain requested it to stop.
The Prophet (ﷺ) did not pray for the rain to stop entirely but to be diverted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit wording of the du'a shows that when rain is harmful, one should ask Allah to place it around them (hawalayna) and not on them, and specifically on hills, small mountains, valleys, and tree groves.
This indicates the recommended action and the wording to use.
4
Understand the wisdom and adab
Why this du'a and not a request for complete cessation? The commentary explains that rain is needed for agriculture, so the Prophet asked to prevent its harm while preserving its benefit. This teaches us to not complain about blessings, but to ask Allah to remove their harmful aspects.
This adab is consistent with tawakkul and tafwid (trust in Allah).
5
Apply the lesson
In practice, when one sees excessive rain causing damage, they should recite this du'a. This is a sunnah act, not obligatory, but following it brings barakah.
The du'a can be recited in any language, but the Arabic wording is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن زاد المطر حتى خيف الضرر قالوا: «اللَّهُمَّ حَوالَيْنَا الحديث، لما في الصحيحين، أن رجــلاً دخل المسجد ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قائماً يخطب، فقال: يا رسول الله هَلَكَتِ الأَمْوَالُ، وَانْقَطَعَتِ السُّبُلِ فَادْعُ الله يُغيْتَنَا، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «اللَّهُمَّ أغِتْنَا، اللهم أغِثْنَا اللَّهُمَّ أَعْتُنَا» قال أنس : فـلا والله ما ندري بالسماء من سحاب ولا قزعة، وما بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَ سَلْعِ مِنْ [ بَيْتِ ] وَلَا دَارٍ، قَالَ: فَطَلَعَتْ مِنْ وَرَائِهِ سَحَابَةٌ مِثْلَ التَّرْسِ ، فَلَمَّا تَوَسَطَتِ السَّمَاءَ انْتَشَرَتْ ثُمَّ أمْطَرَتْ، فَلا وَاللَّهِ مَا رَأَيْنَا الشَّمْسَ سَبَتَا، قال : ثُمَّ دَخَلَ رَجُلٌ مِنْ ذَلِكَ البَابِ فِي الجُمُعَةِ المُقْبِلَةِ، وَرَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَائِمٌ يَخْطُبُ فَاسْتَقْبَلَهُ قَائِمَاً، فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ الله هَلَكَتِ الأَمْوَالُ وانْقَطَعَتِ السُّبُلْ فَادْعُ الله يُمْسِكَهَا عَنَّا، قال: فَرَفَعَ رَسولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يديهِ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «اللَّهُمَّ حَوَالَيْنَا وَلَا عَلَيْنَا اللَّهُمَّ عَلى الآكَامِ والزِّرَابِ، وَبُطُونِ الْأَوْدِيَةِ، وَمَنَابِتِ الشَّجَر » قال: فأقْلَعَتْ، وخرجنا نمشي في الشمس، حوالينا بفتح اللام-: أي: اجعله في الأودية والمراعي التي لا [ يضرها المطر على ] الأبنية والطرق، والآكـام بـالـمـد جمـع: أُكـم، بضمتين جمع: إكام ككتاب جمع أكم بفتحتين : جمع أكمة، وهي: دون الجبــل وفــوق الرابية، والظــراب: بالظاء المشالة ووهم من قال: بالضاد الساقط جمع ظرب بفتح فسكون الجبل الصغير، وفيـه إرشاد لتعليمنا الأدب في هذا الدعاء، حيث لم يدع برفعه مطلقاً، لأنه يحتاج إليه مستمراً بالنسبة لبعض الأودية والمزارع إلى حصول الكفاية التي يعلمها الله ، فطلب منع ضرره وبقــاء نـفـعـه، وفيـه إعلام بأنه إذا قارن النعمة عارض لا يتسخط منه، فيسأل الله تعالى رفع العارض وبقاء النعمة، والدعاء برفع الضار لا ينافي التوكل والتفويض
If the rain increases until harm is feared, they say: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us' as per the hadith in the two Sahihs, that a man entered the mosque while the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم was standing delivering the sermon, and said: O Messenger of Allah, wealth has perished and roads have been cut off, so pray to Allah to give us rain. He said: 'O Allah, give us rain, O Allah, give us rain, O Allah, give us rain.' Anas said: By Allah, we did not see in the sky any cloud or patch, and between us and Sal' there was no house or dwelling. He said: Then a cloud like a shield appeared from behind him, and when it reached the middle of the sky it spread and then it rained. By Allah, we did not see the sun for a week. Then a man entered from that door on the following Friday while the Messenger of Allah was standing delivering the sermon. He faced him standing and said: O Messenger of Allah, wealth has perished and roads have been cut off, so pray to Allah to withhold it from us. He said: The Messenger of Allah raised his hands and said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us; O Allah, on the hills, the small mountains, the valleys, and the tree groves.' He said: It cleared, and we went out walking in the sun. 'Hawalayna' with fat-ha on the lam: meaning make it in the valleys and pastures which the rain does not harm, not on buildings and roads. And 'al-akam' with madd is the plural of 'ukam' with two dammas, the plural of 'ikam' like kitab, the plural of 'akam' with two fathas: the plural of 'akamah', which is lower than a mountain and higher than a hill. And 'al-zirab' with za' mushalah (and mistaken is he who says with dad) is the plural of 'zirb' with fath then sukun, a small mountain. In it is guidance teaching us etiquette in this supplication, because he did not pray for its removal absolutely, since it is continuously needed for some valleys and farms to obtain sufficiency which Allah knows. So he asked to prevent its harm and preserve its benefit. And in it is an indication that when a blessing is accompanied by an adverse element, one should not complain, but ask Allah to remove the adverse and preserve the blessing. And supplication to remove what is harmful does not contradict trust and reliance (tawakkul and tafwid).
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the recommended du'a when rain becomes excessive and causes harm. The text says: 'If the rain increases until harm is feared, they say: Allahumma hawalayna wa la 'alayna' (O Allah, around us and not upon us).' The proof is the hadith of Anas in al-Sahihayn about the man who first asked for rain and then, after a week of rain, asked for it to stop. The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم prayed for the rain to be diverted to hills and valleys, not to harm buildings and roads. The commentary explains the linguistic meaning of 'hawalayna' and the wisdom in the prayer: not asking for complete removal of rain, but only to prevent its harm, because rain is needed for agriculture. This teaches us adab (etiquette) in supplication: when a blessing comes with an unwanted side effect, we ask for removal of the side effect while preserving the blessing. This is consistent with tawakkul and tafwid (reliance and entrustment to Allah).

Key Terms
حوالينا (ḥawālaynā): Around us (i.e., divert rain to the surroundings, not on us).
آكام (ākām): Hills; plural of أُكْم or أَكَمَة, referring to elevated ground lower than a mountain.
ظراب (ẓirāb): Small mountains; plural of ظَرِب with ظاء مشالة.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) اللهم اسقنا غيثاً مغيثاً
B) اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا
C) اللهم صيباً نافعاً
D) مطرنا بفضل الله وبرحمته

Key Takeaway
The sunna when rain is harmful is to recite 'Allahumma hawalayna wa la 'alayna' asking for diversion to beneficial places, balancing gratitude and trust in Allah.

Ruling on Turning the Cloak in Istisqa' - Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the imam turns his cloak during rain prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions within the Hanafi school regarding turning the cloak during istisqa' and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Turning the cloak in istisqa' is not wajib; it is a recommended practice based on prophetic example, though Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf did not consider it part of the prayer.

The Istisqa' prayer (prayer for rain) includes several recommended acts, one of which is turning the cloak. However, within the Hanafi school there is an internal difference of opinion on whether this act is prescribed. This lesson examines the views of the three major Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—and the evidence each brings. Understanding this dispute clarifies the nature of the practice and helps a mufti determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions on turning the cloak
Identify the ruling according to each of the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Note the hukm level (not part of prayer vs. mustahabb).
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say there is no turning of the cloak; Muhammad says it is recommended.
2
Examine the proof for each position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that istisqa' is a supplication and thus no specific physical act is prescribed. Muhammad relies on the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) turning his cloak during the prayer.
The hadith evidence is strong and includes multiple narrations.
3
Understand the interpretation of the hadith
Abu Hanifa interprets the turning of the cloak as an act of optimism (tafā'ul), not as a ritual act of worship. Muhammad and later scholars see it as a sunnah act based on the Prophet's explicit actions.
The dispute is essentially over the nature of the action: is it part of the prayer or just a good omen?
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The later authorities, including the author of Imdad al-Fattah, support the practice as recommended, and it is commonly observed.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the hadith evidence and the practice of the community.
5
Note the related dispute on the sermon
Abu Hanifa holds no sermon; Abu Yusuf says one sermon; Muhammad says two sermons. This is a separate (though connected) intra-Hanafi disagreement.
This shows the broader ikhtilaf on the structure of istisqa'.

على المنبر فكبر وحمد الله عز وجل ثم قال: «إنكم شكوتم جدب دياركم، واستنخار المطر عن زمانه عنكم، وقد أمركم الله عز وجل أن تدعوه، ووعدكم أن يستجيب لكم، ثم قال: الحمد لله رب العالمين الرحمن الرحيم ملك يوم الدين لا إله إلا الله يفعل ما يريد اللهم أنت الله الذي لا إله إلا أنت الغني ونحن الفقراء، أنزل علينا الغيث، واجعل ما أنزلت قوة وبلاغا إلى حين ثم رفع يديه، فلم يزل في الرفع حتى بدا بياض إبطيه، ثم حول إلى الناس ظهره، وقلب أو حول رداءه وهو رافع يديه ثم أقبل على الناس ونزل من المنبر، وصلى ركعتين فأنشأ الله سبحانه وتعالى سحابة فرعدت وبرقت، ثم أمطرت بإذن الله عز وجل، فلم يأت عليه الصلاة والسلام مسجده حتى سالت السيول، فلما رأى سرعتهم إلى السكن ضحك حتى بدت نواجذه، فقال: أشهد أن الله على كل شيء قدير، وأني عبد الله ورسوله، انتهى.
And there is no turning of the cloak in it. And behind him was a cloud like a shield, and when it had reached the middle of the sky it spread and then rained. So by Allah, we did not see the sun for a week. He said: Then a man entered from that door the following Friday while the Messenger of Allah was standing delivering the sermon. He faced him while standing and said: O Messenger of Allah, wealth has been destroyed and roads have been cut off, so supplicate Allah to withhold it from us. He said: So the Messenger of Allah raised his hands and then said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us. O Allah, upon the hills and the small mountains, and the valleys, and the places where trees grow.' He said: And it cleared, and we went out walking in the sun. 'Hawalayna' with fatha on the lam: meaning place it in the valleys and pastures that do not harm the buildings and roads. Al-akam (with madd) is plural of ukum (with two dammas) plural of ikam like kitab plural of akam (with two fathas) plural of akamah, which is below a mountain and above a hill. Al-zirab (with the emphasized za) and it is a mistake of whoever said with the dropped dad, plural of zarb (with a fatha and sukun) which is a small mountain. In it is guidance to teach us etiquette in this supplication, for he did not supplicate for its complete removal, because it is needed continuously for some valleys and farms until the sufficiency that Allah knows. So he asked for the prevention of its harm and the continuation of its benefit. And in it is an indication that when a blessing is accompanied by a harmful condition, one should not be displeased with it, but ask Allah to remove the harmful condition and preserve the blessing. And supplication for the removal of harm does not contradict reliance and delegation. (And there is not in it) i.e. the rain prayer (turning of the cloak) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, and according to a narration from him, because it is a supplication, so it is considered like other supplications. And what was narrated by Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, is interpreted as optimism. Al-Kamal, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And it came explicitly in al-Mustadrak from the hadith of Jabir, and he authenticated it, he said: 'And he turned his cloak so that the drought would turn away.' And in al-Tabarani from the hadith of Anas: 'And he turned his cloak' so that the drought would turn to fertility. And in Musnad Ishaq: 'So that the year would turn from drought to fertility.' And he does not give a sermon according to Abu Hanifa because it is a follower of the congregational prayer, and there is no congregation for him in it. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he gives a sermon, but according to Abu Yusuf one sermon, and according to Muhammad two sermons, and this is a narration from Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: The imam turns his cloak without the people. And from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations. Thus in al-Tabyin. And in al-Burhan: Muhammad ordered the imam to turn his cloak after the beginning of his sermon. And in al-Fath: He said in Sunan Abi Dawud from Aisha who said: The people complained to the Messenger of Allah about the lack of rain, so the Messenger of Allah ordered a pulpit, and it was placed for him in the prayer area, and he promised the people a day they would go out. He said: The Messenger of Allah went out when the sun had risen, and he sat on the pulpit, said the takbir and praised Allah, then said: 'You have complained of the drought of your lands and the delay of rain at its time from you. And Allah has commanded you to supplicate to Him, and He has promised to answer you.' Then he said: 'Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, the Most Merciful, the Most Gracious, King of the Day of Judgment. There is no god but Allah who does what He wills. O Allah, You are Allah, there is no god but You. You are the Rich and we are the poor. Send down rain upon us, and make what You send down a strength and a provision until a time.' Then he raised his hands, and continued raising until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. Then he turned his back to the people, and turned or moved his cloak while still raising his hands. Then he faced the people, descended from the pulpit, and prayed two rak'ahs. Then Allah sent a cloud that thundered and flashed, then it rained by Allah's permission. He had not reached his mosque until the valleys flowed. When he saw their haste to shelter, he smiled until his molars appeared, and he said: 'I testify that Allah is over all things capable, and that I am the servant of Allah and His Messenger.' End.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on turning the cloak (قلب رداء) during the istisqa' (prayer for rain). The author begins by stating the matn that there is no turning of the cloak in the rain prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Then the commentary expands with a detailed hadith about the Prophet's supplication during a drought, including the turning of the cloak. The text presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that turning the cloak is not part of the sunnah, while Muhammad narrates that the Prophet turned his cloak, which is interpreted as a good omen (تفاؤل) for the changing of drought to fertility. The commentary also discusses the khutbah (sermon): Abu Hanifa says no sermon because there is no congregation, while Abu Yusuf says one sermon and Muhammad says two. The overall lesson is that the practice of turning the cloak is not obligatory but is recommended based on prophetic practice, with internal Hanafi differences.

Key Terms
قلب رداء (qalb ridā'): Turning the cloak or garment, specifically the action of turning the outer garment inside out or reversing it, performed during the rain prayer as a symbolic act.
استسقاء (istisqā'): The prayer for rain, a special congregational prayer performed during drought.
تفاؤل (tafā'ul): Optimism or taking a good omen; in this context, interpreting the physical action of turning the cloak as an optimistic gesture for the changing of conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on turning the cloak (قلب رداء) during the istisqa' prayer?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is mustahabb.
C) It is not part of the prayer.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Turning the cloak in istisqa' is a recommended sunnah based on the Prophet's practice, though early Hanafi masters differed on its inclusion.
